Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh: Idafi and Laqami
Author presents separate and combined definitions of usul al-fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state both the idafi and laqami definitions of usul al-fiqh and explain the significance of each component.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is defined either by separating its components (asl + fiqh) or as a single science of rules for deriving fiqh with certainty.

The author introduces two approaches to defining Usul al-Fiqh: the idafi (separate) definition, which defines 'asl' and 'fiqh' individually, and the laqami (combined) definition, which treats the term as a single discipline. In this lesson, we will unpack each component, exploring the multiple technical meanings of 'asl' and the various definitions of 'fiqh', culminating in the complete laqami definition that forms the foundation of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish idafi from laqami
Note that idafi definition defines each term separately (mudaf and mudaf ilayh), while laqami defines them together as a single field of study.
This mirrors the distinction between defining a compound term by its parts or as a whole.
2
Define mudaf: the five meanings of 'asl'
List the five technical usages of 'asl': basis, prevalent rule, comprehensive rule, proof, and istishab (presumption of continuity). Provide examples from the text for each.
The word 'asl' is polysemous in Hanafi usul; context determines its meaning.
3
Define mudaf ilayh: linguistic and technical meanings of 'fiqh'
First, state the linguistic meaning (splitting/opening). Then present the four technical definitions: Abu Hanifa's broad definition, the later Hanafi restricted definition, al-Shafi'i's definition, and Hasan al-Basri's ascetic definition.
The Hanafi school recognizes a broader scope for fiqh than the Shafi'i school.
4
State the laqami definition of usul al-fiqh
The combined definition: 'It is the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh with certainty.' Identify the three key elements: knowledge, rules (qawa'id), and arriving at fiqh with certainty.
The emphasis on 'with certainty' (tahqiq) is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the definition to a sample derivation
Take the Quranic command 'And give zakah' (وَآتُوا الزَّكَاةَ). Identify 'asl' as proof (the verse), 'fiqh' as the ruling of obligation, and the usul rule that 'command indicates obligation' to derive the ruling.
This illustrates how the laqami definition functions in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعریف اصول الفقه تعریف کو حد بھی کہا جاتا ہے۔ حد کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) حد اضافی (۲) حد لقمی جس کو حد حقیقی بھی کہا جاتا ہے۔ حد اضافی: یہ ہے کہ مضاف مضاف الیہ کی علیحدہ علیحدہ تعریف کی جائے۔ حد لقمی : یہ ہے کہ دونوں کی اجتماعا تعریف کی جائے بامیں حیثیت کہ ایک فن کا نام بن چکے ہیں۔ اولا اصول فقہ کی حد اضافی ثانیا حدیقمی بیان کی جائے گی ۔ حداضافی کا بیان (تعریف مضاف ( الاصول جمع ہے اصل کی لفظ اصل متعدد معانی میں مستعمل ہوتا ہے (۱) ما یبنی علیہ غیرہ مثال ابتناء السقف على الجدار (۲) رائج جیسے الاصل في الاستعمال الحقيقة (۳) قاعد و کلیه مثال کل فاعل مرفوع اصل من النحو (۴) دلیل مثال قوله تعالی واتو الزکوۃ اصل وجوب الزكوة (۵) استصحاب حال مثال الاصل في الماء لمهارة - تعریف مضاف الیہ: الفقه (۱) لغوی معنی الشق والفتح والفقيه هو الذي يشق الاحکام و تفتح ما استغلق منها بكذاذكر الزمخشري في کتاب الفائق (۲) وقال صاحب در مختار الفقه العلم بشی (۳) وقال صاحب البحر الرائق الفقه الفهم من باب سمع و از باب کرم معناہ فقیہ ہونا و از باب تفعیل فقیہ بنانا از مفاعلہ علم فقہ کا تکرار کرنا ۔ فقہ کا اصطلاحی معنی : (۱) معرفتہ النفس مالها وما عليها وهذا التعريف منقول عن الامام ابی حنیفہ۔ یہ تعریف عام ہے علم العقائد علم الفقہ علم الوجدانیات ( اخلاق ) سب کو شامل ہے (۲) عند بعض المتاخرین معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها من العمل (۳) تیسری تعریف منقول عن الشافعی ہے ھو العلم بالا حكام الشرعية الفرعية العملية من ادلتها التفصیلیۃ ۔ شرعی کی قید سے احکام غیر شرعی خارج ہو گئے الفرعیہ کی قید سے احکام اصلی خارج ہو گئے ادلہ سے قرآن وسنت، اجماع، قیاس مراد ہیں۔ (والتفصیل یاتی بعد انشاءاللہ (۴) امام حسن بصری فقہ کی تعریف کرتے ہیں الاعراض عن الدنيا و التوجہ الی العقی۔ حد لقمی کا بیان : ھو علم بقواعد التي يتوصل بھا الی الفقه على وجه التحقیق ۔
Definition of Usul al-Fiqh. Definition is also called 'had'. There are two types of had: (1) idafi definition, (2) laqami definition, which is also called haqiqi definition. Idafi definition: that the mudaf and mudaf ilayh are defined separately. Laqami definition: that both are defined together, with the consideration that they have become the name of an art. First the idafi definition of usul fiqh will be mentioned, then the laqami definition. Explanation of idafi definition: (Definition of mudaf: al-usul is the plural of asl. The word asl is used in multiple meanings: (1) that on which something else is built, e.g., the building of the roof on the wall, (2) the prevalent, e.g., the principle in usage is the literal meaning, (3) a comprehensive rule, e.g., every agent is nominative is a grammatical principle, (4) proof, e.g., Allah's saying 'and give zakah' is the proof for the obligation of zakah, (5) istishab of the current state, e.g., the principle regarding water is purity.) Definition of mudaf ilayh: al-fiqh. (1) Linguistic meaning: splitting and opening, and a faqih is one who splits rulings and opens what is difficult of them, as mentioned by Zamakhshari in al-Fa'iq. (2) The author of Durr Mukhtar said: al-fiqh is knowledge of something. (3) The author of Bahr al-Ra'iq said: al-fiqh is understanding, from the pattern of sami'a, and from the pattern of karuma meaning he became a faqih, and from the pattern of taf'il to make someone a faqih, and from mufa'ala to repeat the science of fiqh.) Terminological meaning of fiqh: (1) Knowledge of the self of what is for it and what is against it. This definition is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. This definition is general, including the science of beliefs, the science of fiqh, the science of inner consciousness (ethics). (2) According to some later scholars: knowledge of the self of what is for it and what is against it from actions. (3) The third definition is transmitted from al-Shafi'i: It is the knowledge of the subsidiary practical Shar'i rulings from their detailed evidences. The restriction 'Shari'i' excludes non-Shar'i rulings; 'subsidiary' excludes fundamental rulings; 'evidences' refers to Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. (Details will come later, insha'Allah.) (4) Imam Hasan al-Basri defines fiqh as: turning away from the world and directing towards the Hereafter. Explanation of the laqami definition: It is the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh with certainty.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a detailed definitional analysis of the term 'Usul al-Fiqh'. The author follows the standard Hanafi method of dividing definitions into two types: idafi (separate) and laqami (combined). In the idafi definition, he first defines the mudaf (أصول) as the plural of أصل, listing five distinct usages of the word 'asl' in Islamic sciences: (1) basis or foundation (e.g., roof on wall), (2) the predominant or default rule (e.g., literal meaning is the default), (3) a comprehensive rule (e.g., grammatical rule), (4) proof or evidence (e.g., a Qur'anic verse as proof for a ruling), (5) istishab (presumption of continuity, e.g., water is presumed pure). Then he defines the mudaf ilayh (فقه) linguistically and technically. Linguistically, fiqh means splitting and opening, indicating the faqih's role in extracting and clarifying rulings. Technically, he gives multiple definitions: from Imam Abu Hanifa, a broad definition encompassing beliefs, practical fiqh, and spirituality; from later Hanafis, a narrower action-based definition; from Imam al-Shafi'i, the classic definition of 'knowledge of practical subsidiary Shar'i rulings from their detailed evidences'; and from Hasan al-Basri, an ascetic definition. Finally, he gives the laqami (combined) definition of usul al-fiqh as a single science: 'knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh with certainty.' This is the standard Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh, focusing on the methodological principles (qawa'id) that lead to deriving fiqh rulings. Note that the Hanafi definition emphasizes 'with certainty' (تحقیق), reflecting their concern for epistemic certainty in the derivation process.

Key Terms
اصول (uṣūl): Plural of أصل; in this context, it is part of the compound 'usul al-fiqh' meaning the principles/methodology of fiqh.
حد اضافی (ḥadd iḍāfī): A definition made by defining the two components of a compound term separately.
حد لقمی (ḥadd laqamī): A definition that treats the compound term as a single unit, giving a holistic definition.
فقه (fiqh): Linguistically: splitting/opening. Technically: in the Hanafi laqami definition, fiqh is the discipline whose rulings are derived through usul rules.
قواعد (qawāʿid): Rules; the plural of qa'idah, referring to the methodological principles of usul al-fiqh.
تحقیق (taḥqīq): Certainty; the laqami definition states that usul al-fiqh leads to fiqh 'with certainty' (علی وجه التحقیق).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the laqami definition, what is usul al-fiqh?
A) Knowledge of the rulings of fiqh.
B) Knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh with certainty.
C) The study of evidences like Qur'an and Sunnah.
D) The history of Islamic jurisprudence.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of methodological rules that enable the mujtahid to derive fiqh rulings from detailed evidences with certainty.

Four Definitions of Fiqh: Hanafi and Beyond
Lists and explains four definitions of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four definitions of fiqh and distinguish the Hanafi definition from the Shafi'i definition.

Core Idea
Fiqh in the Hanafi school includes belief and ethics, not only practical rulings.

The term 'fiqh' has undergone semantic development. In the Hanafi school, it originally encompassed all knowledge beneficial for the Hereafter—creed, ethics, and practical law. Later definitions, especially that of al-Shafi'i, narrowed it to subsidiary practical rulings. This lesson unpacks four key definitions, highlighting the Hanafi position and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first definition (Abu Hanifa)
Locate the definition attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa: 'knowledge of the self, what is for it and against it.' Note its breadth—it includes beliefs and ethics.
This is the foundational Hanafi definition.
2
Understand the second definition (later Hanafis)
See how later scholars restricted the first definition by adding 'in terms of action'—focusing on practical deeds while still including some inner states.
Shows evolution within the school.
3
Analyze the third definition (al-Shafi'i)
Examine the Shafi'i definition: 'knowledge of the subsidiary practical Shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences.' Note the exclusions: non-Shar'i, non-subsidiary, and rulings without detailed evidence.
This became the standard usul al-fiqh definition.
4
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i definitions
Contrast the broad Hanafi definition (includes belief and ethics) with the narrow Shafi'i definition (only practical rulings). Understand the thamarah: the scope of fiqh as a discipline differs between the two schools.
This ikhtilaf affects how each school categorizes topics.
5
Note the remaining definitions
Identify the fourth definition from Hasan al-Basri (ascetic orientation) and the final phrase about 'rules leading to fiqh'—likely referring to usul al-fiqh.
These are peripheral but show the term's flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقہ کا اصطلاحی معنی : (۱) معرفتہ النفس مالها وما عليها وهذا التعريف منقول عن الامام ابی حنیفہ۔ یہ تعریف عام ہے علم العقائد علم الفقہ علم الوجدانیات ( اخلاق ) سب کو شامل ہے (۲) عند بعض المتاخرین معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها من العمل (۳) تیسری تعریف منقول عن الشافعی ہے ھو العلم بالا حكام الشرعية الفرعية العملية من ادلتها التفصیلیۃ ۔ شرعی کی قید سے احکام غیر شرعی خارج ہو گئے الفرعیہ کی قید سے احکام اصلی خارج ہو گئے ادلہ سے قرآن وسنت، اجماع، قیاس مراد ہیں۔ (والتفصیل یاتی بعد انشاءاللہ (۴) امام حسن بصری فقہ کی تعریف کرتے ہیں الاعراض عن الدنيا و التوجہ الی العقی۔ حد لقمی کا بیان : ھو علم بقواعد التي يتوصل بھا الی الفقه على وجه التحقیق ۔
The terminological meaning of fiqh: (1) Knowledge of the self, what is for it and against it. This definition is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. This definition is general, including creedal knowledge, fiqh knowledge, and experiential knowledge (ethics). (2) According to some later scholars: Knowledge of the self, what is for it and against it in terms of action. (3) The third definition is transmitted from al-Shafi'i: It is knowledge of the subsidiary practical Shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences. The restriction 'Shar'i' excludes non-Shar'i rulings; 'subsidiary' excludes fundamental rulings; 'evidences' refers to Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. Details will follow, insha'Allah. (4) Imam Hasan al-Basri defines fiqh as: Turning away from the world and directing towards the Hereafter. The saying of [someone]: It is knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh in a verified manner.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage presents four definitions of fiqh, starting with the Hanafi position. The first definition, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is broad and includes belief and ethics. The second narrows it to actions. The third, from al-Shafi'i, is the standard definition in usul al-fiqh, emphasizing Shar'i rulings from detailed evidences. The fourth is ascetic. The final phrase likely refers to the rules of usul al-fiqh. Note: Hanafis distinguish between fiqh as understood here and the subject matter of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of the self or Shar'i rulings depending on the definition.
معرفة النفس (ma'rifat al-nafs): Knowledge of what benefits or harms the self in the Hereafter.
الفرعية (al-far'iyyah): Subsidiary or branch; as opposed to fundamental (usul).
العملية (al-'amaliyyah): Practical; referring to actions of the limbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which qualifier in the Shafi'i definition excludes matters of creed (such as belief in God)?
A) Shar'i
B) Far'iyyah (subsidiary)
C) 'Amaliyyah (practical)
D) Min adillatiha al-tafṣiliyyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh is broader than the Shafi'i definition, including belief and ethics, which impacts the scope of the discipline.

Subject Matter and Purpose of Usul al-Fiqh
States the subject (four proofs & six rulings) and purpose of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the subject matter (the four proofs and six rulings) and the two purposes of usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh's subject is the four proofs and six rulings; its purpose is both worldly success and understanding fiqh's sources.

This lesson introduces the building blocks of usul al-fiqh: what it studies (the four proofs and six rulings) and why we study it. These definitions are foundational—every ruling in fiqh is derived from these sources and falls into one of these categories. Mastering them gives you the skeleton of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject components
The passage states the subject as 'the four proofs and the six rulings'. Recognise that the subject is twofold: the sources of law (proofs) and the categories of rulings.
These two parts will be studied in detail throughout usul al-fiqh.
2
Enumerate the four proofs
List them: Quran (Book), Sunnah, Ijma (consensus), Qiyas (analogy). Commit these to memory as the primary sources of Islamic law in Hanafi usul.
Hanafis also accept secondary proofs like Istihsan and Urf, but the core four are always cited first.
3
Enumerate the six rulings
List them: Wajib, Mandub, Mubah, Makruh Tahrimi, Makruh Tanzihi, Haram. Note that in this list, 'Wajib' includes both fard (definitive) and wajib (necessary) in the broader sense.
Hanafis distinguish fard (qat'i) from wajib (zanni), but here they are grouped under 'wajib' for convenience.
4
Distinguish the two purposes
The passage gives a general purpose (happiness in both worlds) and a specific purpose (knowledge of the sources of fiqh). Understand that usul al-fiqh serves both spiritual and academic goals.
The specific purpose—knowing how rulings are derived—is the key intellectual aim of the discipline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) موضوع: دلائل اربعه واحکام سته - دلائل اربعہ سے مراد (۱) کتاب (۲) سنت (۳) اجماع (۴) قیاس ۔ احکام ستہ سے مراد ( واجب (۲) مندوب (۳) مباح (۴) مکروہ تحریمی (۵) مکروہ تنزیہی (۶) حرام ۔ (۳) غرض و غایت دو قسم ہے (۲) عمومی (۱) خصوصی اول حصول سعادة الدارین۔ دوم الاطلاع على ما خذ الفقه --
(2) Subject: The four proofs and the six rulings. By the four proofs is meant: (1) Book, (2) Sunnah, (3) Ijma, (4) Qiyas. By the six rulings is meant: (1) Wajib, (2) Mandub, (3) Mubah, (4) Makruh Tahrimi, (5) Makruh Tanzihi, (6) Haram. (3) Purpose and goal: two types: (1) general, (2) specific. The first is attainment of happiness in both abodes. The second is knowledge of the sources of fiqh.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of usul al-fiqh: the four primary proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and the six legal categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, haram). These categories are standard in Hanafi fiqh. The purpose of studying usul is twofold: a general spiritual goal (success in this world and the Hereafter) and a specific academic goal (understanding how fiqh rulings are derived). Note: Hanafis often distinguish between fard and wajib (fard is definitively proven), but here the list uses wajib inclusively.

Key Terms
دلائل اربعہ (adillah arba'ah): The four proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
احکام ستہ (ahkam sitta): Six legal categories: Wajib, Mandub, Mubah, Makruh Tahrimi, Makruh Tanzihi, Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Five
C) Six
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh studies the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and the six rulings (wajib through haram), aiming for spiritual success and knowledge of fiqh's sources.

Defining Foundational Terms: Ahkama, Usul, and Shari'ah
Lexical parsing of opening terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'ahkama', 'usul', and 'shari'ah' as used in Hanafi usul, distinguish linguistic from terminological meanings, and explain the conceptual overlap of shari'ah, din, and millat.

Core Idea
Usul are firm foundations; Shari'ah is the revealed path — both anchored in the Quran.

The opening doxology of Al-Tawdih praises Allah for establishing the principles (usul) of the Shari'ah through His Book. Before diving into advanced discussions, the commentator provides a lexical parsing of key terms. This lesson unpacks those definitions, giving you the precise Hanafi understanding of 'ahkama', 'usul', and 'shari'ah' — essential building blocks for the entire study of usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Locate the terms being defined
From the Arabic text, identify the three key terms: أحكم, أصول, شريعة. Notice the structure: the doxology uses them, and the commentary then glosses each separately.
The commentary is titled 'حل مفردات' (solution of vocabulary), indicating a lexical analysis.
2
Analyze the definition of 'ahkama'
The author explains that 'ahkama' is from the form IV verb 'أفعل' meaning 'to make firm/well-ordered'. This verb is used to describe how Allah firmly established the principles of Shari'ah through His Book.
Form IV often conveys causation or intensification. Here it emphasizes the firmness of the foundations.
3
Analyze the definition of 'usul'
'Usul' is the plural of 'asl', defined as 'that upon which something else is built'. In Hanafi usul, it refers to the principles from which derived rulings (furu') are extracted. The commentary links this to the Quran as the source.
This definition is broader than just 'Quran and Sunnah'; it includes the principles derived from them.
4
Analyze the definition of 'shari'ah'
Linguistically, 'shari'ah' comes from 'al-shar'' meaning 'al-izhar' (manifestation). Terminologically, it is 'what Allah has legislated as a practice'. The commentary then clarifies that 'shari'ah', 'din', and 'millat' have the same referent (Islam) but differ in consideration — shari'ah highlights the path that servants enter to quench their thirst.
Thus, shari'ah is the revealed law itself, not the human understanding of it (fiqh).
5
Synthesize the relationship
The Quran ('Kitabuhu') is the source that firmly establishes the usul (principles). These usul form the foundation for the furu' (branches) of the Hanafi school. Shari'ah is the overall revealed path that encompasses these principles and branches.
This hierarchy is central to Hanafi methodology: Quran → Usul → Furu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحمد لله الذى احكم بكتابه اصول الشريعة الغراء ورفع بخطابه فروع الحنفية المسمحة البيضاء حتى اضحت كلمته الباقية راسخة الاساس شامخة البناء . كشجرة طيبة اصلها ثابت وفرعها في السماء .
حل مفردات احكم از باب افعال مضبوط کرنا اصول جمع ہے اصل کی ما یعنی علیہ غیرہ - الشريعه من الشرع لغوى معنی الاظهار اصطلاحی معنی ما شرع الله عاده تحقیق شریعه دین ملت شریعہ ودین ملت کا مصداق ایک ہے یعنی دین اسلام ان میں تغایر اعتباری ہے دین اسلام بائیں حیثیت کہ عباد اللہ اس پر وارد ہو کر اپنی علمی پیاس بجھاتے ہیں اس کو شریعت
Praise be to Allah who has firmly established through His Book the principles of the noble Shari'ah, and through His speech raised the luminous and expansive branches of the Hanafi school, until His enduring word became firm in foundation and lofty in structure, like a good tree whose root is firm and whose branches are in the sky. Solution of vocabulary: 'Ahkama' from the form 'af'ala' means to make firm, 'usul' is plural of 'asl', meaning 'that upon which something else is built'. 'Al-shari'ah' from 'al-shar' linguistically means 'al-izhar' (manifestation), terminologically means 'what Allah has legislated as a practice'. Verification: Shari'ah, din, and millat have one referent, i.e., the religion of Islam; they differ only in consideration. The religion of Islam, in the respect that the servants of Allah enter upon it and quench their scholarly thirst, is called Shari'ah.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the sharh (commentary) on Al-Tawdih. It starts with a doxology praising Allah, then provides a lexical analysis (حل مفردات) of key terms from the opening sentence. The word 'أحكم' (from the form IV verb 'أحكم') is explained as meaning 'to make firm or well-ordered'. 'أصول' is identified as the plural of 'أصل' (root/foundation), defined as 'that upon which something else is built' — a standard definition in Hanafi usul. The term 'الشريعة' is examined linguistically (from 'الشرع' meaning 'manifestation') and terminologically ('what Allah has legislated as a practice'). The commentary then clarifies that 'شريعة', 'دين', and 'ملة' all refer to Islam, differing only in perspective: when one enters it to quench scholarly thirst, it is called Shari'ah. This parsing exercise sets the stage for the entire work by defining foundational concepts.

Key Terms
أحكم (ahkama): From باب إفعال; means 'to make firm/well-ordered'.
أصول (usul): Plural of أصل; that upon which something else is built.
شريعة (shari'ah): Linguistically: 'al-izhar' (manifestation). Terminologically: what Allah has legislated as a practice. It is synonymous with 'din' and 'millat' in referent, differing only in consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The foundational terms 'ahkama', 'usul', and 'shari'ah' are precisely defined in Hanafi usul to establish the Quran as the firm source of principles for deriving rulings.

Definition Types and Refutation of al-Razi's Definition of Asl
Critique of al-Razi's definition through definition taxonomy and logical conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions, apply the conditions of muttarid and mun'akis to evaluate definitions, and critique al-Razi's definition of 'asl' using Hanafi usul methodology.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be coextensive: it must apply only to the defined term and to all instances of it.

In usul al-fiqh, precise definitions are essential to avoid ambiguity. This passage critiques Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' (origin) and, in doing so, introduces the distinction between real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions, as well as the twin conditions of exclusivity (tard) and comprehensiveness ('aks). Understanding these tools will sharpen your ability to evaluate any definition in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and proposed definition
The term 'asl' is defined by al-Razi as 'al-muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed). Note the author's claim that this definition is not muttarid.
The Hanafi definition is 'ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh' (that upon which something else is built).
2
Classify the definition type
Determine whether the definition is haqiqi (real) or ismi (nominal). Definitions of technical terms like 'asl' are ismi, as they describe conventional meaning, not essence.
al-Razi's definition is also ismi, but the issue is not the type but the failure in conditions.
3
Define the conditions of tard and 'aks
Tard (exclusivity): whenever the definition applies, the defined term must apply. 'Aks (comprehensiveness): whenever the defined term applies, the definition must apply. Together they ensure coextensiveness.
Example: 'rational animal' is muttarid and mun'akis for man; 'walking animal' is not muttarid (applies to horse).
4
Apply conditions to al-Razi's definition
The definition 'al-muhtaj ilayh' applies to five types of causes and conditions (material, formal, efficient, final, and conditions), but 'asl' technically only refers to the material cause. Thus the definition is not muttarid: it applies to entities not called 'asl'.
This is the core critique: the definition is too broad (ghayr mani' an dukhul ghayr).
5
State the correct definition and justification
The correct Hanafi definition is 'ma yabtani 'alayhi ghayruh' (that upon which something else is built). This is muttarid (only material cause qualifies) and mun'akis (all instances of 'asl' are that upon which something else is built).
This definition aligns with conventional usage and avoids the overbreadth of al-Razi's definition.

(Misk al-Malih) Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. We will explain additionally. Secondly, haqiqi. He explains the limit [definition]. When explaining the limit additionally, he is stating the investigation of the word 'usul'. 'Usul' is the plural of 'asl'. 'Asl' means 'that upon which something else is built'. Then he clarified that building (ibtina') is of two types: (1) sensory building, (2) rational building. The word 'ibtina'' includes both. The first example is the building of the roof upon the wall. The second example the author gave is the ordering of a ruling upon the evidence. And its definition as 'that which is needed' (al-muhtaj ilayh) is not exclusive (la yatrud). Imam al-Razi defined it as such in al-Mahsul. The author's purpose is to refute Imam al-Razi. Imam al-Razi defined 'asl' as 'that which is needed' – i.e., 'asl' is the thing to which another thing is in need. 'Allamah Sadr al-Shari'ah, while refuting, says that the definition which the Imam mentioned in al-Mahsul is incorrect; the reason is that this definition is not exclusive (mani' an dukhul ghayr). Know that definition is either haqiqi... [Urdu continues explaining haqiqi and ismi definitions, conditions of muttarid and mun'akis, and finally that al-Razi's definition fails because 'muhtaj ilayh' applies to five types of causes and conditions, while 'asl' only applies to material cause.]
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' (origin) as presented in his work al-Mahsul. The author, following Sadr al-Shari'ah, argues that al-Razi's definition is not exclusive (muttarid) because it applies to more than just the term 'asl'. The passage first explains the two types of building (ibtina'): sensory and rational, linking to the definition of 'asl' as 'that upon which something else is built'. Then it introduces a preamble about the nature of definitions. The author distinguishes between haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal) definitions. Haqiqi definitions describe the essence of a thing as it exists in reality, like 'man is a rational animal'. Ismi definitions explain the conventional meaning of a term, like defining 'asl' as 'that upon which something else is built'. For both types, the conditions of 'mut'arid' (exclusive) and 'mun'akis' (coextensive) are required. 'Muttarid' means whenever the definition applies, the defined term applies. 'Mun'akis' means whenever the defined term applies, the definition applies. For example, defining 'man' as 'walking animal' is not muttarid because it also applies to horse and donkey. Defining 'man' as 'rational animal' is muttarid and mun'akis. The author then applies this to al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'that which is needed' (al-muhtaj ilayh). He points out that 'that which is needed' applies to five categories: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and conditions. However, the term 'asl' in its technical sense only applies to the material cause. Thus al-Razi's definition is not muttarid; it includes things that are not called 'asl'. Therefore, it is not a valid definition. This is a classic Hanafi critique of the Mutakallimin approach to definitions, emphasizing precision and the need for definitions to be both comprehensive and exclusive.

Key Terms
تعريف حقيقي (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that describes the real essence of a thing as it exists in reality (e.g., defining man as rational animal).
تعريف اسمي (ta'rif ismi): A definition that explains the conventional meaning of a term (what the word is coined for), not the real essence (e.g., defining 'asl' as 'that upon which something else is built').
طرد وعكس (tard wa 'aks): Two conditions for a valid definition: tard means the definition applies only to the defined (exclusive), 'aks means the definition applies to all instances of the defined (comprehensive). Together they ensure the definition is coextensive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is al-Razi's definition of 'asl' (as 'al-muhtaj ilayh') not valid?
A) Because it is too narrow and does not include all types of causes.
B) Because it applies to five types of causes and conditions, while 'asl' only refers to the material cause, making it too broad.
C) Because it is a nominal definition instead of a real definition.
D) Because it was not endorsed by Sadr al-Shari'ah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi critique of al-Razi's definition of 'asl' demonstrates that a valid definition must be both exclusive and comprehensive, a principle applied across usul al-fiqh.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner

Haqiqi and Ismi Definitions with Conditions of Tard and Aks
Explaining definition types and the logical conditions for valid definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions and apply the conditions of tard and aks to evaluate a definition's validity.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be co-extensive: not broader nor narrower than the definiendum.

Definitions in usul al-fiqh can describe real essences (haqiqi) or merely explain the coinage of a term (ismi). Regardless of type, every definition must satisfy twin logical conditions: tard and aks. This lesson unpacks these conditions with examples from the Hanafi logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify definition type
Determine whether the definiendum is a real quiddity (māhiyya ḥaqīqiyya) or a conceptual one (māhiyya iʿtibāriyya). This decides if the definition is haqiqi or ismi.
Real quiddities have real definitions; conceptual ones have nominal definitions.
2
Check tard (applicability)
Tard: Whenever the definition applies, the definiendum must also apply. If the definition applies to something not called by the definiendum, it fails tard (not muttarid).
Tard ensures exclusivity (maniʿ).
3
Check aks (comprehensiveness)
Aks: Whenever the definiendum applies, the definition must also apply. If a genuine instance of the definiendum fails the definition, it fails aks (not munʿakis).
Aks ensures inclusivity (jāmiʿ).
4
Evaluate co-extensiveness
A valid definition must be perfectly co-extensive (musāwī) with the definiendum – neither broader (aʿamm) nor narrower (akhass). Tard and aks together guarantee this.
If either condition fails, the definition is invalid.

مسک الملیح شرح التی besturdubooks علی کثیرین متفقين بالحقائق فی جواب ماضو کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے خلاصہ اینکہ تعریف اسمی اس بات کو بیان کرنے کیلئے ہوتی ہے کہ سید اسم و لفظ کسی مفہوم کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے مثلا جب سوال کیا جائے ما هو الاصل جتو جواب میں وہی مفہوم مرکب ذکر کر دیا جائے گا۔ ما يبتنی علیه غیره مصنف یہ فرماتے ہیں ماحیات حقیقیہ ثابت نفس الامر کی تعریف ہمیشہ تعریف حقیقی ہوگی جیسے تعریف الانسان بالحيوان الناطق و تعریف الفرس بالحيوان الصاحل وغیرہ اور ماحیات اعتباریہ کی تعریف تعریف اسمی ہوگی جیسے تعریف الاصل، نا یقنی علیہ غیرہ ، تعريف الجنس ، کلی مقول الخ تعریف النوع کلی مقول على كثیرین متفقين الخ۔ وشرط لكلا التعريفين الطرد والعكس اى كلما ! مقصد عبارت یہ ہے دونوں تعریفیں ( حقیقی واسمی ) کیلئے طر دو عکس شرط ہے۔ طرد کا مقصد مانع ہونا اور عکس کا مقصد جامع ہونا مصنف طرد کی تعریف یہ کر رہے ہیں كلما صدق عليه الحد صدق عليه المحدود جہاں تعریف وجد صادق آ رہی ہو معرف محدود بھی صادق آئے اگر حد و تعریف صادق ہے محدود صادق نہیں ہے تو تعریف مطرود نہیں ہوگی بلکہ کہا جائے گا هذا التعريف غير مطرد وغير مانع مثلا انسان کی تعریف کی جائے ھو حیوان ماش یہ تعریف غیر مطرد ہے کیونکہ حیوان ماش تو فرس وحمار پر بھی صادق ہے جب کہ اس کو انسان نہیں کہا جاتا تو تعریف صادق آ رہی ہے اور محدود ومعرف صادق نہیں آرہا اور عکس کی تعریف کی گئی ہے کلما صدق علیہ الحد و صدق علیہ الحد جہاں محدود و معرف صادق آئے حد تعریف بھی صادق آئے اگر محدود معرف تو صادق آ رہا ہے لیکن تعریف صادق نہیں آ رہی تو وہ تعریف منعکس نہ ہوگی بلکہ کہا جائے گا هذا التعريف غير منعكس وغير جامع مثلاً انسان کی تعریف کی جائے ھو حیوان کا تب بالفعل یہ تعریف غیر منعکس ہے کیونکہ جو انسان کا تب بالفعل نہیں ہے اُس پر محدود (انسان) تو صادق آ رہا ہے لیکن تعریف وجد صادق نہیں آ رہی لہذا یہ تعریف جامع لافراد المعرف نہیں ہے خلاصہ اینکه تعریف حقیقی واسی میں طر دو عکس و منع وجمع شرط ہے۔ یعنوان دیگر تعریف کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ معرف کے مساوی ہو اعم من المعرف بھی نہ ہو اخص بھی نہ ہو۔ ولا شك ان تعریف الخ اس عبارت سے مصنف تعریف الا صل کی تعیین فرمار ہے ہیں کہ تعریف الاصل ہر حال میں تعریف اسکمی ہے خواہ ماینی علیہ غیرہ ہو ( کما عرفا) خوا تحتاج الیہ ہو ( کما عرفہ الرازی) لہذا اس تعریف کیلئے طر دو کس شرط ہو گا نا التعريف الذی ذکر فی المحصول لا طبر وبعد التمہید علامہ صدر الشریعہ مقصود ( تردید رازی و تفصیل عدم اطراد ) کی طرف عود فرمارہے ہیں کہ امام رازی کی تعریف مطرد نہیں ہے کیونکہ محتاج الیہ پانچ چیزیں ہیں (۱) علت مادی (۲) علت صوری (۳) علت فاعلی (۴) علت غائی (۵) شروط مثلا کاریگری و صنعت کے اسباب و آلات ۔ تو تعریف اصل (محتاج الیہ ) پانچ اشیاء پر صادق آ رہی ہے جبکہ معرف لفظ اصل فقط علت مادی پر صادق آتا ہے۔ باقی اشیاء اربعہ کو اصل نہیں کہا جاتا تو تعریف رازی غیر افراد معرف پر صادق آ رہی ہے لہذا یہ تعریف مطرد و مانع نہیں فلا یصح تعریف الرازی۔
Misk al-Malih Sharh al-Tawdih: ... Definition ismi indicates that the word is coined for a meaning. For example, when asked 'what is asl?', the answer will mention that same meaning. The author says: Real quiddities (haqiqiyya) fixed in themselves always have a real definition (haqiqi), like the definition of human as 'rational animal' and horse as 'whinnying animal'. Conceptual quiddities (i'tibariyya) have a nominal definition (ismi), like the definition of asl ('that on which something else depends'), definition of genus as 'universal predicated of many differing in quiddity', definition of species as 'universal predicated of many agreeing in quiddity'. Both definitions require tard (comprehensiveness) and aks (converse/exclusiveness). The meaning: both definitions (haqiqi and ismi) require tard and aks. The purpose of tard is to be exclusive (mani'); the purpose of aks is to be comprehensive (jami'). The author defines tard: 'Whenever the definition applies, the definiendum applies.' If the definition applies but the definiendum does not, the definition is not muttarid (comprehensive) but is muntakas? Actually it is said 'this definition is not muttarid and not mani'. For example, if human is defined as 'walking animal', this definition is not muttarid because 'walking animal' applies to horse and donkey, while they are not called human: the definition applies but the definiendum does not. Aks is defined: 'Whenever the definiendum applies, the definition applies.' If the definiendum applies but the definition does not, the definition is not mun'akis (exclusive) and not jami'. For example, if human is defined as 'actually writing animal', this definition is not mun'akis because a human who does not actually write still is human: the definiendum applies but the definition does not, so the definition is not comprehensive of all individuals of the definiendum. In summary, real and nominal definitions require tard and aks, and exclusiveness and inclusiveness. In other words, a definition must be co-extensive with the definiendum: not broader nor narrower. The phrase 'wa la shakka anna...' The author determines the definition of asl; it is always nominal, whether it is 'that on which something else depends' (as the author defined) or 'that to which something else is in need' (as al-Razi defined). Hence for this definition, the condition of tard applies. The definition mentioned in al-Mahsul is not muttarid. After the introduction, Sadr al-Shari'a returns to the purpose of refuting al-Razi and explaining the lack of tard. Al-Razi's definition is not muttarid because 'that to which something else is in need' includes five things: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and conditions. The definition of asl (that which is in need) applies to all five, while the word 'asl' applies only to the material cause. The other four are not called 'asl'; thus al-Razi's definition applies to things outside the definiendum, so it is not muttarid and not mani'; hence al-Razi's definition is invalid.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of definition theory in logic as applied to usul al-fiqh. The commentator distinguishes between 'haqiqi' definitions (for real quiddities) and 'ismi' definitions (for conceptual entities). Real definitions describe the essence, e.g., human = rational animal. Nominal definitions are mere explanations of the term's coinage, e.g., the definition of 'asl' as 'something on which something else depends.' Both types must fulfill the twin conditions of tard and aks. Tard ensures that the definition applies to all instances of the definiendum (so it is inclusive but also exclusive: it does not apply to non-instances – this is the 'mani' aspect). Aks ensures that all instances of the definiendum are covered by the definition (so it is comprehensive). The commentator gives examples: defining human as 'walking animal' fails tard because it applies to horses. Defining human as 'actually writing animal' fails aks because non-writing humans are excluded. Later, the text applies this to Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'that to which something else is in need' (ma yahtaju ilayhi ghayruh). This is broader than the true meaning because 'need' includes four other kinds of causes besides the material cause. Since only the material cause is called 'asl' in common usage, the definition is not muttarid and therefore invalid. The commentator notes that Sadr al-Shari'a is refuting al-Razi on this point. The Hanafi position, following the author of al-Tawdih, is that the definition of 'asl' is nominal and must be limited to the material cause in this context.

Key Terms
التعريف الحقيقي (al-ta'rīf al-ḥaqīqī): Definition of a real quiddity (māhiyya ḥaqīqiyya) that exists in itself; it describes the essence.
التعريف الاسمي (al-ta'rīf al-ismī): Definition of a conceptual quiddity (māhiyya iʿtibāriyya); it explains the coinage of a term.
الطرد (al-ṭard): The condition that wherever the definition applies, the definiendum applies (comprehensiveness exclusivity).
العكس (al-ʿaks): The condition that wherever the definiendum applies, the definition applies (comprehensiveness inclusivity).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A student defines 'qiyas' as 'analogy between two cases'. Which condition of valid definition does this likely violate according to the passage?
A) Tard, because it includes analogies that are not qiyas in usul (e.g., poetic analogy)
B) Aks, because it excludes some valid qiyas (e.g., qiyas with illa)
C) Neither, it is a valid definition
D) Both, it is too broad and too narrow

Key Takeaway
A valid definition in usul al-fiqh must satisfy tard (exclusivity) and aks (comprehensiveness), ensuring it is perfectly co-extensive with the definiendum.

Applying Definition Conditions: The Case of 'Asl' and the Refutation of al-Razi's Definition
Applying definition theory to critique al-Razi's definition of 'asl'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of tard and aks to critique al-Razi's definition of 'asl' and explain why the Hanafi definition is preferred.

Core Idea
Al-Razi's definition of 'asl' fails tard because it includes entities that are not called 'asl' in legal usage.

In this lesson, we apply the logical conditions from the previous lesson to a real usul dispute: the definition of 'asl'. Imam al-Razi proposed a broad definition that Hanafis reject as invalid because it violates tard. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate definitions in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition conditions
Remember that a valid definition must be co-extensive: tard (definition applies only to definiendum) and aks (definiendum always satisfies definition).
2
State al-Razi's definition
Al-Razi defined 'asl' as 'that to which something else is in need' (ma yahtāju ilayhi ghayruh). This includes all five causes: material, formal, efficient, final, and conditions.
This is a broader definition than the Hanafi one.
3
Apply the tard test
Check if al-Razi's definition applies only to what is conventionally called 'asl'. In usul, 'asl' refers only to the material cause (e.g., the original case in qiyas). But 'need' also applies to other causes like efficient cause (e.g., the mujtahid) which is not called 'asl'. Thus the definition applies to non-instances, failing tard.
Tard fails because the definition is too broad.
4
Apply the aks test
Check if every genuine 'asl' satisfies al-Razi's definition. Does every material cause fit 'that to which something else is in need'? Yes, because the branch depends on the original. So aks may hold. But since tard fails, the definition is invalid overall.
A valid definition requires both conditions to hold.
5
Conclude with Hanafi preference
The Hanafi definition 'ma yabtanī 'alayhi ghayruh' (that on which something else depends) is limited to the material cause and passes both tard and aks. Therefore it is the correct definition for 'asl' in usul al-fiqh.
This dispute shows the practical importance of definition precision.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of definition theory in logic as applied to usul al-fiqh. The commentator distinguishes between 'haqiqi' definitions (for real quiddities) and 'ismi' definitions (for conceptual entities). Real definitions describe the essence, e.g., human = rational animal. Nominal definitions are mere explanations of the term's coinage, e.g., the definition of 'asl' as 'something on which something else depends.' Both types must fulfill the twin conditions of tard and aks. Tard ensures that the definition applies to all instances of the definiendum (so it is inclusive but also exclusive: it does not apply to non-instances – this is the 'mani' aspect). Aks ensures that all instances of the definiendum are covered by the definition (so it is comprehensive). The commentator gives examples: defining human as 'walking animal' fails tard because it applies to horses. Defining human as 'actually writing animal' fails aks because non-writing humans are excluded. Later, the text applies this to Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'that to which something else is in need' (ma yahtaju ilayhi ghayruh). This is broader than the true meaning because 'need' includes four other kinds of causes besides the material cause. Since only the material cause is called 'asl' in common usage, the definition is not muttarid and therefore invalid. The commentator notes that Sadr al-Shari'a is refuting al-Razi on this point. The Hanafi position, following the author of al-Tawdih, is that the definition of 'asl' is nominal and must be limited to the material cause in this context.

Key Terms
الأصل (al-aṣl): In usul al-fiqh, the original case whose ruling is known and from which the branch is analogized.
العلة المادية (al-ʿilla al-māddiyya): Material cause: the substance or subject in which the ruling inheres.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is al-Razi's definition of 'asl' considered not muttarid according to the Hanafi analysis?
A) Because it is not a nominal definition
B) Because it applies to efficient, formal, final causes, and conditions, which are not called 'asl'
C) Because it fails aks
D) Because it is too narrow

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's definition of 'asl' fails the condition of tard because it is not co-extensive with the conventional use of the term; therefore the Hanafi definition is the valid one.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

8 min
Preferring the Idafi Definition of Usul al-Fiqh
Debate on defining usul al-fiqh: iḍāfī vs laqabī with resolution of pronoun inconsistency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the iḍāfī and laqabī definitions of uṣūl al-fiqh and evaluate the arguments for which should be presented first.

Core Idea
Uṣūl al-fiqh is both a construct and a proper name; its definition method determines textbook structure.

This passage from Misk al-Malih presents a key methodological dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: how should the term 'uṣūl al-fiqh' be defined? The author, commenting on Taftazani's Al-Talwih, explains that the term originated as an iḍāfī (construct) compound but later became a technical title (laqab). This dual nature leads to two possible definitions, and scholars disagree on which should be presented first. Understanding this debate is crucial for grasping how the Hanafi tradition structures the very introduction of its legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the dual nature of 'uṣūl al-fiqh'
Identify that the term has two aspects: as an iḍāfī compound (where 'uṣūl' is plural and 'fiqh' is its object) and as a proper name (laqab) for the science. This duality is the source of the two definitions.
The iḍāfī sense treats the term literally; the laqabī sense treats it as a technical title.
2
Define the two definition types
Explain that the iḍāfī definition defines the muḍāf ('uṣūl') and muḍāf ilayh ('fiqh') separately, while the laqabī definition defines the term as a single unit without analyzing its parts.
The iḍāfī definition is like building a term from components; the laqabī definition is like giving a proper name.
3
Analyze the first group's arguments
Study the two proofs given by those who prioritize the iḍāfī definition: (1) the original (manqūl ʿanhu) takes precedence over the transferred (manqūl), and (2) presenting the laqabī first forces repetition in defining 'fiqh', since it must be defined both in the laqabī definition and again as muḍāf ilayh in the iḍāfī definition.
This group includes the author of Al-Tawdih.
4
Analyze the second group's arguments
Consider the two proofs of those who prioritize the laqabī definition: (1) 'uṣūl al-fiqh' has become a proper name, so the scientific meaning is directly expressed by the laqabī definition; (2) the laqabī definition is like a simple term (basīṭ) which takes precedence over a compound (murakkab) like the iḍāfī definition.
This group may include Ibn al-Ḥājib.
5
Resolve the pronoun inconsistency
Note that the author uses a feminine pronoun (e.g., 'arrafahā') when giving the iḍāfī definition and a masculine pronoun (e.g., 'na'rifuhu') when giving the laqabī definition. The resolution is that in the iḍāfī sense, 'uṣūl' is plural (non-rational) taking feminine pronoun; in the laqabī sense, it is a singular proper name taking masculine pronoun. Both are correct.
This shows how linguistic usage reflects the two legal aspects of the term.

النفس مالها وما عليها (۲) دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ تعریف تھی میں لفظ نقہ نہ ذکر کیا جائے فقط اس کی تفسیر ذکر کی جائے عبارت یوں ہوگی ھو علم بقواعد التي يتوصل بها الى معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها اول صورت مردود ہے کیونکہ اس میں طول بلا سود ہے ثانی صورت اگر چہ قابل قبول ہے لیکن اس میں وہی تکرار والی خرابی لازم آتی ہے کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ تو یہاں فقہ کی تعریف ہوگی پھر جب حد اضافی کی جائے گی تو اس میں دوبارہ فقہ کی تعریف کرنی پڑے گی اس لئے کہ الفقہ مضاف الیہ ہے حد اضافی یہ ہے کہ مضاف اور مضاف الیہ کی علیحدہ تعریف کی جائے تو بحیثیت مضاف الیہ ہونے کے فقہ کی دوبارہ تعریف کرنی پڑے گی تو تکرار محض لازم آئے گا جس طرح کہ علامہ ابن حاجب نے اپنی کتاب الاضول میں ایسا ہی کیا ہے لیکن اگر تعریف اضافی کو مقدم کیا جائے تو تکرار والی خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی کیونکہ فقہ کی تعریف مفصلاً اس میں آجائے گی بعدہ حدیقی میں صرف الفقہ کا لفظ ذکر کر دینا کافی ہو گا تعریف کی ضرورت نہیں ہوگی طالب الفقہ کرد علم پہلے ہی تعریف جان چکا ہوگا۔ گروہ ثانی بھی دو دلیلیں بیان کرتا ہے (۱) دلیل اول یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ اب علم بن چکا ہے اس فن کا اور اعلام میں مقصود معنی علمی ہوا کرتا ہے اور حدیقی میں بھی معنی علمی بیان کیا جاتا ہے لہذا اس کو مقدم ہونا چاہیے اضافی پر جو که غیر مقصود ہے (۲) دلیل دوم یہ ہے کہ حد اضافی بمنزلہ مرکب کے ہے اور حالتی بمنزلہ بسیط کے ہے اور ، ضابطہ ہے البسيط مقدم على المركب البذا جو بمنزلہ بسیط ہے وہ بھی مقدم ہوگا بمنزلہ مرکب پر اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ حد لقمی مقدم علی الاضافی ہوگی۔
ولما كان اصول الفقه عند قصد معنى الاضافي جمعا الخ غرض شارح جواب سوال مقدر ۔ سوال! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت میں تضاد و تعارض ہے کیونکہ یہاں حد اضافی بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا فعرفها اولاها ضمیر اصول الفقہ کی طرف عود کر رہی ہے تو یہاں ضمیر مئونث راجع کی ہے اور آگے حد قمی بیان کرتے ہوئے کہا فا الآن نعرفه با عتبارا نہ لقب العلم مخصوص ( ملاحظہ فرمائیں صفحہ نمبر ۵ پر ) وہاں اصول فقہ کی طرف ضمیر مذکر کو راجع کیا ہے اب سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اصول الفقہ مفرد ہے یا جمع اگر مفرد ہے تو ضمیر مئونث راجع کرنا اور فنتعر فھا کہنا صحیح نہیں ہے اگر جمع ہے تو ضمیر مذکر راجع کرنا اور فتعرفہ کہنا درست نہیں ہے دونوں میں کوئی ایک غلط ہے۔ جواب ! شارح تفتازانی جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ مصنف کی عبارت میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے اور ضمیر مئونث و مذکر لانا دونوں صحیح ہیں وجہ یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ میں دو حیثیتیں ہیں ایک معنی اضافی ہونے کی اور دوسری معنی لقمی ہونے کی اول معنی کے اعتبار سے یہ جمع ہے ثانی معنی کے اعتبار سے مفرد ہے کعبد اللہ فی حالتہ العلم البندا حد اضافی بیان کرتے ہوئے اس کی طرف ضمیر مؤنث راجع کی کیونکہ جمع غیر ذ والعقول کی طرف ضمیر مئونث راجع ہوتی ہے اور حد قمی بیان کرتے ہوئے اس کی طرف ضمیر مذکر راجع کی کیونکہ بائیں حیثیت وہ مفرد ہے۔ فلا تضاد ولا تعارض بینھما ، سوان
Misk al-Malih. Explanation of Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. He had stated (1) Usul al-Fiqh is the predicate of the deleted subject 'hadha'. (2) Usul al-Fiqh is the subject of a past sentence. Taftazani, while clarifying the first syntactic possibility, says: When the listener/student knows that a science is distinguished by its definition and subject matter, the soul and heart of the student of usul al-fiqh become eager and desirous to know the definition of this art so that it can be distinguished from other sciences. But just as the listener/student was preparing to ask, the author, seeing the eagerness of the eager listener before the question, himself said, 'This is what we mentioned: usul al-fiqh' and then began to define usul al-fiqh, so that the listener/student would not need to ask. In other words, the author answered the student's implicit question. And 'he said regarding the second' explains the second syntactic possibility: that the author, acting on behalf of the eager listener, himself asks, 'What is usul al-fiqh?' and then begins to define it: 'And usul al-fiqh is a title for this art, etc.' The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to explain the text of Al-Tawdih. He says: 'Usul al-fiqh is a title for this specific art; it was transferred from the iḍāfī compound; i.e., originally it was an iḍāfī compound, then it was transferred from that to become a title for this art. After the transfer, the composition is not considered. So it has two aspects: (1) that of iḍāfah, (2) that of being a title. Therefore it also has two definitions: one according to the iḍāfī aspect, i.e., defining the muḍāf separately and the muḍāf ilayh separately; the second according to the title aspect. The first is called the iḍāfī definition and the second the laqabī definition. Some present the laqabī definition.' The purpose of the commentator is to mention the disagreement of authors. It has previously been known that usul al-fiqh has two definitions: an iḍāfī definition and a laqabī definition. But authors disagree as to which definition should be presented first. Some scholars prefer the iḍāfī definition; some prefer the laqabī. The first group, which includes the author, gives two proofs: (1) The laqabī definition is transferred from the iḍāfī, and the iḍāfī is the source of transfer. The rule is that the source of transfer takes precedence over the transferred. Therefore the iḍāfī definition should also take precedence over the laqabī. (2) The second proof: if the laqabī definition is presented first, then repetition without benefit in the definition of fiqh necessarily follows, because the definition of usul al-fiqh is 'the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh'. So 'fiqh' is mentioned in the definition of usul al-fiqh, and the laqabī definition of usul al-fiqh cannot be complete until fiqh is defined, because for a complete clarification of the defined, it is necessary to define its component parts; otherwise ignorance in definition would be necessary. Therefore, when mentioning the laqabī definition, defining fiqh becomes necessary. Then there are two possibilities: (1) In the definition, the word 'fiqh' and its definition are both mentioned; the phrase would be: 'It is the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh, which is knowledge of the self's rights and obligations.' (2) The second possibility: In the definition, the word 'fiqh' is not mentioned, only its interpretation is mentioned; the phrase would be: 'It is the knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at knowledge of the self's rights and obligations.' The first possibility is rejected because it is unnecessarily long. The second possibility, though acceptable, has the same defect of repetition, because once fiqh is defined here, then when the iḍāfī definition is given, fiqh would have to be defined again, because 'al-fiqh' is the muḍāf ilayh. The iḍāfī definition is that the muḍāf and muḍāf ilayh are defined separately. So, by virtue of being muḍāf ilayh, fiqh would have to be defined again, leading to pure repetition, as Ibn al-Ḥājib did in his book. But if the iḍāfī definition is presented first, then the defect of repetition does not necessarily follow, because the definition of fiqh will come in detail in it. Later, in the laqabī definition, merely mentioning the word 'fiqh' will suffice; no definition is needed, as the student will have already known the definition of fiqh. The second group also gives two proofs: (1) The first proof: Usul al-fiqh has now become a proper name for this art, and in proper names, the scientific meaning is intended, and in the laqabī definition the scientific meaning is also stated, so it should take precedence over the iḍāfī, which is not intended (as a proper name). (2) The second proof: The iḍāfī definition is like a compound, and the laqabī is like a simple term. The rule is that the simple takes precedence over the compound. Therefore, what is like a simple term should also take precedence over what is like a compound. From this it is established that the laqabī definition takes precedence over the iḍāfī. 'And since usul al-fiqh, when intending the iḍāfī meaning, is plural, etc.' The purpose of the commentator is to answer an implicit question. Question: There is contradiction and inconsistency in the author's expression, because here, while giving the iḍāfī definition, he said 'fa-'arrafahā awwalan' — the pronoun refers to usul al-fiqh, so here he used a feminine pronoun. And later, while giving the laqabī definition, he said 'fa-'āna na'rifuhu bi'tibāri annahu laqabun lil-'ilmi al-makhṣūṣ' (see page 5); there he used a masculine pronoun for usul al-fiqh. Now the question: Is usul al-fiqh singular or plural? If it is singular, then using a feminine pronoun and saying 'fa-nata'arrafuhā' is incorrect. If it is plural, then using a masculine pronoun and saying 'fa-nata'arrafuhu' is incorrect. One of them must be wrong. Answer: The commentator Taftazani answers that there is no contradiction in the author's expression, and using both feminine and masculine pronouns is correct. The reason is that usul al-fiqh has two aspects: one as an iḍāfī meaning, and the other as a laqabī meaning. According to the first meaning, it is plural; according to the second meaning, it is singular, like 'Abdullah in the state of being a proper noun. When giving the iḍāfī definition, a feminine pronoun was used for it because for non-rational plurals, a feminine pronoun is used. And when giving the laqabī definition, a masculine pronoun was used for it because in that aspect it is singular. So there is no contradiction or inconsistency between them; all is well.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is an usul al-fiqh definition commentary from Taftazani's Al-Talwih explaining a section of Sadr al-Shariah's Al-Tawdih. The discussion focuses on the definition of the discipline 'usul al-fiqh'. The author explains that 'usul al-fiqh' originated as an iḍāfī (construct) compound but later became a technical title (laqab) for this science. Consequently, it can be defined in two ways: (1) an iḍāfī definition, which treats it as a compound and defines each part separately; and (2) a laqabī definition, which treats it as a simple technical term. A dispute exists among scholars as to which definition should be presented first. The first group (including the author of Al-Tawdih) argues for the iḍāfī definition first, giving two reasons: first, the laqabī definition is derived from the iḍāfī, and the original takes precedence over the derivative; second, if the laqabī definition is presented first, one would need to define 'fiqh' within it, leading to repetition when later defining it again as the muḍāf ilayh in the iḍāfī definition. The second group argues for the laqabī definition first, also with two reasons: first, 'usul al-fiqh' has become a proper name (ʿalam) for this art, and in proper names the scientific meaning is what matters, so the laqabī definition that expresses that meaning should be prioritized over the iḍāfī definition which is not directly intended; second, the laqabī definition is like a simple term (basīṭ) while the iḍāfī is like a compound (murakkab), and the simple takes precedence. The passage then resolves a potential confusion in the author's wording: in the iḍāfī definition he uses a feminine pronoun (referring to usul al-fiqh as a plural of non-rationals), while in the laqabī definition he uses a masculine pronoun (referring to it as a singular proper name). Taftazani explains that both are correct because usul al-fiqh has two aspects: as an iḍāfī compound it is plural (since 'uṣūl' is plural), and as a laqab it is singular (like a proper noun). Thus there is no contradiction.

Key Terms
اصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The specific art/science; originally an iḍāfī compound but used as a technical title (laqab) for the science of legal methodology.
تعریف اضافی (taʿrīf iḍāfī): The definition of a compound expression by defining its parts (muḍāf and muḍāf ilayh) separately.
تعریف لقبی (taʿrīf laqabī): The definition of a term as a simple technical title (laqab), treating it as a proper name without analyzing its parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first group (which includes the author of Al-Tawdih), why should the idafi definition of usul al-fiqh be presented before the laqabi definition?
A) Because the laqabi definition is simpler and thus easier to understand.
B) Because the laqabi definition leads to unnecessary repetition in defining 'fiqh'.
C) Because the laqabi definition is derived from the idafi definition, and the derived must come after the original.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The iḍāfī definition avoids repetition and respects the principle that the original definition precedes the derived, while the laqabī definition treats 'usul al-fiqh' as a proper name and is simpler but can cause redundancy.

Definition of Laqab and Classification of Proper Names
Defining laqab and distinguishing it from kunyah and ism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define laqab, distinguish it from kunyah and ism using two classical methods, and apply the definition to examples like Abu Jahl.

Core Idea
A laqab is a proper name indicating praise or blame – meaning can override form in classification.

This lesson introduces the concept of laqab, a type of proper noun that conveys praise or blame. The commentator Taftazani provides a definition and then explains how proper names are classified into three categories: laqab, kunyah (teknonym), and ism (given name). Two methods of classification are presented, differing in whether they prioritize meaning or form. Understanding this classification is foundational for analyzing the names of sciences in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of laqab
Read the first sentence: 'Laqab is a proper noun that indicates praise or blame.' Recognize that laqab must be a proper noun (alam) and must carry the connotation of praise or blame.
2
Identify the three types of proper nouns
According to the passage, proper nouns are divided into laqab, kunyah, and ism. Kunyah begins with 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm'. Ism is the remainder.
3
Compare the two methods of classification
Method 1: If a proper noun indicates praise/blame, it is laqab regardless of beginning. Method 2: If it begins with 'ab' etc., it is kunyah regardless of meaning. Analyze the example of Abu Jahl under each method.
Method 1: Abu Jahl = laqab (blame). Method 2: Abu Jahl = kunyah (starts with 'Abu').
4
Note the third view (composite classification)
Some scholars consider names like Abu Jahl as both kunyah and laqab, depending on aspect. This is a valid compromise.

اس عبارت میں شارح یہ بتلانا چاہتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ علم کی تین اقسام میں سے کون سی قسم ہے تو فرماتے ہیں کہ اصول فقہ اس فن کا لقب ہے کیونکہ لقب اس علم کو کہا جاتا ہے جو مشعر بسوئے مطرح و زم ہو اصول فقہ کا معنی مشعر الی المدح ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کا معنی ہے فقہ کا بنی اور بنیاد اور فقہ وہ علم ہے جس کے ذریعہ سے نظام معاش دنیوی اور نجات معاد حاصل ہوتی ہے تو علم فقہ ایک نور ہو گا اور اصول فقہ نور علی نور ہو جائے گا مبنی ہونے کی وجہ سے اصول فقہ کا علم مشعر الی المدح ہوگا اس لیے اس کو لقب کہا جائے گا۔ فائدہ! علوم وفنون کے جو نام اور اعلام ہیں مثلا کا النحو الصرف المنطق، الفقه ، وغیره نیه اسامی فنون و علوم علم میں یا اسم جنس ہیں یا علم جنس ہیں اس میں تین مذاہب ہیں (۱) علامہ سبکی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ یہ اسامی فنون اسم جنس ہیں جیسے الرجل الماء الشراب ، اسم جنس ہیں اس کی تین دلیلیں ہیں (۱) جس طرح اسم جنس موضوع ہوتا ہے امر کلی کیلئے اور قلیل وکثیر پر صادق آتا ہے اسی طرح یہ اسامی فنون بھی امریکی کیلئے موضوع ہیں یعنی لطائفة من المسائل المعتدة (۲) علم کے مسائل میں کمی بیشی ہوتی رہتی ہے اور یہ بھی کلی کا خاصہ ہے کیونکہ علم کے مصداق میں کمی بیشی نہیں ہوتی (۳) اسامی فنون پر الف لام داخل ہوتا ہے جیسے المنطق الصرف وغیرہ جبکہ اعلام پر الف لام داخل نہیں
And laqab is a proper noun that indicates praise or blame. In this phrase, the commentator Taftazani is defining laqab: laqab is a proper noun in which the meaning of praise or blame is found. Further clarification: a proper noun (alam) is that which is placed for a specific thing. Then it has three types: (1) laqab, (2) kunyah, (3) ism. The exhaustive proof is that a proper noun is free from two states: either it indicates praise or blame, or not. First is laqab. Second is free from two states: either it begins with the word 'ab' or 'umm', or not. First is kunyah, second is ism. According to the first method, it is necessary that a kunyah not indicate praise or blame; otherwise it would enter into laqab, even if it begins with 'ab' or 'umm'. Hence, Abu Jahl, Abu al-Kalam, Abu al-Khair, for this reason, enter into laqab, not kunyah. Some scholars presented another method: either a proper noun begins with 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm', or not. First is kunyah, second is free from two states: either it indicates praise or blame, or not. First is laqab, second is ism. Based on this, for laqab it is necessary that it not begin with 'ab' or 'umm', even if it indicates praise. Hence, Abu Jahl etc. enter into kunyah, even if they indicate praise or blame. Some scholars say that a kunyah that indicates praise or blame is in one aspect kunyah and in another aspect laqab, and there is no harm in that. And Usul al-Fiqh is a proper noun for this art indicating... In this phrase, the commentator wants to explain which of the three types of proper nouns Usul al-Fiqh is. He says that Usul al-Fiqh is a laqab for this art because laqab is called a proper noun that indicates praise or blame. The meaning of Usul al-Fiqh indicates praise because the meaning of Usul al-Fiqh is the foundation of fiqh, and fiqh is the science through which the system of worldly life and salvation in the afterlife are attained. So the science of fiqh is a light, and Usul al-Fiqh becomes light upon light. Due to being foundational, the science of Usul al-Fiqh indicates praise, therefore it is called a laqab. Benefit: The names and proper nouns of sciences and arts, such as al-nahw, al-sarf, al-mantiq, al-fiqh, etc., are these names of arts proper nouns (a'lam) or common nouns (asma' jins)? There are three schools: (1) Allama Subki's school: these names of arts are common nouns, like al-rajul, al-ma', al-sharāb. They have three proofs: (1) Just as a common noun is placed for a universal thing and applies to few and many, similarly these names of arts are placed for a universal, i.e., a collection of established issues. (2) The issues of a science increase and decrease, and this is a characteristic of a universal, because the actual science does not increase or decrease. (3) The definite article al can enter on names of arts, like al-mantiq, al-sarf, etc., whereas it does not enter on proper nouns.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage defines laqab (a proper name indicating praise or blame) and classifies proper names into three types: laqab, kunyah (teknonym), and ism (given name). The commentator Taftazani explains two methods of classification: the first method prioritizes meaning (praise/blame) over form (beginning with ab/umm), so names like Abu Jahl are considered laqab due to their blameful meaning. The second method prioritizes form, so names with ab/umm are kunyah regardless of meaning. A third view allows such names to be both. The passage then applies this to 'Usul al-Fiqh', arguing it is a laqab because it indicates praise (foundation of a praiseworthy science). Finally, a note (fa'idah) discusses the linguistic status of names of sciences: whether they are proper nouns or common nouns. Allama Subki's view is presented that they are common nouns, with three linguistic proofs: they are universal, they allow increase/decrease of issues, and they take the definite article. This classification is important in usul al-fiqh for understanding how terms like 'usul al-fiqh' are treated in definitions and rulings.

Key Terms
لقب (laqab): A proper noun that indicates praise or blame.
کنیت (kunyah): A proper noun beginning with 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm'.
اسم (ism): A proper noun that is neither laqab nor kunyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first method of classification, why is 'Abu Jahl' considered a laqab?
A) Because it begins with 'Abu'
B) Because it indicates blame
C) Because it is a common noun
D) Because it is a proper noun

Key Takeaway
A laqab is a proper noun indicating praise or blame; two methods exist to distinguish it from kunyah and ism, with meaning often overriding form for sciences.

Why Usul al-Fiqh is a Laqab
Applying the definition of laqab to the science name 'Usul al-Fiqh'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'Usul al-Fiqh' is classified as a laqab and apply the same reasoning to other science names.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is a laqab because its meaning as the foundation of fiqh indicates praise.

This lesson focuses on the passage where the commentator applies the definition of laqab to the term 'Usul al-Fiqh'. By analyzing its meaning—'the foundation of fiqh'—we see it conveys praise, since fiqh leads to worldly benefit and salvation. Hence, it qualifies as a laqab. This application demonstrates how the linguistic classification works in practice for usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of laqab
Laqab is a proper noun indicating praise or blame. Then identify the proper noun: 'Usul al-Fiqh'.
2
Analyze the meaning of 'Usul al-Fiqh'
The phrase means 'the foundations of fiqh'. Fiqh is the science that guides worldly life and afterlife salvation. Thus, 'foundations of fiqh' is praiseworthy.
The passage describes fiqh as a light and usul al-fiqh as light upon light.
3
Determine if the meaning indicates praise
Yes, because being foundational to a noble science is praiseworthy. Therefore, 'Usul al-Fiqh' is a laqab.
4
Apply to other sciences
Similarly, names like 'Usul al-Din', 'Ilm al-Tafsir', etc., can be evaluated: if they imply praise (e.g., 'foundation of religion'), they are laqabs.

Are Science Names Proper or Common Nouns? The Dispute and Its Proofs
Discussing the linguistic classification of science names

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three positions on whether names of sciences are proper nouns (a'lam) or common nouns (asma' jins) and state the three proofs of Imam Subki's view.

Core Idea
Names of sciences are common nouns, not proper nouns, as argued by Subki with three linguistic proofs.

The passage concludes with a beneficial discussion (fa'idah) on the linguistic status of science names like 'al-nahw', 'al-sarf', etc. Are they proper nouns (a'lam) or common nouns (asma' jins)? The commentator presents three schools, with Imam Subki's view that they are common nouns supported by three proofs. This classification affects how we understand definitions and usage of these terms in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the problem
Recognize that names of sciences (e.g., al-nahw, al-fiqh) could be proper nouns (specific sciences) or common nouns (generic classes).
2
Identify the three schools
There are three opinions: (1) they are common nouns (Subki), (2) they are proper nouns (others), (3) a third view. The passage only elaborates Subki's view.
3
Examine Subki's first proof
Like common nouns (e.g., 'al-rajul'), science names are placed for a universal (a collection of issues). They apply to few and many issues.
4
Examine Subki's second proof
The issues of a science increase and decrease, which is a property of universals, not of a fixed proper noun.
5
Examine Subki's third proof
The definite article 'al' can enter on science names (e.g., al-mantiq), whereas true proper nouns (like Zaid) do not typically take 'al'.
6
Understand the implication for usul
If science names are common nouns, they refer to any instance of that science, affecting how we define 'usul al-fiqh' as a generic methodology.

والـلـقـب علم يشعر بمدح او ذم ! اس عبارت میں شارح تفتازانی لقب کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں کہ لقب وہ علم ہے جس میں مدح یا زم کا معنی پایا جائے مزید وضاحت کیلئے عرض ہے کہ علم وہ ہے جو معین چیز کیلئے وضع کیا جائے پھر اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) لقب (۲) کنیت (۳) اسم دلیل حصریہ ہے کہ علم دو حال سے خالی نہیں مفید مدح وذم ہو گا یا نہ اول لقب ہے ثانی دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا اس کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب یا ام ہوگا یا نہ اول کنیت ہے ثانی اسم ہے۔ اس وجہ مصر کے اعتبار سے کنیت میں ضروری ہوگا کہ وہ مفید مدح وزم نہ ہو ورنہ وہ لقب میں داخل ہو جائے گی اگر چہ اس کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب اورام ہو لہذا ابو جہل ابوالکلام ابوا الخیر بایں وجہ حصر لقب میں داخل ہو نگے نہ کہ کنیت میں بعض حضرات نے بطریق آخر وجہ حضر بیان کی ہے کہ علم کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب یا ابن یا ام ہوگا یا نہ اول کنیت ہے ثانی دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا دال بر مدح وذم ہوگا یا نہ اول لقب ثانی اسم ہے بناء بر میں حصر لقب کیلئے ضروری ہوگا کہ اس کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب اور ام نہ ہوا گر چہ وہ مفید مدرج ہو لہذا ابو جہل وغیرہ کنیت میں داخل ہو جائیں گے اگر چه وه مفید مدرح یا زم ہیں بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ وہ کنیت جو مفید مدح یا زم ہے من وجہ کنیت ہے اور من وجہ لقب ہے ولا باس نیہ واصول الفقه علم لهذا الفن مشعر الخ ! اس عبارت میں شارح یہ بتلانا چاہتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ علم کی تین اقسام میں سے کون سی قسم ہے تو فرماتے ہیں کہ اصول فقہ اس فن کا لقب ہے کیونکہ لقب اس علم کو کہا جاتا ہے جو مشعر بسوئے مطرح و زم ہو اصول فقہ کا معنی مشعر الی المدح ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کا معنی ہے فقہ کا بنی اور بنیاد اور فقہ وہ علم ہے جس کے ذریعہ سے نظام معاش دنیوی اور نجات معاد حاصل ہوتی ہے تو علم فقہ ایک نور ہو گا اور اصول فقہ نور علی نور ہو جائے گا مبنی ہونے کی وجہ سے اصول فقہ کا علم مشعر الی المدح ہوگا اس لیے اس کو لقب کہا جائے گا۔ فائدہ! علوم وفنون کے جو نام اور اعلام ہیں مثلا کا النحو الصرف المنطق، الفقه ، وغیره نیه اسامی فنون و علوم علم میں یا اسم جنس ہیں یا علم جنس ہیں اس میں تین مذاہب ہیں (۱) علامہ سبکی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ یہ اسامی فنون اسم جنس ہیں جیسے الرجل الماء الشراب ، اسم جنس ہیں اس کی تین دلیلیں ہیں (۱) جس طرح اسم جنس موضوع ہوتا ہے امر کلی کیلئے اور قلیل وکثیر پر صادق آتا ہے اسی طرح یہ اسامی فنون بھی امریکی کیلئے موضوع ہیں یعنی لطائفة من المسائل المعتدة (۲) علم کے مسائل میں کمی بیشی ہوتی رہتی ہے اور یہ بھی کلی کا خاصہ ہے کیونکہ علم کے مصداق میں کمی بیشی نہیں ہوتی (۳) اسامی فنون پر الف لام داخل ہوتا ہے جیسے المنطق الصرف وغیرہ جبکہ اعلام پر الف لام داخل نہیں
And laqab is a proper noun that indicates praise or blame. In this phrase, the commentator Taftazani is defining laqab: laqab is a proper noun in which the meaning of praise or blame is found. Further clarification: a proper noun (alam) is that which is placed for a specific thing. Then it has three types: (1) laqab, (2) kunyah, (3) ism. The exhaustive proof is that a proper noun is free from two states: either it indicates praise or blame, or not. First is laqab. Second is free from two states: either it begins with the word 'ab' or 'umm', or not. First is kunyah, second is ism. According to the first method, it is necessary that a kunyah not indicate praise or blame; otherwise it would enter into laqab, even if it begins with 'ab' or 'umm'. Hence, Abu Jahl, Abu al-Kalam, Abu al-Khair, for this reason, enter into laqab, not kunyah. Some scholars presented another method: either a proper noun begins with 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm', or not. First is kunyah, second is free from two states: either it indicates praise or blame, or not. First is laqab, second is ism. Based on this, for laqab it is necessary that it not begin with 'ab' or 'umm', even if it indicates praise. Hence, Abu Jahl etc. enter into kunyah, even if they indicate praise or blame. Some scholars say that a kunyah that indicates praise or blame is in one aspect kunyah and in another aspect laqab, and there is no harm in that. And Usul al-Fiqh is a proper noun for this art indicating... In this phrase, the commentator wants to explain which of the three types of proper nouns Usul al-Fiqh is. He says that Usul al-Fiqh is a laqab for this art because laqab is called a proper noun that indicates praise or blame. The meaning of Usul al-Fiqh indicates praise because the meaning of Usul al-Fiqh is the foundation of fiqh, and fiqh is the science through which the system of worldly life and salvation in the afterlife are attained. So the science of fiqh is a light, and Usul al-Fiqh becomes light upon light. Due to being foundational, the science of Usul al-Fiqh indicates praise, therefore it is called a laqab. Benefit: The names and proper nouns of sciences and arts, such as al-nahw, al-sarf, al-mantiq, al-fiqh, etc., are these names of arts proper nouns (a'lam) or common nouns (asma' jins)? There are three schools: (1) Allama Subki's school: these names of arts are common nouns, like al-rajul, al-ma', al-sharāb. They have three proofs: (1) Just as a common noun is placed for a universal thing and applies to few and many, similarly these names of arts are placed for a universal, i.e., a collection of established issues. (2) The issues of a science increase and decrease, and this is a characteristic of a universal, because the actual science does not increase or decrease. (3) The definite article al can enter on names of arts, like al-mantiq, al-sarf, etc., whereas it does not enter on proper nouns.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage defines laqab (a proper name indicating praise or blame) and classifies proper names into three types: laqab, kunyah (teknonym), and ism (given name). The commentator Taftazani explains two methods of classification: the first method prioritizes meaning (praise/blame) over form (beginning with ab/umm), so names like Abu Jahl are considered laqab due to their blameful meaning. The second method prioritizes form, so names with ab/umm are kunyah regardless of meaning. A third view allows such names to be both. The passage then applies this to 'Usul al-Fiqh', arguing it is a laqab because it indicates praise (foundation of a praiseworthy science). Finally, a note (fa'idah) discusses the linguistic status of names of sciences: whether they are proper nouns or common nouns. Allama Subki's view is presented that they are common nouns, with three linguistic proofs: they are universal, they allow increase/decrease of issues, and they take the definite article. This classification is important in usul al-fiqh for understanding how terms like 'usul al-fiqh' are treated in definitions and rulings.

Key Terms
اسم جنس (ism jins): A common noun that refers to a universal class.
علم (alam): A proper noun in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of Subki's proofs that names of sciences are common nouns?
A) They are placed for a universal
B) They can take the definite article
C) They are always derived from verbs
D) Their issues may increase or decrease

Key Takeaway
Names of sciences are common nouns according to Subki, supported by three proofs: universality, variability of issues, and admission of the definite article.
