Definition of Laqab and Its Application to Usul al-Fiqh
Defining laqab and establishing usul al-fiqh as a laqab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define laqab, distinguish it from kunyah and ism, and apply the classification to identify usul al-fiqh as a laqab.

Core Idea
A laqab is a name conveying praise or blame; usul al-fiqh is a laqab because it is the praiseworthy foundation of fiqh.

In this passage, Sharif Taftazani defines the technical term 'laqab' within the Hanafi usul tradition. Understanding the precise classification of names—laqab, kunyah, ism—is essential for analyzing how disciplines are designated. The commentator then applies this to 'usul al-fiqh', showing that it qualifies as a laqab due to its praiseworthy connotation. This lesson will guide you through the logical division and the application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of proper nouns
Recognize that alam (proper noun) is divided into laqab, kunyah, and ism. Laqab conveys praise or blame, kunyah starts with 'ab'/'umm'/'ibn', and ism is the remainder.
This division is exhaustive according to the text.
2
Examine the two methodological approaches (hasr)
The passage presents two ways to distinguish these types: one prioritizing meaning (praise/blame) and the other prioritizing prefix (ab/umm). Understand how each approach reclassifies examples like Abu Jahl.
The first approach makes Abu Jahl a laqab; the second makes it a kunyah.
3
Apply the definition to usul al-fiqh
The commentator argues that usul al-fiqh is a laqab because its meaning implies praise: it is the foundation of fiqh, which leads to worldly and otherworldly success.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the praiseworthy connotation.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi debate on kunyah with praise/blame
Some scholars consider such kunyah as dual-aspect (kunyah and laqab). This shows flexibility in classification within the school.
The commentator adopts Taftazani's view but notes the alternative.

والـلـقـب علم يشعر بمدح او ذم ! اس عبارت میں شارح تفتازانی لقب کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں کہ لقب وہ علم ہے جس میں مدح یا زم کا معنی پایا جائے مزید وضاحت کیلئے عرض ہے کہ علم وہ ہے جو معین چیز کیلئے وضع کیا جائے پھر اس کی تین قسمیں ہیں (۱) لقب (۲) کنیت (۳) اسم دلیل حصریہ ہے کہ علم دو حال سے خالی نہیں مفید مدح وذم ہو گا یا نہ اول لقب ہے ثانی دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا اس کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب یا ام ہوگا یا نہ اول کنیت ہے ثانی اسم ہے۔ اس وجہ مصر کے اعتبار سے کنیت میں ضروری ہوگا کہ وہ مفید مدح وزم نہ ہو ورنہ وہ لقب میں داخل ہو جائے گی اگر چہ اس کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب اورام ہو لہذا ابو جہل ابوالکلام ابوا الخیر بایں وجہ حصر لقب میں داخل ہو نگے نہ کہ کنیت میں بعض حضرات نے بطریق آخر وجہ حضر بیان کی ہے کہ علم کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب یا ابن یا ام ہوگا یا نہ اول کنیت ہے ثانی دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا دال بر مدح وذم ہوگا یا نہ اول لقب ثانی اسم ہے بناء بر میں حصر لقب کیلئے ضروری ہوگا کہ اس کی ابتداء میں لفظ اب اور ام نہ ہوا گر چہ وہ مفید مدرج ہو لہذا ابو جہل وغیرہ کنیت میں داخل ہو جائیں گے اگر چه وه مفید مدرح یا زم ہیں بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ وہ کنیت جو مفید مدح یا زم ہے من وجہ کنیت ہے اور من وجہ لقب ہے ولا باس نیه واصول الفقه علم لهذا الفن مشعر الخ ! اس عبارت میں شارح یہ بتلانا چاہتے ہیں کہ اصول الفقہ علم کی تین اقسام میں سے کون سی قسم ہے تو فرماتے ہیں کہ اصول فقہ اس فن کا لقب ہے کیونکہ لقب اس علم کو کہا جاتا ہے جو مشعر بسوئے مطرح و زم ہو اصول فقہ کا معنی مشعر الی المدح ہے کیونکہ اصول فقہ کا معنی ہے فقہ کا بنی اور بنیاد اور فقہ وہ علم ہے جس کے ذریعہ سے نظام معاش دنیوی اور نجات معاد حاصل ہوتی ہے تو علم فقہ ایک نور ہو گا اور اصول فقہ نور علی نور ہو جائے گا مبنی ہونے کی وجہ سے اصول فقہ کا علم مشعر الی المدح ہوگا اس لیے اس کو لقب کہا جائے گا۔
And the laqab is a name that conveys praise or blame. In this phrase, Sharif Taftazani is defining laqab: laqab is a name in which the meaning of praise or blame is found. For more clarification, it is said that a name (alam) is that which is placed for a specific thing; then it has three types: (1) laqab, (2) kunyah, (3) ism. A conclusive proof: a name is not free from either being indicative of praise/blame or not; the former is laqab; the latter is free from either having 'ab' or 'umm' at its beginning or not; the former is kunyah, the latter is ism. According to this reasoning, for a kunyah it is necessary that it not be indicative of praise/blame, otherwise it would enter into laqab even if it has 'ab' or 'umm' at its beginning. Therefore, Abu Jahl, Abu al-Kalam, Abu al-Khayr would enter into laqab, not kunyah. Some scholars have stated another way: if the name has 'ab', 'ibn', or 'umm' at its beginning, it is kunyah; otherwise, it is either indicative of praise/blame (laqab) or not (ism). According to this, for laqab it is necessary that it not have 'ab' or 'umm' at its beginning, even if it conveys praise/blame. So Abu Jahl etc. would enter into kunyah, even though they convey praise/blame. Some say that such a kunyah is kunyah from one aspect and laqab from another, and there is no harm. And usul al-fiqh is a name for this discipline that conveys... In this phrase, the commentator intends to show which of the three types of names usul al-fiqh belongs to. He says that usul al-fiqh is a laqab for this discipline, because laqab is called a name that conveys praise or blame. The meaning of usul al-fiqh conveys praise because it means the foundation of fiqh, and fiqh is the knowledge through which worldly livelihood and salvation in the hereafter are attained. Thus fiqh is a light, and usul al-fiqh becomes light upon light. Due to being a foundation, the knowledge of usul al-fiqh conveys praise, so it is called a laqab.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Sharif Taftazani (the hashiya author) on the definition of 'laqab' (title/epithet) and its application to 'usul al-fiqh'. The author begins by quoting Taftazani's definition: a laqab is a name (alam) that conveys praise (madḥ) or blame (dhamm). He then expands on this by explaining that an 'alam' (proper noun) is assigned to a specific object and has three types: laqab, kunyah (surname like Abu...), and ism (simple name). The commentator provides a logical division (حصر) for distinguishing them. There are two ways presented: one focusing on the meaning (praise/blame) and the other on the prefix (ab/umm). The commentator then applies this to usul al-fiqh, arguing that it is a laqab because its meaning implies praise: it is the foundation (aṣl) of fiqh, which is the science that guides worldly and otherworldly success. Hence usul al-fiqh is 'light upon light' and carries praiseworthy connotation. In Hanafi usul, this classification is important because the name of a discipline can affect how it is defined and understood. The passage also shows the inner-Hanafi debate on the classification of kunyah that conveys praise/blame, with some scholars considering it dual-aspect. The commentator maintains the definition from Taftazani, which is a refinement of the matn's position.

Key Terms
لقب (laqab): A proper noun that indicates praise or blame.
کنیت (kunyah): A proper noun starting with 'ab' or 'umm' indicating a relationship.
اسم (ism): A proper noun that is neither laqab nor kunyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it conveys praise as the foundation of fiqh
C) Because it is a simple ism
D) Because it is a kunyah

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh qualifies as a laqab because its name conveys the praiseworthy concept of being the foundation of the sacred knowledge of fiqh.

Classification of Essences: Real and Conventional
Preface on types of māhiyyah before definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real essence (māhiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah) and conventional essence (māhiyyah iʿtibāriyyah) and identify examples from Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
An essence is real if it exists independently; conventional if it depends on mental positing.

Before defining anything, we must understand what we are defining. In Hanafi usul, every definition corresponds to an essence (māhiyyah). The commentator al-Taftāzānī, in his commentary on al-Talwīḥ, introduces a crucial classification of essences into real and conventional. This distinction underpins how legal terms like 'aṣl' and 'fiqh' are constructed and used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of māhiyyah
The passage states that essence is either real (ḥaqīqī) or conventional (iʿtibārī). Real essence is independent of mental consideration; conventional depends on it.
2
Define real essence
Real essence has existence in nafs al-amr regardless of anyone positing or considering it. Examples include human, stone, sky, etc.
3
Define conventional essence
Conventional essence exists only through intellectual consideration and positing. Example: the terms 'aṣl' (root) and 'fiqh' (jurisprudence), coined by a positor.
4
Understand the scope of nafs al-amr
Nafs al-amr includes both external and mental existence, though some theologians (mutakallimūn) deny mental existence. Hanafi usul generally accepts it.
5
Apply the classification to definitions
Since a definition clarifies an essence, knowing whether the essence is real or conventional helps avoid confusion. For example, defining technical terms requires awareness of their conventional nature.

قوله واعلم ان التعريف اما حقيقى الخ الماهية اما ان يكون لها تحقق وثبوت مع قطع النظر عن اعتبار العقل اولا الاولى الخ مصنف نے تعریف کی دو قسمیں بیان کی تھیں حقیقی واعتباری شارح تفتازانی ان کی تشریح سے قبل ایک تمہید بیان کر رہے ہیں جس میں ماہیت کی اقسام بیان کر رہے ہیں کیونکہ تعریف ماهیت ہی کی ہوتی ہے تو قبل از بحث تعریف ماهیت کی تعریف اور اقسام کا جاننا ضروری ہے اس لیے فرمایا کہ ماہیت کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) ماہیت حقیقیہ (۲) ماہیت اعتبار یہ کیونکہ ہر ماہیت دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اس کا تحقق وثبوت و وجود نفس الامر میں واقع میں ہو گا قطع نظر اس کے کہ کوئی فارض اس کو فرض کرے یا عقل اس کا اعتبار کرے یعنی کسی معتبر کے اعتبار اور فرض فارض کے تابع نہ ہوگا یا پھر اس کا ثبوت و وجود کسی معتبر کے اعتبار اور فرض فارض کے تابع ہوگا اول کو ماہیت حقیقیہ کہتے ہیں تحقیقیہ کا معنی ہے الثابتہ فی نفس الامر اور ثانی کو ماہیت اعتبار یہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ ای الکائنه الخ یعنی ماہیت اعتباریہ کا مقصد ہے جو عقل کے اعتبار کرنے پر موقوف ہو جیسے واضع چند امور کا اعتبار کر کے ان کو مرکب کرے اور اس کے مقابلہ میں ایک لفظ وضع کر دے۔ ماہیت حقیقیہ کی مثال انسان، حجر، شجر، فرس بقر - ارض ، سماء ، شمس، قمر، ونجوم ، وغیرہ یہ سب نفس الامر میں موجود متحقق ہیں لیکن یہ یادر ہے کہ نفس الامر میں تقسیم ہے موجود فی الخارج اور موجود فی الذہن دونوں کو شامل ہے البتہ تکلمین حضرات وجود ذہنی کے قائل نہیں، شارح تفتازانی نے ماہیت اعتباریہ کی متعدد مثالیں بیان فرمائی ہیں (۱) اصل کہ واضع نے اس کو وضع کیا ہے ایسی چیز کیلئے جس میں اس وصف کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہو کہ اس پر کسی دوسری چیز کی بناء ہے (۲) فقہ واضع نے اس کو مسائل
His statement: 'Know that the definition is either ...' The essence (māhiyyah) is either such that it has realization and existence independent of intellectual consideration, or not. The first is such that... The author mentioned two types of definition: real (ḥaqīqī) and conventional (iʿtibārī). The commentator Taftazani, before explaining these, presents a preface in which he discusses the types of essence, because definition is of essence. So before discussing definition, it is necessary to know the types of essence. He says that essence is of two types: (1) real essence (māhiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah) and (2) conventional essence (māhiyyah iʿtibāriyyah). Every essence is either such that its realization, existence, and being in the thing-in-itself (nafs al-amr) occur independent of any positor or intellectual consideration, i.e., it is not subject to the consideration of a considerer or the positing of a positor; or its existence and being are subject to the consideration of a considerer and the positing of a positor. The first is called real essence; 'real' meaning established in the thing-in-itself. The second is called conventional essence. That is, it is something that depends on intellectual consideration, like a positor considers several matters and composes them, and then posits a word for it. Examples of real essence: human, stone, tree, horse, cow, earth, sky, sun, moon, stars, etc. All these exist and are realized in the thing-in-itself. But it should be noted that nafs al-amr includes both existent in the external and existent in the mind; however, the theologians (taklmīn) do not accept mental existence. The commentator Taftazani gave several examples of conventional essence: (1) 'aṣl' (root) that the positor has coined for a thing in which the description is considered that something else rests upon it; (2) 'fiqh' (jurisprudence) that the positor has coined for the science of rulings.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion (expansion_probe) from Sharḥ al-Talwīḥ, where the commentator prepares the ground for discussing types of definition by first classifying essences (māhiyyāt). Since definitions define essences, one must know what an essence is and its types. The text distinguishes real essence (māhiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah) which exists independently of mental consideration, e.g., natural objects like humans and stones, and conventional essence (māhiyyah iʿtibāriyyah) which depends on intellectual conception and positing, such as technical terms like 'aṣl' and 'fiqh'. The commentator notes that nafs al-amr includes both external and mental existence, but some theologians (mutakallimūn) deny mental existence. This classification is foundational in Hanafi usul for understanding how legal concepts (e.g., aṣl, farʿ, and definitions themselves) are constructed.

Key Terms
ماہیت حقیقیہ (māhiyyah ḥaqīqiyyah): An essence that has realization independent of any mental consideration or positing.
ماہیت اعتباریہ (māhiyyah iʿtibāriyyah): An essence that depends on intellectual consideration and conventional positing.
نفس الامر (nafs al-amr): The thing-in-itself, encompassing both external and mental existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A human being
B) The sky
C) The term 'fiqh' as a science of rulings
D) A stone

Key Takeaway
The distinction between real and conventional essences is fundamental in Hanafi usul for correctly understanding and constructing definitions of legal terms.

The Four Types of Definition and the Taftazani Controversy
Explains the four types of definition and the disagreement over Taftazani's classification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the four types of definition (haqiqi, ismi, lafzi, rasmi) and explain the disagreement between Taftazani and the majority regarding nominal and verbal definitions.

Core Idea
A definition is real (haqiqi) if it gives new knowledge; nominal (ismi) recalls known knowledge; verbal (lafzi) explains a word; Taftazani conflates the latter two.

This passage is a classic usul al-fiqh discussion on the taxonomy of definitions. The commentator defends the majority view that real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions are distinct, and that verbal (lafzi) definition is a separate category. He critiques Taftazani for conflating nominal and verbal definitions. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for precise istinbat (derivation) because definitions determine how shari'ah texts are understood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types
List the four types mentioned: haqiqi, ismi, lafzi, rasmi. Note that the passage focuses on the first three.
Rasmi (descriptive definition) is part of haqiqi according to the text (bound with or without all essentials).
2
Understand the wad' objection and responses
Taftazani's inclusion of wad' (positing) in real definition is questioned. The commentator gives three answers: (1) by correlation with nominal, (2) because teaching requires wad', (3) both require conceptualization by a positor.
This shows the interplay between linguistic convention and essential reality.
3
Distinguish real from nominal definition
Real definition provides a new image of the thing in the mind; nominal definition recalls an already existing image. This is the primary functional difference.
Benefit (4) highlights that real definition 'yufid taswira al-mahiyya' (benefits the depiction of the quiddity) anew.
4
Analyze Taftazani's error
Taftazani gave 'al-ghudanfar al-asad' as an example of nominal definition, but the majority consider it verbal (lafzi) because it explains a less known word by a more known one. Nominal definition defines by the meaning of the name, not by synonym.
This error leads to conflating two distinct categories; the passage asserts that nominal and verbal are separate.

(۴) یفید تصویر الماہیہ اس سے اشارہ ہے کہ تعریف حقیقی میں حصول صورة الشئي الخير الحاصلة في العقل ہوتا ہے یعنی حصول جدید فی الذہن ہوتا ہے بخلاف تعریف اسی کے اس میں حصول صورة حاصلہ فی الذہن ہوتا ہے اس تحصیلا ثانیا۔ مقصد اینکہ تعریف اسی میں صورت قوت مدرکہ میں پہلے سے موجود ہوتی ہے صرف ذہول کی وجہ سے مدرکہ سے نکل جاتی ہے ۔ تو تعریف اسمی کے ذریعہ ثانیا قوة مدرکہ میں آجاتی ہے ۔ فائدہ (۵) با الذاتيات كلها أو بعضها اس عبارت میں شارح تعریف حقیقی کے اقسام اربعہ بیان کر رہے ہیں (۱) حد نام (۲) حد ناقص (۳) رسم تام (۴) رسم ناقص ۔ فائدہ (۶) تعریف حقیقی واسی میں چند فروق ہیں (۱) حقیقی میں حصول صورۃ غیر حاصلہ فی الذہن ہوتا ہے یعنی حصول جدید اور تعریف آسمی میں حصول صورۃ حاصلہ ہوتا ہے اس فرق کو شارح نے یفید تصویر الماسیہ فی الذہن سے بیان کیا ہے (۲) تعریف حقیقی صرف ماہیات حقیقیہ کی ہوتی ہے لیکن تعریف اسمی ماہیات حقیقیہ کی بھی ہوتی ہے اور ماہیات اعتباریہ کی بھی (۳) معدومات کی تعریف اسمی ہو سکتی ہے حقیقی نہیں ہو سکتی اس فرق کو شارح نے تعریفات المعد ومات سے بیان کیا (۴) تعریف اسمی میں صرف مفہوم لغوی و معنی موضوع لہ کو بیان کیا جاتا ہے۔ تعریف حقیقی میں حقیقت مئی یا احوال شئی کو بیان کیا جاتا ہے (۵) تعریف اسمی تعریف حقیقی سے مقدم ہوتی ہے کیونکہ سب سے پہلے مفہوم لغوی کے بارے میں سوال کیا جاتا ہے پھر اس کے وجود کے بارے میں سوال کیا جاتا ہے بعدہ اس کی حقیقت و ماہیت کے بارے میں سوال کیا جاتا ہے (۱) تعریف آسی ما شارحہ اسمیہ کے جواب میں واقع ہوتی ہے اور تعریف حقیقی ما حقیقیہ کے جواب میں ذکر کی جاتی ہے۔ فائدہ ! (۷) صدر وسعد دونوں کی کلام سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تعریف کی دو قسمیں ہیں حقیقی واسمی اور تعریف اسی مقابل ہے حقیقی کے حالانکہ یہ جمہور محققین کے مذہب کے خلاف ہے بلکہ تعریف اسی قسم ہے تعریف حقیقی کی اور تعریف لفظی مقابل ہے تعریف حقیقی کے شارح تفتازانی نے تعریف اسمی اور تعریف لفظی کو خلط ملط کر دیا ہے اور دونوں کو شئی واحد قرار دیا ہے اور الغضنفر الاسد کو تعریف اسمی کی مثال قرار دیا ہے حالانکہ یہ تعریف اسمی نہیں ہے بلکہ تعریف لفظی ہے اور جمہور کے نزدیک تعریف اسمی اور لفظی دو الگ الگ قسمیں ہیں اور ایک دوسرے کا غیر ہیں
For [the definition] is wad' not necessary. Objection: if so, why did Taftazani mention wad'? This would oppose the majority's doctrine. Answer: (1) It is a teaching that for a real quiddity wad' is not necessary, but since for the nominal it is necessary, by looking at the nominal, he mentioned wad' in the real by way of correlation. (2) Since the purpose is understanding and teaching, and this purpose cannot be achieved without wad', in the real definition, even if in reality wad' is not necessary, for teaching and learning (which is the primary purpose) mentioning wad' in the real definition is necessary. (3) The truth is that for both nominal and real definitions it is necessary that they be conceptualized by a positor, and also that they be named by the name. Benefit (3): ... Benefit (4): 'It benefits the depiction of the quiddity' indicates that in real definition the acquisition of the image of the thing already in the mind occurs anew, unlike nominal definition where the image already in the mind is acquired again. Benefit (5): 'With all or some of the essentials' – in this phrase the commentator explains the four types of real definition: (1) complete definition, (2) incomplete definition, (3) complete description, (4) incomplete description. Benefit (6): There are several differences between real and nominal definition: (1)... (2)... (3)... (4)... (5)... Benefit (7): From the words of Sadr and Sa'd it is understood that there are two types of definition: real and nominal, and nominal is opposite to real, although this opposes the doctrine of the majority of investigators. Rather, nominal is a type of real definition, and verbal definition is opposite to real. Commentator Taftazani has mixed up nominal and verbal definitions, making them one thing, and gave 'al-ghudanfar' (lion) as an example of nominal definition, whereas it is not nominal but verbal. According to the majority, nominal and verbal are two separate types and are other than each other.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the classification of definitions in usul al-fiqh. The commentator is responding to potential objections about the necessity of wad' (positing/linguistic convention) for real (haqiqi) definitions. He clarifies that while wad' is not intrinsically necessary for real definitions, it is mentioned because of the correlative relation to nominal (ismi) definitions and because the primary purpose of definition is teaching and understanding, which requires wad'. The passage then enumerates several benefits (fawa'id), including the distinction between real and nominal definitions: real definitions provide new knowledge, while nominal definitions recall already present knowledge. The commentator also highlights Taftazani's error in conflating nominal definition (which defines a quiddity through its name) with verbal definition (which explains a word by a synonym), whereas the majority of scholars treat them as distinct categories. The example 'al-ghudanfar al-asad' (the lion is the lion) is a verbal definition (explaining a less known word by a more known word), not a nominal definition.

Key Terms
التعريف الحقيقي (al-ta'rif al-haqiqi): Definition that gives the real essence of a thing, using its essential attributes (jins and fasl).
التعريف الاسمي (al-ta'rif al-ismi): Definition that explains the meaning of a name by pointing to its linguistic meaning or by a synonym.
التعريف اللفظي (al-ta'rif al-lafzi): Definition that explains a word by a more well-known synonym, e.g., al-ghudanfar is al-asad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of scholars, which type of definition is exemplified by 'al-ghudanfar is al-asad'?
A) Real definition (haqiqi)
B) Nominal definition (ismi)
C) Verbal definition (lafzi)
D) Description (rasmi)

Key Takeaway
The four types of definition are distinct: real (haqiqi) gives new essence knowledge, nominal (ismi) defines the meaning of a name, verbal (lafzi) explains by synonym, and descriptive (rasmi) uses accidents; Taftazani's conflation of nominal and verbal is rejected by the majority.

Conditions of Definitions and the Hierarchy of Questions in Hanafi Usul
Sets forth conditions for definitions and sequence of inquiries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the three types of definition, apply the five conditions for a valid real definition, and sequence the four stages of inquiry about a thing.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be coextensive and exclusive; inquiry follows a logical order: name, existence, essence, attributes.

This passage introduces the three types of definition (verbal, descriptive, real) and the strict conditions that a real definition must satisfy. It then explains the logical hierarchy of questions (from name to attributes) that one poses when seeking to know a thing. Understanding these foundations is essential for precise legal reasoning in Hanafi usul, as definitions underpin the accurate identification of legal subjects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of definition
Locate the initial classification: verbal (lafzi) – synonym; descriptive (rasmi) – exclusive property; real (haqiqi) – complete essence. Note their differences.
The text gives examples: al-ghudanfar = al-asad for verbal; 'man is a laughing animal' for descriptive; 'man is a rational animal' for real.
2
List the five conditions for a real definition
Find the enumerated conditions: (1) include all essential attributes, (2) order general before specific, (3) use proximate genus if available, (4) avoid strange words, (5) avoid ambiguous/figurative terms.
These conditions ensure the definition fully and precisely captures the quiddity (mahiyya).
3
Examine the hierarchy of questions
The text describes four levels of inquiry: ma sharhi (linguistic meaning), hal basita (existence), ma haqiqiyya (essence), hal murakkaba (attributes). Each uses a specific interrogative particle.
This hierarchy is known as 'ummahat al-matalib' (mothers of demands) in logic.
4
Understand the condition of tard wa 'aks
The passage later states that both real and nominal definitions must satisfy tard (coextensiveness) and 'aks (exclusiveness). These ensure the definition covers all instances and only those instances.
The linguistic meanings of tard (prevention, generality, removal, rectitude) reinforce this requirement.
5
Connect the hierarchy to definition types
Notice that the nominal definition answers 'ma sharhi', while the real definition answers 'ma haqiqiyya'. The descriptive definition may answer 'hal murakkaba' if it mentions exclusive attributes.
Thus, the hierarchy directly corresponds to the types of definition, showing their systematic relationship.

علماء نے تعریف کی تین قسمیں بیان کی ہیں (۱) لفظی (۲) رسمی (۳) حقیقی تعریف لفظی وہ ہے ما تنم عن الشئی بلفظ الظهر واشهر عند السائل مرادف له مثاله الخضفر الاسد العقار الخمر وغيره - تعريف رسمی یہ ہے مائی عن الشئی بلازم مختص کہ جیسے الانسان حوضا حک مخصب القامة عریض الاظفار بادى البشرة الخ : تعریف حقیقی ما ينبئ عن تمام ماهیتہ الشی و حقیقتہ جیسے الانسان هو جسم نام متحرک بالارادة ناطق پھر تعریف حقیقی کے چند شرائط ہیں (۱) جمیع الذاتیات جنس و فصول کو تعریف میں ذکر کیا جائے (۲) ذاتی اعم کو اخص پر مقدم کیا جائے (۳) جنس قریب کی موجودگی میں جنس بعید کو ذکر نہ کیا جائے (۴) الفاظ وحشیہ غریبہ کو تعریف میں ذکر نہ کیا جائے (۵) الفاظ مشتر کہ و مجازیہ کے ذکر سے بھی احتراز کیا جائے۔ فائدہ ! جب کسی چیز کو طلب کیا جائے تو اس کے درجات ہیں ہر ایک کیلئے مستقل حرف وضع کیا گیا ان کو حروف طلب اور امہات المطالب کہا جاتا ہے اہل میزان کے نزدیک ان کی ترتیب کچھ اس طرح ہے، چونکہ مجہول مطلق کی طلب نہیں ہو سکتی اس لیے ضروری ہے کہ مطلوب کا تصور نوجہ ماھو اس کیلئے مطلوب کے اسم کی شرح اور اس کے مفہوم لغوی کو بیان کرنا ضروری ہے تو سب سے پہلے ما کے ذریعہ سے اسم کے مفہوم لغوی کے بارے میں سوال کیا جائے گا اس کو مالشارحہ (اسمیہ ) کہا جاتا ہے اس کے جواب میں تعریف اسمی آتی ہے پھر اس کے بعد اسی شئی کے وجود کے بارے میں سوال ہوگا کیونکہ حقیقت و ماہیت موجود کی ہوتی ہے نہ کہ معدوم کی اس کیلئے لفظ مل وضع کیا گیا ہے اس کو حل بسیطہ کہا جاتا ہے اس کے بعد اسی شئی کی حقیقت کے بارے میں لفظ ما کے ذریعہ سے سوال کیا جاتا ہے اس کو ما حقیقیہ کہا جاتا ہے اس کے جواب میں تعریف حقیقی آتی ہے بعدہ اس شئی کے احوال وصفات کے بارے میں سوال کیا جاتا ہے مسل کے ذریعہ سے اس کو ھل مرکبہ کہا جاتا ہے جیسے حل زید قائم عل زید عالموغیرہ واللہ اعلم بحقیقۃ الکلام ۔ قوله وشرط لكلا التعريفين أى الحقيقى والاسمى الطرد والعكس الخ غرض شارح تفتازانی توضیح متن و طردو عکس کی تعریف اما الطرد - سے شارح طرد کا اصطلاحی معنی بیان کر رہے ہیں لیکن قبل از میں طرد کا لغوی معنی جاننا ضروری ہے اس کے متعد داغوی معانی بیان کے گئے ہیں (1) الطرد بمعنی اسمع جیسے طردته ای منعته ورجل طرید ای مطرود رو کا ہوا دفع کیا ہوا مناسبت واضح ہے کہ تعریف مانع بھی غیر افراد معرف کیلئے مانع اور دافع بنتی ہے (۲) طرد بمعنی عام جیسے this حكم مطرد اى عام شامل للجميع تو تعریف مانع بھی عام ہوتی ہے معرف کے جميع افراد پر صادق آتی ہے فلھذ اسمی طردا (۳) طرد کا معنی ابعاد ( دور کرنا ) مناسبت ظاہر ہے کیونکہ تعریف مانع غیر افراد معرف کو دور کر دیتی ہے (۴) طرد کا معنے استقامتہ الشئی تو طرد سے بھی تعریف مستقیم ہوتی ہے اور عدم طرد سے غیر مستقیم ہوتی ہے۔ فائدہ اطر دو کس کے اصطلاحی معنی کی متعد تعبیریں ہیں (۱) یجب في التعريف الطرد والعكس (۲)
Scholars have mentioned three types of definition: (1) verbal, (2) descriptive, (3) real. Verbal definition is that which expresses the thing by a word that is more apparent and well-known to the questioner, synonymous with it; for example, al-ghudanfar is al-asad, al-'aqqar is al-khamr, etc. Descriptive definition is that which expresses the thing by an exclusive necessary property; for example, man is an animal that laughs, with upright stature, broad nails, bare skin, etc. Real definition is that which informs about the complete quiddity of the thing and its reality; for example, man is a growing body, moving by will, rational. Then real definition has several conditions: (1) All essential attributes (genus and differentiate) should be mentioned in the definition. (2) The more general essential should be placed before the more specific. (3) The distant genus should not be mentioned when the proximate genus is present. (4) Obscure and strange words should not be used in the definition. (5) Ambiguous and figurative words should also be avoided. Benefit: When something is sought, there are grades [of questions]. For each, an independent particle has been coined, called particles of seeking and mothers of demands. According to the people of logic, their order is as follows: Since the absolutely unknown cannot be sought, it is necessary to form a conception of the sought in some way. For that, it is necessary to explain the name of the sought and its linguistic meaning. So first, by the word 'ma' (what), a question will be asked about the linguistic meaning of the name; this is called 'ma sharhi' (explanatory what) [or ismi]. In response, the nominal definition comes. Then after that, a question about the existence of that same thing will be asked, because reality and quiddity belong to existing things, not to non-existent. For this, the word 'hal' (whether) is coined; this is called 'hal basita' (simple whether). Then after that, a question about the reality of that thing is asked with the word 'ma'; this is called 'ma haqiqiyya' (real what). In response, the real definition comes. Then after that, a question about the conditions and attributes of that thing is asked with the word 'hal' (whether) but in compound form; this is called 'hal murakkaba' (compound whether); for example, 'Is Zaid standing?', 'Is Zaid knowledgeable?', etc. And Allah knows best the reality of speech. His statement: 'And the condition for both definitions [real and nominal] is coextensiveness and exclusiveness (tard wa 'aks)...' The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to clarify the text and define tard wa 'aks. From 'ammā al-ṭard...' the commentator explains the technical meaning of tard. But before that, it is necessary to know the linguistic meaning of tard. Several linguistic meanings have been mentioned: (1) tard meaning 'prevention' – the definition prevents non-members of the defined from entering. (2) tard meaning 'generality' – the definition applies to all members. (3) tard meaning 'removal' – the definition removes non-members. (4) tard meaning 'rectitude' – the definition is straight. Benefit: For the technical meaning of tard and 'aks, there are various expressions: (1) It is necessary for definition that it be coextensive and exclusive.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage begins by enumerating the three types of definition recognized by scholars: verbal (lafzi) which explains a word by a synonym; descriptive (rasmi) which describes the thing by its exclusive properties without giving the full essence; and real (haqiqi) which gives the complete quiddity through genus and differentia. It then lists five conditions for a valid real definition: including all essential attributes, ordering from general to specific, using proximate genus over distant, avoiding strange or obscure terms, and avoiding ambiguous or figurative words. The text then discusses the logical hierarchy of questions about a thing: first the meaning of the name (ma sharhi/ismi) answered by nominal definition; then its existence (hal basita); then its reality (ma haqiqiyya) answered by real definition; then its attributes (hal murakkaba). This hierarchy shows the progression from unknown to known. Finally, the commentator Taftazani's discussion of the necessary conditions of tard (coextensiveness) and 'aks (exclusiveness) for any definition is introduced, with linguistic meanings of tard: prevention, generality, removal, and rectitude. The condition of tard wa 'aks ensures the definition fully and exclusively covers the defined term.

Key Terms
الطرد والعكس (al-ṭard wa al-'aks): Coextensiveness (applying to all instances) and exclusiveness (applying only to those instances) – a condition for any valid definition.
ما شارحة (ma sharhiyya): The question about the linguistic meaning of a word, answered by nominal definition.
حل بسیطہ (hal basita): The simple question about existence (whether the thing exists).
ما حقیقیہ (ma haqiqiyya): The question about the real essence of a thing, answered by a real definition.
حل مرکبہ (hal murakkaba): The compound question about attributes or states of a thing (e.g., 'Is Zaid standing?').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for a valid real definition?
A) Including all essential attributes (jins and fasl).
B) Placing the more general essential before the more specific.
C) Using the distant genus even when the proximate is available.
D) Avoiding strange and ambiguous words.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must satisfy coextensiveness (tard) and exclusiveness ('aks), and a real definition requires all essential attributes ordered from general to specific using proximate genus while avoiding obscure or ambiguous terms.

The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh: Ma'rifat al-Nafs Mā Lahā wa Mā 'Alayhā
Presenting the Hanafi definition of fiqh with an explanation of its terms and a debate on including theology and Sufism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh and explain how the addition of 'amalan affects its scope.

Core Idea
Fiqh is the soul's knowledge of what benefits and harms it—rooted in evidence, not blind imitation.

This lesson begins with the foundational definition of fiqh according to Imam Abu Hanifa, as presented in Sadr al-Shariah's Tanqīḥ al-Uṣūl. The definition—'ma'rifat al-nafs mā lahā wa mā 'alayhā'—is rich with implications regarding the scope of fiqh, the role of evidence, and the inclusion or exclusion of theology and spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the definition
Break down 'ma'rifat al-nafs mā lahā wa mā 'alayhā' into its components: ma'rifah (knowledge based on evidence), nafs (soul), mā lahā (what benefits it), mā 'alayhā (what harms it). Identify each term's legal significance.
2
Analyze the addition of 'amalan
Understand why some scholars restrict fiqh to practical matters by adding 'amalan, excluding creedal and experiential knowledge. Contrast with the unrestricted definition that includes theology and Sufism.
3
Identify the epistemological implication
Recognize that ma'rifah excludes taqlid because it requires evidence (dalīl). This distinguishes fiqh from blind imitation.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i definition
Note the narrower Shafi'i definition (knowledge of practical legal rulings) and see how the Hanafi definition is broader when unrestricted.
5
Apply the definition to categorize knowledge
Given a topic (e.g., the attributes of Allah, the stages of the spiritual path, the ruling on prayer), determine whether it falls under fiqh according to each version of the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن تنقيح مع التوضيح والفقه معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها ويزاد عملا مصنف حد اضافی بیان کر رہے تھے اس سے قبل مضاف (الاصل) کی تعریف و تشریح بیان کی اب مضاف الیہ (فقہ) کی تعریف بیان فرماتے ہیں فقہ کی تین تعریفات بیان کیں سب سے پہلی تعریف امام ابو حنیفہ سے منقول ہے اور دوسرى هو العلم بالاحكام الشرعية العملية الخ اصحاب شافعی سے منقول ہے اور تعریف ثالث خود ماتن اپنی طرف سے بیان کریں گے۔ سب سے پہلی تعریف معرفة النفس یعنی نفس کا اُن چیزوں کی معرفت حاصل کرنا جو اُس کے لئے نفع دینے والی ہیں اور نقصان دینے والی ہیں۔ پھر بعض حضرات نے اس تعریف میں عملا کی قید کا اضافہ کیا ہے تو مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ وہ مالها وما عليها عمل کے قبیلے سے ہوا اور بعض نے یہ قید نہیں لگائی۔ مصنف نے بتلا دیا کہ جن حضرات نے یہ قید لگائی ہے ان کا مقصود من هذا المقید اعتقادیات اور وجدانیات کو فقہ سے خارج کرنا ہے لہذا ان کے نزدیک علم الکلام جو اعتقادیات سے متعلق ہوتا ہے اور علم تصوف جو وجدانیات سے متعلق ہوتا ہے دونوں فقہ سے خارج ہو جائیں گے اور جو حضرات اس قید کا اضافہ نہیں کرتے ان کا مقصد ان دونوں کو فقہ میں داخل کرنا ہے تو ان کے نزدیک فقہ علوم ثلاثہ کے مجموعہ کا نام ہو گا (۱) علم کلام (۲) تصوف (۳) نقته (۴) هذا التعريف منقول مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ تعریف (معرفة النفس) امام ابو حنیفہ سے منقول ہے قا المعرفۃ سے اس تعریف کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ لفظ المعرفۃ کا معنی ہے جزئیات کو دلیل سے جان لینا لہذا اس لفظ کی قید سے تقلید خارج ہو جائے گی کیونکہ تقلید میں اگر چہ ادراک جزئیات ہوتا ہے لیکن دلیل سے
Text of Tanqīḥ with al-Tawḍīḥ: 'And fiqh is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and what is against it, and it is increased with [the word] 'amalan'. The author was explaining a relational definition; before this he explained the definition and clarification of the muḍāf (al-asl). Now he states the definition of the muḍāf ilayh (fiqh). He mentioned three definitions: the first definition is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa; the second is 'it is knowledge of the practical legal rulings' etc. transmitted from the Shafi'is; and the third definition the author himself will give. The first definition is 'ma'rifat al-nafs' i.e., the soul's acquisition of knowledge of those things that are beneficial and harmful for it. Then some scholars added the restriction 'amalan (practically). The purpose would be that those things that are for it and against it are of the category of action. And some did not add this restriction. The author explained that those who added this restriction intend by this to exclude creedal matters (i'tiqādiyāt) and experiential matters (wijdāniyāt) from fiqh. Therefore, according to them, 'ilm al-kalām (theology) which deals with creedal matters, and 'ilm al-taṣawwuf (Sufism) which deals with experiential matters, both are excluded from fiqh. And those who do not add this restriction intend to include both in fiqh; so according to them, fiqh is the name of the collection of three sciences: (1) kalām, (2) taṣawwuf, (3) [unclear]. (4) This definition is transmitted. The author says that this definition (ma'rifat al-nafs) is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. He said: from 'ma'rifah' he clarifies that the word 'ma'rifah' means knowing particulars with evidence. Therefore, by this word, taqlīd (blind following) is excluded, because in taqlīd, even though there is perception of particulars, it is not with evidence.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is the matn of Tanqīḥ al-Uṣūl by Sadr al-Sharī'ah with its commentary (al-Tawḍīḥ). It presents the definition of fiqh, focusing on the first definition attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa: 'ma'rifat al-nafs mā lahā wa mā 'alayhā' (the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it). The author notes that some scholars add the word 'amalan (practically) to this definition. The purpose of this addition is to exclude theoretical matters like theology (kalām) and Sufi experiential knowledge (tasawwuf) from the scope of fiqh, restricting fiqh to practical rulings. Without this addition, fiqh would encompass all three: theology, Sufism, and practical jurisprudence. The author then clarifies that the word 'ma'rifah' in the definition implies knowledge based on evidence (dalīl), thus excluding blind taqlīd. This emphasizes the rational and evidence-based nature of fiqh, as understood in the Hanafi tradition. The passage also mentions that there are two other definitions: one from the Shafi'i school (knowledge of practical legal rulings) and a third that the author will provide later.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): According to Imam Abu Hanifa: the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it (معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها); some add 'amalan to restrict to practical matters.
معرفۃ (ma'rifah): Knowledge of particulars based on evidence (dalīl), excluding taqlīd.
نفس (nafs): The soul or self, which is the subject of moral and legal responsibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, what does the word 'ma'rifah' in the definition of fiqh exclude?
A) Knowledge based on evidence
B) Blind imitation (taqlid)
C) Knowledge of the soul
D) Practical actions

Key Takeaway
Fiqh, in the Hanafi tradition, is defined as the soul's knowledge of what benefits and harms it, based on evidence, optionally restricted to practical matters.

The Hanafi Definition of Fiqh: Ma'rifat al-Nafs ma laha wa ma 'alayha
Explanation of the first definition of fiqh from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh, explain why it excludes taqlid, and identify the five probabilities of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'.

Core Idea
Fiqh is the soul's knowledge of its duties with evidence — taqlid is excluded.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the first definition of fiqh transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa: 'ma'rifat al-nafs ma laha wa ma 'alayha' (the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it). We will see how the word 'ma'rifa' is specified to mean knowledge with evidence, thereby excluding taqlid (blind following). The commentator also explores the possible interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha', revealing the depth of Hanafi terminological analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the first definition of fiqh attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa. Note the addition of 'amalan by some scholars.
The definition is: 'ma'rifat al-nafs ma laha wa ma 'alayha'.
2
Analyze the term 'ma'rifa'
Understand that 'ma'rifa' here means knowledge of particulars with evidence from the four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), thus excluding taqlid.
The text explicitly states that 'al-ma'rifa' is 'ma'rifat al-juz'iyyat 'an dalil'.
3
Interpret 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'
Recognize the three initial probabilities: benefit/harm (otherworldly), permissible/prohibited, permissible/obligatory.
The first probability (benefit/harm) is further divided into three sub-probabilities, making five total.
4
Break down the benefit/harm probability
See that the benefit/harm probability splits into: reward/punishment, immunity from punishment/punishment, reward/immunity from reward.
These three sub-probabilities, plus the other two initial probabilities, yield five total probabilities.
5
Apply the premise of twelve actions
Use the classification of actions into six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, haram) each with doing/leaving (12 cases). Test the first probability (reward/punishment) and see it fails to cover all cases, showing the need for a more comprehensive interpretation.
The text cuts off while testing the second probability.

متن تنقيح مع التوضيح
والفقه معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها ويزاد عملا مصنف حد اضافی بیان کر رہے تھے اس سے قبل مضاف (الاصل) کی تعریف و تشریح بیان کی اب مضاف الیہ (فقہ) کی تعریف بیان فرماتے ہیں فقہ کی تین تعریفات بیان کیں سب سے پہلی تعریف امام ابو حنیفہ سے منقول ہے اور دوسرى هو العلم بالاحكام الشرعية العملية الخ اصحاب شافعی سے منقول ہے اور تعریف ثالث خود ماتن اپنی طرف سے بیان کریں گے۔ سب سے پہلی تعریف معرفة النفس یعنی نفس کا اُن چیزوں کی معرفت حاصل کرنا جو اُس کے لئے نفع دینے والی ہیں اور نقصان دینے والی ہیں۔ پھر بعض حضرات نے اس تعریف میں عملا کی قید کا اضافہ کیا ہے تو مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ وہ مالها وما عليها عمل کے قبیلے سے ہوا اور بعض نے یہ قید نہیں لگائی۔ مصنف نے بتلا دیا کہ جن حضرات نے یہ قید لگائی ہے ان کا مقصود من هذا المقید اعتقادیات اور وجدانیات کو فقہ سے خارج کرنا ہے لہذا ان کے نزدیک علم الکلام جو اعتقادیات سے Text of al-Tanqih with al-Tawdih. And fiqh is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and what is against it, and it is added with 'amalan. The author was explaining the additive definition; before this he explained the definition of the added term (al-asl). Now he explains the definition of the added-to (fiqh). He gave three definitions: the first is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa, the second is 'knowledge of practical legal rulings etc.' transmitted from the Shafi'is, and the third definition the author himself will give from his own side. The first definition: ma'rifat al-nafs – i.e., the soul's acquisition of knowledge of those things that are beneficial and harmful to it. Then some people added the restriction 'amalan (deed), so the meaning is that what is for it and against it is of the category of action; and some did not add this restriction. The author explained that those who added this restriction intend by it to exclude theological beliefs (i'tiqadiyat) and experiential states (wijdaniyat) from fiqh. So according to them, kalam (theology) which deals with beliefs and tasawwuf (mysticism) which deals with experiential states are both excluded from fiqh. As for those who did not add this restriction, their intention is to include both in fiqh; so according to them, fiqh is the name of the collection of three sciences: (1) kalam, (2) tasawwuf, (3) fiqh. (4) This definition is transmitted. The author says: this definition (ma'rifat al-nafs) is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa. He said: al-ma'rifa means knowing particulars with evidence. Therefore, by this word, taqlid (blind following) is excluded, because in taqlid, even though there is perception of particulars, it is not with evidence, because by evidence is meant one of the four proofs, and the muqallid does not have any of the four proofs; rather his proof is the statement of a mujtahid. Hence his knowledge of particulars is not from evidence, so taqlidi knowledge is excluded from the terminological definition of fiqh. And his statement 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' – the author is explaining 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha'. First, there are three probabilities: (1) 'Laha' means benefit and 'alayha' means harm, on the basis that 'lam' is for benefit and 'ala' is for harm, as in the Almighty's saying: 'Laha ma kasabat wa 'alayha ma iktasabat' where 'lam' is for benefit and 'ala' is for harm. Then the author clarified that benefit and harm here mean otherworldly benefit and harm, not worldly, because fiqh is among the religious sciences and in religious sciences benefit and harm are otherworldly. (2) 'Ma laha' means what is permissible for it, and 'ma 'alayha' means what is prohibited for it. (3) 'Ma laha' means what is permissible for it, and 'ma 'alayha' means what is obligatory on it. Then the first probability has three forms regarding what is meant by benefit and harm: (1) benefit means reward and harm means punishment, (2) benefit means immunity from punishment and harm means punishment, (3) benefit means reward and harm means immunity from reward. Initially there were three probabilities, at the end they became five. The author discussed all five probabilities in detail. 'Fa'lam anna ma ya'ti bihi al-mukallaf' – he presented a premise: the action that the mukallaf performs is in one of six states: (1) wajib, (2) mandub, (3) mubah, (4) makruh tahrimi, (5) makruh tanzihi, (6) haram. Then each of these has two aspects: (1) the aspect of doing, (2) the aspect of leaving (i.e., not doing). So there are twelve images: (1) doing wajib, (2) doing mandub, (3) doing mubah, (4) doing haram, (5) doing makruh tahrimi, (6) doing makruh tanzihi, (7) leaving wajib, (8) leaving mandub, (9) leaving mubah, (10) leaving makruh tahrimi, (11) leaving makruh tanzihi, (12) leaving haram. Among the twelve, six are of doing and six of leaving. After this premise, see the detail of the five probabilities of 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha': (1) The first of the five probabilities: 'ma laha' means reward and 'ma 'alayha' means punishment. In this case, doing wajib and doing mandub are included under 'yuthabu 'alayha', and doing haram, doing makruh tahrimi, and leaving wajib are included under 'yu'aqabu 'alayha'. Apart from these, the remaining seven categories – (1) doing mubah, (2) doing makruh tanzihi, (3) leaving mandub, (4) leaving mubah, (5) leaving makruh tanzihi, (6) leaving makruh tahrimi, (7) leaving haram – are neither included under 'yuthabu 'alayha' nor under 'yu'aqabu 'alayha', because in all these cases there is neither reward nor punishment. So the first probability would not encompass all categories. (2) The second probability: 'ma laha' means immunity from punishment and 'ma 'alayha' means punishment. In this case, (1) doing haram, (2) doing makruh tahrimi, (3) leaving wajib are included under 'yu'aqabu 'alayhi'. Apart from these, the remaining nine categories are included under 'la yu'aqabu 'alayhi'. They are: (1) doing wajib, (2) doing mandub, (3) doing mubah, (4) doing makruh tanzihi, (5) leaving haram, etc. (The text cuts off).
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of fiqh as given in al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih. The author explains three definitions of fiqh: first from Imam Abu Hanifa: 'ma'rifat al-nafs ma laha wa ma 'alayha' (the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it). Some add 'amalan (practically) to emphasize that it concerns actions, and to exclude creedal and mystical sciences. The word 'ma'rifa' means knowing particulars with evidence, thus excluding taqlid (blind following) because the muqallid knows particulars but not via the standard four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas); his evidence is a mujtahid's opinion. Then the author analyzes 'ma laha wa ma 'alayha' with three initial probabilities: (1) benefit/harm (otherworldly), (2) permissible/prohibited, (3) permissible/obligatory. The first probability (benefit/harm) further splits into three sub-probabilities: reward/punishment, immunity from punishment/punishment, reward/immunity from reward. This yields five total probabilities. The author then presents a premise: the mukallaf's actions fall into six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, haram), each with two aspects (doing/leaving), giving twelve cases. He then tests the first probability (reward/punishment) against these twelve cases and finds it fails to cover all (e.g., doing mubah gives no reward or punishment), so it is not comprehensive. The second probability (immunity from punishment/punishment) is then examined, and the text cuts off while enumerating which cases fall under punishment and which under immunity. Overall, the passage shows the rigorous terminological analysis of the Hanafi definition of fiqh.

Key Terms
معرفة النفس (ma'rifat al-nafs): The soul's knowing of particulars with evidence; used in the definition of fiqh to exclude taqlid.
مالها وما عليها (ma laha wa ma 'alayha): What is beneficial/harmful or permissible/prohibited/obligatory for the soul, with multiple interpretations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the definition of fiqh as 'ma'rifat al-nafs ma laha wa ma 'alayha' exclude taqlid?
A) Because taqlid involves knowledge of particulars without evidence from the four proofs.
B) Because taqlid is forbidden in Hanafi fiqh.
C) Because taqlid only concerns doctrinal matters, not practical ones.
D) Because the muqallid does not know the particulars at all.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in the Hanafi tradition is the soul's evidence-based knowledge of its duties, not just any knowledge of rulings.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
8 min
Analyzing the Five Probabilities of 'Ma Laha wa Ma Alayha' in the Hanafi Definition of Fiqh
Commentary on five interpretations of the definition's core phrase and their evaluation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five probabilities for 'ma laha wa ma alayha', apply the criterion of comprehensiveness (jami' jami' al-aqsam) to evaluate them, and distinguish which interpretations define fiqh in the technical sense.

Core Idea
The phrase 'what is for and against the mukallaf' must cover all twelve categories of actions; only three of five interpretations achieve this.

The classical Hanafi definition of fiqh—'knowledge of practical legal rulings from detailed evidence'—hinges on the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha'. This passage unpacks the multiple meanings of that phrase, testing each against the full taxonomy of actions. We will learn why the muqallid is excluded and why only certain interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' can serve as the core of the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitional framework
Recognize that fiqh is defined as 'knowledge of the practical legal rulings from detailed evidence' and that the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is its core. Note that the muqallid is excluded because his knowledge lacks proof from detailed evidence.
The muqallid has only the mujtahid's statement, not the four proofs.
2
Enumerate the twelve action categories
List the six types of rulings (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, haram), each with its act and abandonment, giving 12 forms. This classification is the basis for evaluating comprehensiveness.
The twelve categories: performing wajib, abandoning wajib, etc.
3
Map the five probabilities to the twelve categories
For each probability (reward/punishment, absence of punishment/punishment, reward/absence of reward, permissible/obligatory, permissible/prohibited), assign which categories fall under 'laha' and which under 'alayha' as per the author's analysis.
Use the author's detailed mapping in the passage.
4
Apply the comprehensiveness criterion
Check which probabilities assign a value to all twelve categories. Note that the first probability (reward/punishment) fails to cover seven categories (e.g., mubah acts), and the fourth (permissible/obligatory) fails to cover acts that are neither permissible nor obligatory (e.g., haram acts).
Comprehensiveness means every category falls into either 'laha' or 'alayha'.
5
Determine the most appropriate interpretations
Identify that the second (absence of punishment/punishment), third (reward/absence of reward), and fifth (permissibility/prohibition) probabilities are comprehensive. Also note the distinction between fiqh in the technical sense (restricted to actions) and the broader sense (including beliefs and ethics).
The author favors these three because they cover all twelve categories 'without an intermediary'.

اور باقی دس اقسام چارفصل کی اور چھ ترک کی لا یناب میں داخل ہونگی یہ احتمال بھی جامع مجمع الاقسام ہوگا یہ تین احتمال اس صورت میں تھے کہ مالھیں لام برائے نفع ہو اور علیها میں علی برائے ضرر ہو، چوتھا احتمال یہ تھا کہ مالها سے ما يجوز لها اور عليها ما يجب عليها مراد ہو اس احتمال کے مطابق فعل حرام اور فعل مکروہ تحریمی کے ماسوای جو فعل کی چار قسمیں ہیں ( فعل مندوب فعل مباح فعل واجب فعل مکروہ تنزیہی ) اور ترک واجب کے علاوہ جو ترک کی پانچ اقسام ہیں ( ترک مندوب ، ترک ،مباح، ترک حرام ، ترک مکروہ تحریمی ، اور ترک مکروہ تنزیہی ) یہ سب بیجوز لھا میں داخل ہوں گی اور فعل واجب، ترک حرام، ترک مکروہ تحریمی ، يجب عليها میں داخل ہونگی اور فعل حرام فعل مکروہ تحریمی اور ترک واجب نہ یجوز لھا میں داخل اور نہ يجب عليها میں داخل ہوں گی کیونکہ یہ نہ تو جائز ہیں اور نہ واجب یہ احتمال بھی جامع مجمع الاقسام نہیں ہوگا۔ پانچواں احتمال ، یہ تھا کہ ما لها ما يجوز لها اور ما علیھا سے یحرم عليها مراد ہو اس صورت میں (۱) فعل حرام (۲) مکروہ تحریمی (۳) اور ترک واجب یہ تینوں بس حرم علیها میں داخل ہوں گے اس کے علاوہ فعل واجب فعل مندوب فعل مبا شغل مکروہ تنز ہی ترک مندوب ترک مباح ترک حرام ترک مکروہ تحریمی ترک مکروہ تنزیہی یہ سب یجوز لها میں داخل ہوں گی یہ احتمال بھی جامع بجميع الاقسام ہے اذا عرفت هذا احتمالات خمسہ کو تفصیلا ذکر کرنے کے بعد مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ان پانچ احتمالات میں سے وہ احتمال زیادہ اولی ہے جن میں واسط نہیں ہے یعنی جو شامل جامع جميع الاقسام (۱۲) ہی وہ تین احتمال ہیں (۱) دوسرا احتمال (مالها وما عليها سے عقاب و عدم عقاب مراد ہو ) (۲) تیسرا احتمال (مالها وما عليها سے ثواب و عدم ثواب مراد ہو ) (۳) آخری احتمال مالها وما علیها سے جواز وحرمت مراد ہو یہ تین احتمالات چونکہ جامع مجمع الاقسام ہیں لہذا مالها وما عليها وان پرمحمول کرنازیادہ اولی ہے ثم مالها وما عليها مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ مالها وما عليها عام ہے یہ اعتقادیات کو بھی شامل ہے جیسے وجوب ایمان وغیرہ اور وجدانیات کو بھی شامل ہے جیسے اخلاق باطنہ اور ملکات نفسانیہ جیسے تصوف، زہد، صبر، رضا، حضور قلب في الصلوۃ وغیرہ اور عبادات و عملیات کو بھی شامل ہے کیا لصلوة ، والصوم والبيع ، ونحوها اگر مالها وما عليها اعتقادیات کے باب سے ہوں تو اس کو علم الکلام کہتے ہیں اگر من قبیل الوجدانیات والاخلاق ہو تو اس کو علم الاخلاق و علم التصوف کہتے ہیں اگر من باب العملیات ہو تو اس کو علم الفقہ کہتے ہیں تو ما لها وما عليها تینوں علوم کو شامل ہے اگر مالها وما عليها سے فقط فقہ اصطلاحی کی تعریف کرنا مقصود ہو تو اسمیں عملا کی قید کا اضافہ کرنا ضروری ہوگا تا کہ اعتقادیات اور وجدانیات خارج ہو جائیں اور اگر مسالھا اور وما عليها سے مطلق فقہ کی تعریف کرنا مقصود ہو جو ان تینوں ( عملیات اعتقادیات وجدانیات) کو شامل ہو تو پھر عمل کی قید نہ لگائی جائے گی چنانچہ امام ابو
It does not happen because by 'dahl' is meant one of the four proofs, and the muqallid does not have any of the four proofs; rather his proof is the statement of a mujtahid. Therefore his knowledge of particulars is not from proof, so taqlidi knowledge is excluded from the terminological definition of fiqh. And His statement 'ma laha wa ma alayha' etc.—the author is explaining 'ma laha wa ma alayha'. Initially, there are three probabilities: (1) By 'laha' is meant benefit, and by 'alayha' is meant harm, on the basis that 'lam' is for benefit and 'ala' is for harm, as in the verse of Allah: 'laha ma kasabat wa alayha ma iktasabat'—'lam' is for benefit and 'ala' is for harm. Then the author clarified that the intended benefit and harm are otherworldly benefit and harm, not worldly, because fiqh is among the religious sciences, and in religious sciences, otherworldly benefit and harm are discussed. (2) 'Ma laha' means what is permissible for it, and 'ma alayha' means what is prohibited for it. (3) 'Ma laha' means what is permissible for it, and 'ma alayha' means what is obligatory for it. Then the first probability has three forms regarding what is meant by benefit and harm: (1) By benefit is meant reward, and by harm is meant punishment. (2) By benefit is meant absence of punishment, and by harm is meant punishment. (3) By benefit is meant reward, and by harm is meant absence of reward. Initially there were three probabilities, at the end they became five. The author discussed all five probabilities in detail. 'Fa'lam anna ma ya'ti bihi al-mukallaf'—he introduced a preface that the action performed by the mukallaf occurs in one of six states: (1) wajib, (2) mandub, (3) mubah, (4) makruh tahrimi, (5) makruh tanzihi, (6) haram. Then each of these has two aspects: (1) the aspect of performing, (2) the aspect of abandoning (i.e., non-performance). So there are twelve forms: (1) performing wajib, (2) performing mandub, (3) performing mubah, (4) performing haram, (5) performing makruh tahrimi, (6) performing makruh tanzihi, (7) abandoning wajib, (8) abandoning mandub, (9) abandoning mubah, (10) abandoning makruh tahrimi, (11) abandoning makruh tanzihi, (12) abandoning haram; six are performing and six are abandoning. After this preface, see the detail of the five probabilities of 'ma laha wa ma alayha': (1) The first of the five probabilities: By 'ma laha' is meant reward, and by 'ma alayha' is meant punishment. In that case, performing wajib and performing mandub are included in 'yuthabu alayha', and performing haram, performing makruh tahrimi, and abandoning wajib are included in 'yu'aqabu alayha'. Apart from these, seven categories: (1) performing mubah, (2) performing makruh tanzihi, (3) abandoning mandub, (4) abandoning mubah, (5) abandoning makruh tanzihi, (6) abandoning makruh tahrimi, (7) abandoning haram—are neither included in 'yuthabu alayha' nor in 'yu'aqabu alayha', because in all these forms there is neither reward nor punishment. So the first probability is not comprehensive of all categories. (2) The second probability: By 'ma laha' is meant absence of punishment, and by 'ma alayha' is meant punishment. In that case, (1) performing haram, (2) performing makruh tahrimi, (3) abandoning wajib are included in 'yu'aqabu alayhi'. Apart from these, the remaining nine forms are included in 'la yu'aqabu alayhi': they are (1) performing wajib, (2) performing mandub, (3) performing mubah, (4) performing makruh tanzihi, (5) abandoning mandub, (6) abandoning mubah, (7) abandoning makruh tanzihi, (8) abandoning haram, (9) abandoning makruh tahrimi. This probability is comprehensive of all categories. (3) The third probability: By 'ma laha' is meant reward, and by 'ma alayha' is meant absence of reward. In this case, performing wajib and performing mandub are included in 'yuthabu alayhi', and the remaining ten categories—four of performing and six of abandoning—are included in 'la yuthab'. This probability is also comprehensive of all categories. These three probabilities were in the case where 'lam' is for benefit and 'ala' is for harm. (4) The fourth probability: By 'ma laha' is meant what is permissible for it, and by 'ma alayha' is meant what is obligatory for it. According to this probability, except for performing haram and performing makruh tahrimi, the four categories of performing (performing mandub, performing mubah, performing wajib, performing makruh tanzihi) and except for abandoning wajib, the five categories of abandoning (abandoning mandub, abandoning mubah, abandoning haram, abandoning makruh tahrimi, and abandoning makruh tanzihi)—all these are included in 'yajuzu laha'; and performing wajib, abandoning haram, and abandoning makruh tahrimi are included in 'yajibu alayhi'; and performing haram, performing makruh tahrimi, and abandoning wajib are neither included in 'yajuzu laha' nor in 'yajibu alayhi', because they are neither permissible nor obligatory. This probability is also not comprehensive of all categories. (5) The fifth probability: By 'ma laha' is meant what is permissible for it, and by 'ma alayha' is meant what is prohibited for it. In this case, (1) performing haram, (2) performing makruh tahrimi, (3) and abandoning wajib—these three are included in 'yahrumu alayhi'; apart from these, performing wajib, performing mandub, performing mubah, performing makruh tanzihi, abandoning mandub, abandoning mubah, abandoning haram, abandoning makruh tahrimi, abandoning makruh tanzihi—all these are included in 'yajuzu laha'. This probability is also comprehensive of all categories. 'Idha 'arafta hadha'—after mentioning the five probabilities in detail, the author says: Among these five probabilities, the probability that is more appropriate is the one that is without an intermediary, i.e., those that are comprehensive of all twelve categories. They are three probabilities: (1) the second probability (by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is meant punishment and absence of punishment), (2) the third probability (by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is meant reward and absence of reward), (3) the last probability (by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is meant permissibility and prohibition). Since these three probabilities are comprehensive of all categories, therefore applying 'ma laha wa ma alayha' to them is more appropriate. Then 'ma laha wa ma alayha'—the author says: The word 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is general; it includes beliefs, such as the obligation of faith etc., and also spiritual states, such as inner ethics and psychical dispositions like tasawwuf, asceticism, patience, contentment, presence of heart in prayer etc., and also acts of worship and transactions, like prayer, fasting, sale, etc. If 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is from the category of beliefs, then it is called 'ilm al-kalam; if from the category of spiritual states and ethics, then it is called 'ilm al-akhlaq and 'ilm al-tasawwuf; if from the category of actions, then it is called 'ilm al-fiqh. So 'ma laha wa ma alayha' includes three sciences. If by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' only the terminological definition of fiqh is intended, then it is necessary to add the restriction of 'actions' so that beliefs and spiritual states are excluded; and if by 'ma laha wa ma alayha' the absolute definition of fiqh is intended, which includes all three (actions, beliefs, spiritual states), then the restriction of 'action' should not be added. Thus Imam Abu...
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the phrase 'ما لها وما عليها' ('what is for it and what is against it') from the classical definition of fiqh. The author begins by justifying why taqlidi knowledge is excluded from the technical definition of fiqh: a muqallid does not derive rulings from the four sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) but from the saying of a mujtahid, so his knowledge is not 'from proof'. Then the author focuses on the phrase 'ما لها وما عليها' and presents three initial probabilities for its meaning: (1) benefit and harm (specifically otherworldly), (2) permissible and prohibited, (3) permissible and obligatory. The first probability (benefit/harm) is then subdivided into three specific interpretations: reward/punishment, absence of punishment/punishment, reward/absence of reward. Thus the three probabilities become five. To analyze which probability is comprehensive, the author first enumerates the twelve categories of actions according to the Hanafi classification: six types of rulings (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tahrimi, makruh tanzihi, haram) each with its performance and abandonment. The author then examines each of the five probabilities against these twelve categories. The first probability (reward/punishment) fails to cover seven categories (e.g., performing mubah, abandoning mandub) that have neither reward nor punishment. The fourth probability (permissible/obligatory) fails because some acts are neither permissible nor obligatory (e.g., performing haram is not permissible; abandoning wajib is not obligatory). However, the second (absence of punishment/punishment), third (reward/absence of reward), and fifth (permissibility/prohibition) probabilities are comprehensive: they assign a value to each of the twelve categories. The author then states that these three probabilities are more appropriate for interpreting the phrase. Finally, the author discusses the scope of 'ما لها وما عليها', noting that it can refer to beliefs (kalam), spiritual ethics (tasawwuf), or actions (fiqh). To define fiqh in the technical sense, one must restrict it to actions by adding 'عملیات'; otherwise, the absolute definition includes all three sciences.

Key Terms
ما لها وما عليها (ma laha wa ma alayha): The phrase in the definition of fiqh meaning 'what is for the mukallaf and what is against him' — interpreted variously as benefit/harm, reward/punishment, permissibility/prohibition, etc.
مقلد (muqallid): One who follows the ruling of a mujtahid without knowledge of the proof
احتمالات خمسة (ihtimalat khamsa): The five interpretive probabilities for the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha'
جامع جميع الاقسام (jami' jami' al-aqsam): Comprehensive of all twelve categories of actions (six types with act and abandonment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many of the five probabilities for 'ما لها وما عليها' are comprehensive of all twelve categories of actions?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh requires that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' be interpreted comprehensively, covering all twelve action categories; three interpretations achieve this.

Why Abu Hanifa Did Not Require Action in Fiqh
Explains why Abu Hanifa omitted 'amalan from the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa did not add the condition of action ('amalan) to the definition of fiqh and identify the inclusive scope of fiqh in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Fiqh includes both belief and action; theology is 'al-fiqh al-akbar'.

This passage illuminates a distinctive feature of the Hanafi definition of fiqh. While many scholars restrict fiqh to practical rulings requiring action, Imam Abu Hanifa took a broader view, including theological knowledge (kalam) within fiqh. He even called theology 'al-fiqh al-akbar' (the greater fiqh), showing that fiqh is not limited to practical law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the omission
What condition did Abu Hanifa deliberately omit from the definition of fiqh? The passage states he did not add 'amalan (action).
'Amalan refers to physical actions required by rulings.
2
Understand the reason
Why did he omit it? Because according to him, fiqh includes three things (likely: usul, furu, kalam). The passage mentions he included kalam (theology).
The text says 'he included all three in fiqh'.
3
Analyze the evidence
What proof does the author give? Abu Hanifa named kalam 'al-fiqh al-akbar', indicating that theology is part of fiqh.
This naming is a key indicator of the inclusive definition.
4
Apply the insight
Conclude that fiqh in the Hanafi school covers both theoretical knowledge (beliefs) and practical actions.
This contrasts with schools that define fiqh only as knowledge of practical rulings.

Source Text

besturdubooks.wo مسک الملیح شرح التوضيح والتلويح حنیفہ نے عملاً کی قید کا اضافہ نہیں کیا کیونکہ انہوں نے فقہ میں ان تینوں کو داخل کیا یہی وجہ ہے کہ امام صاحب علم الکلام کا نام الفقه الاکبر رکھتے ہیں اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فلم کلام ان کے نزدیک فقہ میں داخل ہے۔
He did not add the condition of action because he included all three in fiqh. This is why Imam (Abu Hanifa) named Kalam 'al-fiqh al-akbar'. From this it is known that Kalam is included in fiqh according to him.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage explains why Abu Hanifa did not add the condition of 'amalan (action) in the definition of fiqh. According to him, fiqh includes theology (kalam), which is theoretical. Hence, the condition of action is unnecessary. He even called theology 'al-fiqh al-akbar' (the greater fiqh).

Key Terms
الفقه الأكبر (al-fiqh al-akbar): The name Abu Hanifa gave to theology (kalam), meaning the greater fiqh.
عملاً (amalan): Action; the condition that other schools include in the definition of fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Abu Hanifa not require 'amalan (action) in the definition of fiqh?
A) He considered action irrelevant.
B) He included theology (kalam) in fiqh.
C) He followed the Shafi'i school.
D) He defined fiqh as pure knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's definition of fiqh includes theology (al-fiqh al-akbar), so action is not a necessary condition; fiqh encompasses both belief and practice.

Two Definitions of Fiqh and a Third Added
Discussion of definitions of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two transmitted definitions of fiqh (from Imam Abu Hanifa and the Shafi'i school) and state the third definition added by Sadr al-Shariah, identifying which are accepted and why.

Core Idea
Fiqh has two transmitted definitions; one accepted (Hanafi) and one weak (Shafi'i), plus a third from Sadr al-Shariah.

This passage from the Sharh al-Talwih examines the definitions of fiqh as transmitted from earlier authorities. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) presents two definitions of the 'mudaf' (the term being defined) and two of 'fiqh' itself. One definition of fiqh, attributed to the Shafi'i school, is explicitly marked as weak. A third definition is then offered by the author. Understanding these definitions is fundamental to grasping the Hanafi usul perspective.

Guided Path
1
Understand the mudaf/mudaf ilayhi structure
Recognize that in definitions, 'mudaf' is the term being defined (e.g., 'fiqh'), and 'mudaf ilayhi' is the definition attached to it. The passage discusses definitions for both.
This structure is common in usul texts.
2
Identify the two transmitted definitions of fiqh
One definition is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa (the first, left uncommented). The other is attributed to the Shafi'i school and explicitly marked as weak (muzayyaf) and unacceptable.
The exact wording of these definitions is not given in this snippet.
3
Analyze the author's stance
The author remains silent on the Hanafi definition, implying acceptance. He explicitly rejects the Shafi'i definition as weak.
Silence in such contexts often indicates endorsement.
4
Locate the third definition
After presenting the two transmitted definitions, the author (Sadr al-Shariah) adds a third definition from himself.
This third definition is the one considered authoritative in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح تلویح قوله نقل للمضاف تعريفين مقبولا ومزيفا الخ غرض شارح بیان فائدہ! مصنف نے مضاف (اصل) کی دو تعریفیں ذکر کیں (۱) مقبول (۲) غیر مقبول و مزیف اس طرح مضاف الیہ (فقہ) کی بھی دو تعریفیں ذکر کیں ان میں سے ایک کے ضعف اور غیر مقبول ہونے کی تصریح کردی ہے وہ تعریف وہ ہے جو اصحاب شافعی کی طرف منسوب ہے اور پہلی تعریف بنو امام صاحب سے منقول ہے اس کے بارے میں سکوت اختیار کیا ہے پھر اپنی طرف سے تیسری تعریف بیان کی۔
Commentary on Talwih: His saying: He transmitted for the addendum two definitions, acceptable and spurious. The purpose of the commentator is to explain the benefit. The author mentioned two definitions for the original (mudaf): (1) acceptable, (2) unacceptable and spurious. Similarly, he mentioned two definitions for the addendum (fiqh), clarifying the weakness and unacceptability of one, which is attributed to the Shafi'i school. The first definition is transmitted from Imam (Abu Hanifa) and he remained silent about it. Then he expressed a third definition from himself.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage explains the structure of Al-Tawdih's definitions. The author (Sadr al-Shariah) provides two definitions of 'asl' (the term being defined) and two of 'fiqh' (the definition). One definition of fiqh, attributed to the Shafi'i school, is deemed weak and rejected. The other, from Imam Abu Hanifa, is left uncommented. The author then adds his own third definition.

Key Terms
مضاف (mudaf): The term being defined (asl) in the definition
مضاف الیہ (mudaf ilayhi): The definition (fiqh) that is attached to the defined term

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
There are two transmitted definitions of fiqh in this passage, one accepted (Hanafi) and one rejected (Shafi'i), with a third added by the author.

Two Interpretations of 'Nafs' in the Definition of Fiqh
Explains two probabilities for 'nafs' in the first definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of 'nafs' in the classical definition of fiqh and explain why each interpretation matters for the scope of fiqh.

Core Idea
‘Nafs’ can mean the entire human (body+spirit) or just the soul — each affects legal capacity.

The classical definition of fiqh begins with 'ma'rifat al-nafs' (knowledge of the self). But what exactly does 'nafs' refer to in this context? The commentator al-Taftazani clarifies that there are two valid probabilities: the whole human being (body and spirit) or the spirit alone. This distinction influences how we understand the subject of fiqh and the nature of legal address (khitab).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the term 'nafs' in the definition
In the definition 'al-fiqh ma'rifat al-nafs ma laha wa ma alayha', identify the word 'nafs' as the core subject of fiqh.
2
Understand the first interpretation
Taftazani's first probability: 'nafs' means the whole human, body with spirit (jasad ma'a al-ruh), because most rulings concern bodily actions, which require the spirit.
This interpretation emphasizes the physical aspect of acts.
3
Understand the second interpretation
Second probability: 'nafs' means only the spirit/soul (al-ruh), because it is the locus of perception, consciousness, and accountability; the body is merely a tool.
This interpretation emphasizes the spiritual and intellectual aspect.
4
Consider the implications for legal capacity
If 'nafs' is the whole human, then fiqh addresses both physical and spiritual dimensions. If only the spirit, then fiqh primarily concerns the inner capacity for obligation (ahliyyah al-wujub) and performance (ahliyyah al-ada).
Both interpretations are valid and complementary in Hanafi usul.

فالاول معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها . ويجوز ان يريد بالنفس غرض شارح تفتازانی ! تعریف اول کے بعض الفاظ کی توضیح و تشریح چنانچہ لفظ انفس کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ اس میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) اس سے مراد ذات عبد ہو یعنی جسد مع الروح تو معرفة النفس بمعنی معرفۃ العبد ہوگا کیونکہ اکثر احکام اعمال جسدی و بدنی سے متعلق ہوتے ہیں اور اعمال جسد بغیر روح حاصل نہیں ہو سکتے لہذا النفس سے جسد مع الروح دونوں کا مجموعہ مراد ہو گا (۲) احتمال دوم یہ ہے کہ نفس سے فقط روح اور نفس انسانی مراد ہو کیونکہ اسی کی وجہ سے اعمال وجود میں آتے ہیں اور خطاب اس کو ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ادراک و شعور و صلاحیت علم و فہم اس روح میں ہے بدن صرف آلہ ہے جس کے واسطہ سے انسان سے اعمال کا صدور ہوتا ہے۔
So the first is knowledge of the self (nafs) and what is for it and against it. And it is permissible that by 'nafs' the commentator Taftazani means to clarify some words of the first definition. Thus, explaining the word 'anfus' he said that there are two probabilities: (1) It means the essence of the servant, i.e., body with spirit, so knowledge of the self means knowledge of the servant, because most rulings are related to bodily actions, and bodily actions cannot occur without spirit. So by 'nafs' the combination of body and spirit is meant. (2) The second probability is that by 'nafs' only the spirit and human soul is meant, because actions come into existence due to it and address is directed to it, since perception, consciousness, and capacity for knowledge and understanding are in the spirit. The body is merely a tool through which actions emanate from the human.

Two interpretations are given: first, 'nafs' means the entire human (body and spirit), since most rulings pertain to physical actions; second, 'nafs' means only the spirit/soul, because it is the locus of accountability and understanding, while the body is just an instrument.
