Defending the Condition 'an Dalil' in the Definition of Ma'rifah
Objection and response regarding the qayd 'an dalil' in Taftazani's definition of ma'rifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the objection to the qayd 'an dalil' in the definition of ma'rifah and apply the Hanafi usul response.

Core Idea
The condition 'an dalil' is essential to ma'rifah because knowledge in usul is necessarily deduced.

In this passage, we examine Taftazani's critique of including 'an dalil' (from a proof) in the definition of ma'rifah (knowledge). He claims it has no basis in language or terminology. However, the Hanafi tradition provides three robust responses rooted in linguistic usage, terminological convention, and practical necessity. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to recognize how definitions in usul al-fiqh are constructed and defended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Locate Taftazani's claim: the qayd 'an dalil' is arbitrary because it is not found in linguistic or terminological definitions of ma'rifah.
2
Analyze the First Response
Examine the linguistic proof: Imam Raghib al-Isfahani's definition of ma'rifah as perception by reflection and deliberation implies deduction from evidence.
3
Analyze the Second Response
Consider the terminological argument: fiqh is defined as knowledge of rulings from proofs, and a mujtahid is called faqih because he engages in istidlal.
4
Analyze the Third Response
Understand the practical necessity: since it is impossible to know all rulings in detail, the definition must include istinbat to make it feasible.
5
Evaluate the Overall Defense
Synthesize the three responses and assess how they collectively refute Taftazani's objection, reinforcing the Hanafi method of defining usul terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وفسر المعرفة . والقيد الخير ممالا دلالة له الخ غرض شارح تفتازانی اعتراض علی المصنف ا تقریر اشکال یہ ہے کہ مائن نے معرفہ کی تعریف کی ہے ادراک الجزئیات عن دلیل اس میں جو آخری قید عن دلیل ذکر کی ہے یہ اپنی طرف سے ذکر کی ہے اس کا ثبوت نہ لغت میں ہے نہ اصطلاح میں اس پر کوئی دلیل موجود نہیں۔ جواب: اس اشکال کے متعدد جوابات دیے گئے ہیں (۱) یہ قید لخت ثابت ہے کیونکہ امام اللغة امام راغب اصفہانی نے معرفہ کی تعریف یوں کی ہے المعرفة والعرفان ادراک شنى بتفكر و تدبر لاثره بتفكر و تدبر سے استدلال اور ادراک عن دلیل ہی مراد ہے فلہذا یہ کہنا کہ یہ قید ثابت نہیں ہے غلط ہے (۲) فقہ علوم استدلالیہ میں سے ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ فقیہ مجتہد کو کہا جاتا ہے مقلد کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جاتا تو اصطلاح میں بھی فقہ معرفۃ الاحکام عن دلیل کا نام ہے تو ولا اصطلاحا کہنا بھی غلط ہے (۳) مالها وما عليها سے مراد جمع احکام علی سبیل الاستغراق ہیں اور معرفہ جمیع احکام بالتفصیل بالفعل محال ہے لہذا ضروری ہے اس کے اندر استنباط واستدلال کی قید لگائی جائے۔
His saying: And he interpreted knowledge (ma'rifah). And the last restriction is that which has no indication etc. The purpose of commentator Taftazani is an objection against the author. The explanation of the difficulty is that the author defined knowledge as perception of particulars from a proof. The last restriction 'from a proof' he mentioned from himself. It is proven neither in language nor in terminology; there is no proof for it. Answer: Several answers are given: (1) This restriction is firmly established because the linguist Imam Raghib al-Isfahani defined knowledge as perception of a thing by reflection and deliberation, which implies deduction and perception from a proof. Hence saying it is not proven is wrong. (2) Fiqh is among the deductive sciences, so a mujtahid is called a faqih, not a muqallid. So terminologically, fiqh is knowledge of rulings from proofs. Thus saying it is not terminologically proven is also wrong. (3) 'What is for it and against it' means all rulings comprehensively, and knowledge of all rulings in detail is impossible in actuality, so it is necessary to include the condition of deduction and inference.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
Taftazani objects to the author's inclusion of 'an dalil' in the definition of ma'rifah (knowledge), claiming it has no basis in language or terminology. Three responses are given: (1) Raghib al-Isfahani's definition shows that ma'rifah implies reflection and deduction. (2) Terminologically, fiqh is defined as knowledge from proofs, so the qayd is appropriate. (3) Since knowing all rulings in detail is impossible, the condition of istinbat (deduction) is necessary to make the definition feasible.

Key Terms
معرفة (ma'rifah): Perception of particulars from a proof (ادراک الجزئیات عن دلیل)
عن دلیل ('an dalil): The condition that knowledge must be derived from a proof (istidlal)

The Twelve-Fold Classification of Actions According to Imam Muhammad
Derivation of twelve legal categories of actions with dispute on makruh tahrimi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the twelve categories of actions according to Imam Muhammad and identify the dispute regarding makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad's twelve divisions of actions hinge on whether doing or leaving is preponderant, and whether the prohibition is by definitive or speculative proof.

This passage presents the Hanafi classification of legal rulings (ahkam) according to Imam Muhammad. It shows how each category is derived through a binary tree of considerations: equality, preponderance, and proof strength. The dispute with the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) centers on the status of makruh tahrimi, affecting the total count of categories.

Guided Path
1
Start with the mukallaf's action
Every action of a legally responsible person (mukallaf) falls into one of twelve categories according to Imam Muhammad. The derivation begins by asking whether doing and leaving the action are equal or one side is preponderant.
2
Check for equality (mubah)
If the action and its abandonment are considered equal with no preference, the ruling is mubah (permissible). This is the first category.
3
Determine preponderance
If one side is preponderant, identify whether the side of doing (fard/wajib/mandub) or the side of leaving (makruh/haram) is stronger. This splits the remaining actions.
4
Trace the sub-branches
For preponderance of doing: if abandonment is prohibited → wajib; if not prohibited → mandub. For preponderance of leaving: if action is not prohibited → makruh tanzihi; if prohibited, then check the strength of the proof.
Wajib here includes both fard and wajib in the Hanafi sense (definitive vs. speculative).
5
Distinguish haram and makruh tahrimi
If the prohibition is established by a definitive proof (qati) → haram. If by a speculative proof (zanni) → makruh tahrimi. According to Imam Muhammad, makruh tahrimi falls under the category of 'prohibition of action' just like haram, differing only in proof strength.
The two shaykhs may classify makruh tahrimi separately, reducing the total number of categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the divisions are twelve because what the obligated person does etc. The commentator Taftazani is presenting the proof of the twelve divisions of the actions of the obligated person. Since there is a difference between the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Muhammad regarding the definition of makruh tahrimi, there is also difference in the basis of enumeration. According to Imam's opinion, the proof of enumeration is as follows: The action of the obligated human is either such that its doing and leaving are equal (mubah), or one side is preponderant. If the side of doing is preponderant, then either leaving is prohibited (wajib) or not (mandub). If the side of leaving is preponderant, then either doing is prohibited or not. If not prohibited, it is makruh tanzihi. If doing is prohibited, then either the prohibition is by a definitive proof (haram) or by a speculative proof (makruh tahrimi). According to Imam Muhammad, makruh tahrimi is included in prohibition of action, i.e., it is not permissible to do, rather it is obligatory to leave. So both haram and makruh tahrimi are under prohibition of action; the difference is only in the strength of proof: haram is prohibited by definitive proof and makruh tahrimi by speculative proof. And it is appropriate here to say that Imam Muhammad's basis of enumeration is suitable because the author...

This passage explains the twelve-fold classification of actions (ahkam) from a Hanafi perspective, specifically according to Imam Muhammad's view. The classification is derived by considering: (1) balance between action and abandonment (mubah), (2) preponderance of action (wajib if abandonment prohibited, mandub if not), (3) preponderance of abandonment (makruh tanzihi if action not prohibited, then if action prohibited: haram if proof definitive, makruh tahrimi if proof speculative). The dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) centers on whether makruh tahrimi is classified under prohibition or not. This classification is incomplete due to page break.

مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An action prohibited by a speculative proof; it is impermissible to do and obligatory to leave
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An action which is better to leave but not prohibited

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad's twelve-fold classification of actions is derived by considering equality, preponderance, and the strength of the prohibitive proof.

Classification of Mukallaf's Actions and the Makruh Tahrimi Dispute
Explains the six-fold classification of actions and the dispute over makruh tahrimi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define makruh tahrimi and makruh tanzihi according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish between the positions of Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the permissibility of makruh tahrimi, using the classification tree provided in the text.

Core Idea
Makruh tahrimi is prohibited but its doer is not punished with hellfire; it is a distinct Hanafi category between haram and makruh tanzihi.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi usul classification of the actions of the mukallaf, which divides all acts into six categories based on the preponderance of command or prohibition. The passage from Misk al-Malih presents a decision tree that culminates in two types of dislike: makruh tanzihi (closer to permissible) and makruh tahrimi (closer to prohibited). A key intra-Hanafi disagreement emerges over the legal nature of makruh tahrimi: does it fall under 'la yajuzu fi'luhu' (like haram) as Imam Muhammad held, or under 'yajuzu fi'luhu' (permissible but disliked) as the two shaykhs maintained? Understanding this difference has practical implications for the severity of punishment and the possibility of intercession.

Guided Path
1
Map the Classification Tree
Identify the six-fold classification of actions presented in the passage. Start with the equal/unequal sides distinction, then trace the branches leading to wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh tanzihi, and makruh tahrimi.
The tree uses a binary logic of preponderance and prohibition.
2
Define Makruh Tahrimi and Makruh Tanzihi
From the tree, extract the definitions: makruh tanzihi is closer to permissibility (doer not punished, abandoner gets small reward); makruh tahrimi is closer to prohibition (doer deserving rebuke but not hellfire). Note the distinct consequences.
Makruh tahrimi is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools often treat it as equivalent to haram.
3
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Identify that Imam Muhammad considers makruh tahrimi as 'la yajuzu fi'luhu' (like haram), while the two shaykhs consider it 'yajuzu fi'luhu' (permissible but disliked). Understand that the author of the matn sides with Imam Muhammad, but the commentator (sharh) favors the two shaykhs.
The dispute centers on whether the prohibition of makruh tahrimi renders the act impermissible or merely disliked but legally permissible.
4
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The practical difference is whether the doer of makruh tahrimi is considered a sinner deserving hellfire (Imam Muhammad) or merely deserving rebuke without hellfire (the two shaykhs). This affects the gravity of the act and the possibility of prophetic intercession.
The passage then defends the example of deprivation of intercession (shafa'a) for the doer of makruh tahrimi, offering five interpretations.
5
Evaluate the Shafa'a Argument
Review the five answers to the objection that minor sins do not deprive one of intercession. Determine which interpretation aligns best with the two shaykhs' position that makruh tahrimi is not haram.
The response highlights the nuanced understanding of shafa'a in Hanafi theology.

نے مکروہ تلز یہی کو یجوز فعلہ میں اور مکروہ تحریمی کو لا يجوز فعله بل يجب تركه ويعاقب علیہ میں داخل کیا ہے کا لحرام اور یہی اما محمد کی رائے ہے کہ وہ مکروہ تحریمی کو منع عن الفعل اور حرام کے ساتھ شامل کرتے ہیں شیخین کے مذہب کے مطابق دلیل حصر اس طرح ہے مایا تی به المكلف متساوی الطرفین ( فعل و ترک) ہوگا یا نہ اول مباح ہے اگر متساوی الطرفین نہیں ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں جانب فعل راج ہوگی یا جانب ترک اگر جانب فعل راجح و اولی ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں ترک سے منع کیا گیا ہوگایانہ اگر کیا گیا ہے تو واجب دور نہ مندوب اگر جانب ترک اولی ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں فعل سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا نہ اگر منع کیا گیا ہے تو حرام اگر فعل سے منع نہیں کیا گیا تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اقرب الی الحلت ہوگا یا اقرب الی الحرمت اگر اقرب الی الحلت ہے تو مکروہ تنزیہی ہے اقرب الی الحلت ہونے کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اس کے فاعل کو عقاب اور سزا تو نہ ہوگی البتہ اس کے تارک کو ادنی اور تھوڑ اسا ثواب ہوگا اور اگر اقرب الی الحرمت ہو تو اس کو مکروہ تحریمی کہا جائے گا اقرب الی لحرمت کا معنی یہ ہے کہ اس کے فاعل کو عقوبت بالنار تو نہیں ہوگی البتہ وہ مستحق مجذور ہوگا اس کو کوئی اور سزا دی جائے گی جیسے شارح نے اس کی مثال بیان فرمائی ہے حرمان الشفاعة کہ فاعل مکروہ تحریمی شفاعت سے محروم ہو جائے گا تو شیخین کی رائے اور مذہب کے مطابق مکروہ تحریمی يجوز فعلہ میں داخل ہے اور اس کا فاعل مستحق عقاب بالنار نہیں ہے یہ سب اس مقام کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ مصنف نے مکروہ تحریمی کو لا يجوز فعله بل يجب تركه ويعاقب على فعلہ میں درج کیا ہے خلاصہ اختلاف امام محمد شیخین یہی ہے کہ مام مکروہ تحریمی کو لا يجوز فعل او منع عن الفعل میں داخل کرتے ہیں کا لحرام اورشیخین اس کو یجوز فعلہ میں داخل کرتے ہیں۔ سوال ! شارح کا یہ قول کہ مرتکب مکروہ تحریمی شفاعت سے محروم ہو جائے گا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارتکاب مکروہ تحریمی تو گناہ صغیرہ ہے گناہ کبیرہ کا ارتکاب کرنے والا شفاعت سے محروم نہیں ہوگا تو گناہ صغیرہ کا مرتکب کیسے محروم عن الشفاعۃ ہوگا( وفي الحديث شفاعتي للكبائر من امتی ( جواب ! اس اشکال کے متعدد جوابات دیے گئے ہیں (۱) حرمان الشفاعۃ سے شفاعة النبی مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ حرمان هذا الرجل من الشفاعة للمذنبین ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ قیامت کے دن مئومنین بھی ایک دوسرے کی شفاعت کریں گے تو مرتکب مکروہ تحریمی شفاعت کرنے سے محروم ہو جائے گا جواب (۲) حرمان شفاعت کی دو صورتیں ہیں (۱) حرمان موبد (۲) حرمان مسوقت یہاں حرمان موقت مراد ہے کہ مرتکب مکروہ تحریمی کیلئے نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی شفاعت مئوخر ہو جائے گی (۳) جواب ! یہ ہے کہ شفاعة النبی کی کئی قسمیں ہیں مثلا ایک شفاعت ہوگی للاخراج من النار ہوگی ایک شفاعت لرفع درجات ہوگی مرتکب کبیرہ و مکروہ تحریمی اول کا مستحق ہوگا شانی سے محروم ہوگا یعنی اس کے درجات کی بلندی کی شفاعت نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جواب ! (۴) حرمان شفاعت سے شفاعت الملئکہ مراد . ہے جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے نیک آدمی کی دعا کی قبولیت کیلئے فرشتے سفارش کرتے ہیں اور اسکی دعا پر آمین کہتے ہیں مرتکب مکروہ تحریمی اس سے محروم ہو جاتا ہے۔ جواب! (۵) مراد تفتازانی یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص مستحق حرمان شفاعت ہے اور استحقاق حرمان شفاعت وقوع شفاعت کے منافی نہیں ہے جس طرح استحقاق عذاب منافی عفو نہیں ہے ۔
Misk al-Malih, Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The author included makruh tanzihi in 'yajuzu fi'luhu' and makruh tahrimi in 'la yajuzu fi'luhu bal yajibu tarkuhu wa yu'aqabu 'alayhi' like haram. And this is the opinion of Imam Muhammad that he includes makruh tahrimi in prohibition of the action and with haram, according to the madhhab of the two shaykhs. The proof of the enumeration is as follows: What is presented to the mukallaf either has equal sides (act and leave) or not. The first is mubah. If the sides are not equal, then two cases: either the side of action is preponderant or the side of leaving. If the side of action is preponderant and superior, then two cases: either leaving is prohibited or not. If prohibited, then wajib; if not, then mandub. If the side of leaving is superior, then two cases: either the act is prohibited or not. If prohibited, then haram. If the act is not prohibited, then two cases: either closer to permissibility or closer to prohibition. If closer to permissibility, then makruh tanzihi. The meaning of closer to permissibility is that its doer will not be punished, but its abandoner will have a small reward. If closer to prohibition, then it is called makruh tahrimi. The meaning of closer to prohibition is that its doer will not be punished with the fire, but he will be deserving of rebuke and will be given some other punishment, as the commentator gave the example of deprivation of intercession: that the doer of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of intercession. So according to the opinion and madhhab of the two shaykhs, makruh tahrimi is included in 'yajuzu fi'luhu' and its doer is not deserving of punishment by fire. All this is contrary to this place because the author included makruh tahrimi in 'la yajuzu fi'luhu bal yajibu tarkuhu wa yu'aqabu 'alayhi'. The summary of the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs is that Imam includes makruh tahrimi in 'la yajuzu fi'luhu' or prohibition like haram, and the two shaykhs include it in 'yajuzu fi'luhu'. Question: The commentator's statement that the committer of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of intercession is not correct because committing makruh tahrimi is a minor sin, and the committer of a major sin will not be deprived of intercession, so how can the committer of a minor sin be deprived of intercession? And in the hadith: 'My intercession is for the major sins of my ummah.' Answers: Multiple answers have been given to this objection: (1) Deprivation of intercession does not mean the intercession of the Prophet, but rather this person's deprivation of interceding for sinners, because in the hadith it says that on the Day of Judgment, believers will also intercede for each other, so the committer of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of making intercession. (2) Deprivation of intercession has two types: (a) perpetual deprivation, (b) temporary deprivation. Here, temporary deprivation is meant: that the intercession of the Prophet (peace be upon him) for the committer of makruh tahrimi will be delayed. (3) The answer is that the intercession of the Prophet has several types: one intercession will be for removal from the fire, another intercession will be for raising ranks. The committer of major sin and makruh tahrimi will be deserving of the first but deprived of the second, i.e., intercession for raising his ranks will not be made. (4) Deprivation of intercession means intercession of the angels, as in the hadith that angels intercede for the acceptance of a good person's prayer and say 'Amin' to his prayer; the committer of makruh tahrimi is deprived of that. (5) Taftazani's intent is that this person is deserving of deprivation of intercession, and deservingness of deprivation of intercession does not contradict the occurrence of intercession, just as deservingness of punishment does not contradict pardon.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage from Misk al-Malih, a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, addresses the classification of the actions of the mukallaf (legally responsible person) according to the Hanafi school, with particular focus on makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The author presents a decision tree: actions are either equal in act and omission (mubah) or not. If not equal, either the act is preponderant (leading to wajib if omission is prohibited, or mandub if not) or omission is preponderant (leading to haram if act is prohibited, otherwise either makruh tanzihi if closer to permissibility, or makruh tahrimi if closer to prohibition). The key dispute is between Imam Muhammad (who considers makruh tahrimi as prohibited like haram, included in 'la yajuzu fi'luhu') and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, who consider it permissible but disliked, included in 'yajuzu fi'luhu'). The passage then defends the commentator's example of deprivation of intercession for the doer of makruh tahrimi, answering objections with multiple interpretations: it may refer to inability to intercede for others, temporary delay, specific types of intercession, angelic intercession, or deservingness not contradicting actual intercession. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each branch and then addressing the shafa'a issue.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): Action closer to prohibition, doer deserving rebuke but not hellfire, and considered 'yajuzu fi'luhu' by the two shaykhs but 'la yajuzu fi'luhu' by Imam Muhammad.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): Action closer to permissibility, doer not punished, abandoner gets small reward.
شفاعت (shafa'ah): Intercession, particularly of the Prophet or angels, for forgiveness or elevation of ranks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling of makruh tahrimi?
A) It is haram and its doer is punished with hellfire.
B) It is permissible (ja'iz) but disliked, with rebuke but no hellfire.
C) It is obligatory to leave it.
D) It is recommended (mandub).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely classifies actions into six categories, and the debate over makruh tahrimi illustrates how a single term ('prohibition') can yield different rulings based on the strength of evidence and definition of punishment.

Defending the Six-Fold Classification: Wajib and Mandub Scope
Defends the six-fold classification of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi six-fold classification of actions is exhaustive by showing how 'wajib' subsumes 'fard' and 'mandub' subsumes 'sunna' and 'nafl', and evaluate the objection about makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'wajib' includes fard and 'mandub' includes sunna/nafl, making the six-fold classification exhaustive.

You have learned that the mukallaf's actions are divided into six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram). But an objector argues that fard, sunna, and nafl are separate categories, making nine total. This passage from the Sharh al-Taftazani defends the six categories by clarifying the scope of the terms 'wajib' and 'mandub' in Hanafi terminology. Let us walk through the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the Objection
The objector claims that fard, sunna, and nafl are distinct categories not covered by wajib and mandub, so there should be nine categories, not six. Recognize this challenge to the enumeration.
The objector treats fard as separate from wajib, and sunna/nafl as separate from mandub.
2
2. Understand the Hanafi Response for Wajib and Mandub
The commentator explains that 'wajib' in common juristic usage includes fard. For example, 'zakat is wajib' means it is fard. Similarly, 'mandub' is defined as 'that whose doing is superior to leaving', which broadly covers both sunna and nafl. Therefore, fard is subsumed under wajib, and sunna/nafl under mandub.
The Hanafi school distinguishes fard and wajib in strength of evidence, but in classification they can be grouped.
3
3. Analyze the Basis: Widespread Usage (Shuyu')
The Hanafi response relies on the fact that jurists commonly use 'wajib' for fard and 'mandub' for sunna/nafl. This is not a derived ruling but a terminological convention. Recognize the reliance on 'urf al-fuqaha' (juristic custom).
The proof is not a text but established usage among the scholars.
4
4. Address the Secondary Objection: Makruh Tahrimi
A further objection asks: if makruh tahrimi is like haram in being forbidden, why list it separately? The answer: while 'wajib' is commonly used for fard, 'haram' is not commonly applied to makruh tahrimi. Thus, makruh tahrimi must be a separate category.
The distinction is based on common usage, not on intrinsic similarity.
5
5. Conclude the Validity of the Enumeration
Since fard, sunna, and nafl are included under wajib and mandub, the six categories are exhaustive. The enumeration is correct.
This shows the importance of terminological precision in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text

ثم المراد بالواجب ما يشمل الفرض ايضا غرض شارح تفتازانی جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے مایاتی بہ المکلف (افعال و اعمال مکلف) کی چھ قسمیں بنائی ہیں حالانکہ چھ سے زیادہ ہیں کیونکہ فعل مکلف کی ایک قسم فرض ہے اسی طرح سنت نفل بھی فعل مکلف کے اقسام میں سے ہے یہ کل نو اقسام ہو گئیں تو وجہ حصر باطل ہوگئی ۔ جواب ! شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ حصر درست ہے کیونکہ واجب فرض کو بھی شامل ہے کیونکہ فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں فرض کا استعمال بلفظ الواجب شائع ذائع ہے كـمـا يـقـال الزكوة واجبة الحج واجب بمعنی فرض یہاں بھی واجب کا یہی معنی عام مراد ہے اسی طرح مندوب سنت اور نفل دونوں کو شامل ہے کیونکہ مندوب کا معنی ہے ماكان فعلہ اولی من ترکہ یہ معنی عام ہے سنت اور نفل کو بھی شامل ہے۔ سوال ! پھر تو مکروہ تحریمی کو بھی جداز کر نہیں کرنا چاہئے کیونکہ وہ بھی حرام میں داخل ہے بالمعنی الائم تو اس کو کیوں علیحدہ و مستقلا ذکر کیا بخلاف الحرام سے شارح اسی اشکال کو دفع کر رہے ہیں کہ واجب کا اطلاق علی الفرض یہ تو شائع عند الفقہاء ہے لیکن اطلاق حرام مکروہ تحریمی پر یہ مشہور و معروف عند الفقہاء نہیں ہے اس لیے مکروہ تحریمی کو علیحدہ ومستقلا ذکر کیا اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ افعال مکلف منحصر ہیں في ستة اقسام فالحصر صحيح
Then the intended meaning of 'wajib' includes fard as well. The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to answer an implied question. Question: It is that the author made six categories of what is brought to the mukallaf (actions and deeds of the mukallaf), whereas there are more than six, because one category of the action of the mukallaf is fard, similarly sunna and nafl are also among the categories of the action of the mukallaf. That totals nine categories, so the basis of the enumeration becomes invalid. Answer: The commentator is answering that the enumeration is correct because 'wajib' includes fard as well, since in the terminology of the jurists, the usage of 'fard' with the word 'wajib' is widespread and common, as it is said 'zakat is wajib', 'hajj is wajib' meaning fard. Here too, this general meaning of 'wajib' is intended. Similarly, 'mandub' includes both sunna and nafl because the meaning of 'mandub' is 'that whose doing is superior to leaving it'; this meaning is general and includes sunna and nafl. Question: Then makruh tahrimi should also not be separated because it is included in haram in a general sense, so why was it mentioned separately? The commentator is repelling this objection by saying that the application of 'wajib' to fard is widespread among jurists, but the application of 'haram' to makruh tahrimi is not well-known and famous among the jurists. Therefore, makruh tahrimi was mentioned separately. From this, it is established that the actions of the mukallaf are confined to six categories, so the enumeration is correct.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage continues the defense of the six-fold classification of actions of the mukallaf presented earlier. An objector argues that there are more than six categories because fard, sunna, and nafl are distinct from wajib, mandub, etc. The commentator (Taftazani) responds that in Hanafi terminology, 'wajib' is often used interchangeably with 'fard' (e.g., 'zakat is wajib' meaning obligatory), so fard is subsumed under wajib. Similarly, 'mandub' is a general term that covers both sunna (established by the Prophet's continuous practice) and nafl (supererogatory), because mandub simply means 'that whose doing is preferable to leaving.' Thus, the six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram) are exhaustive. A further objection asks why makruh tahrimi is listed separately if it is like haram. The answer is that while 'wajib' is commonly used for fard, 'haram' is not commonly applied to makruh tahrimi among the jurists, so a separate category is needed.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): In this context, includes both fard (established by definitive evidence) and wajib (established by probable evidence), used broadly as obligatory.
مندوب (mandub): Action whose doing is superior to leaving, includes sunna and nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator argue that the six-fold classification is still correct despite fard, sunna, and nafl being separate?
A) Because fard, sunna, and nafl are not actions of the mukallaf.
B) Because 'wajib' includes fard and 'mandub' includes sunna and nafl.
C) Because the author intentionally omitted fard, sunna, and nafl.
D) Because fard is actually a type of mandub.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'wajib' can include fard and 'mandub' can include sunna/nafl due to common juristic usage, making the six-fold classification exhaustive.

The Six Meanings of Wujub in Arabic Usage
Lists six meanings of 'wujub'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the six meanings of 'wujub', and explain which meaning is appropriate in a given context, particularly in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Wujub has six meanings; only one is the Hanafi usul term—context determines which is meant.

The Arabic word 'wujub' (وجوب) is used across many fields, from fiqh to philosophy. In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, it has a precise technical sense: an obligation established by probable (zanni) evidence, distinct from 'fard' which comes from definitive evidence. But in everyday juristic speech, as well as in other disciplines, it carries additional meanings. This lesson will help you recognise these six usages so that you can accurately interpret primary texts and avoid confusion.

Guided Path
1
Memorise the six categories
Read through the six meanings listed in the passage. For each, note the key Arabic phrase that exemplifies it (e.g. 'wajib fi al-istilah', 'wajib bi-ma'na al-fard', 'wajaba al-shams', etc.).
Meaning 1 is the Hanafi technical term; meaning 2 is common among imams; meanings 3–6 are non-fiqh usages.
2
Group meanings by domain
Classify the six meanings into two groups: (a) fiqh-related (meanings 1 and 2) and (b) linguistic/philosophical (meanings 3–6). This helps in identifying which meaning is likely intended in a given text.
In fiqh works, meanings 1 and 2 are most common; in kalam or philosophy, meaning 6 appears.
3
Connect each meaning to a sample sentence
For each meaning, construct a sentence (or use the provided ones) that clearly illustrates that meaning. Drill these pairs so that you can automatically recall the meaning when you see a phrase.
For example: 'zakah wajib' → meaning 2 (fard); 'wajab al-shay' → meaning 4 (established).
4
Practice distinguishing meaning 1 and 2
Meaning 1 (technical Hanafi) and meaning 2 (common for fard) are easily confused. Study the difference: meaning 1 implies zanni dalil, meaning 2 is used loosely for fard. In many classical texts, 'wajib' may be used for both. Look for contextual clues (e.g., discussion of proofs) to decide.
The passage explicitly states that meaning 2 is 'shāi' among the imams, so be alert.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائده! (۱) وجوب متعدد معانی میں مستعمل ہوتا ہے (۱) وجوب اصطلاحی ای ماثبت بدلیل ظنی (۲) وجوب بمعنی الفرض وهذا شائع عند الائمه كما يقال الزكوة واجبة والحج واجب وغيره (۳) وجوب بمعنی غروب كما يقال وجب الشمس اى غربت (۴) وجوب بمعنی ثبوت كما يقال وجب الشئى أى ثبت (۵) وجوب بمعنى اولى راح كما يقال هذا الوقت واجب ای راجح (۶) وجوب بمعنی دوام مقابلے میں امتناع اور امکان کے كما يقال واجب الوجود .
Benefit! (1) 'Wujub' is used in multiple meanings: (1) Terminological obligation: that which is established by probable evidence. (2) 'Wujub' in the meaning of fard, and this is widespread among the imams, as it is said 'zakat is wajib' and 'hajj is wajib' meaning fard. (3) 'Wujub' in the meaning of setting, as it is said 'wajaba al-shams' i.e., it set. (4) 'Wujub' in the meaning of establishment, as it is said 'wajaba al-shay' i.e., it became established. (5) 'Wujub' in the meaning of preponderance, as it is said 'hadha al-waqt wajib' i.e., preponderant. (6) 'Wujub' in the meaning of necessity, in contrast to impossibility and possibility, as it is said 'wajib al-wujud' (necessary existence).
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This is a standalone fa'ida (benefit) that lists six distinct meanings of the Arabic word 'wujub' (وجوب) and its derivatives. The first meaning is the terminological one in usul al-fiqh: something established by a zanni (probable) dalil, as opposed to fard which is qat'i. The second meaning equates 'wajib' with 'fard' in common juristic usage. The third is unrelated to fiqh: 'wajaba al-shams' means the sun set. The fourth means 'became established'. The fifth means 'preponderant' or 'most likely'. The sixth is used in philosophy: 'wajib al-wujud' means necessary existence (of God).

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): A term with multiple meanings: terminological (probable obligation), fard, setting, establishment, preponderance, necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the terminology of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, what does 'wajib' specifically mean?
A) That which is established by a definitive (qat'i) evidence.
B) That which is established by a probable (zanni) evidence.
C) That which is preponderant (rajih).
D) That which is necessary (wajib al-wujud).

Key Takeaway
The word 'wajib' has six distinct meanings; in Hanafi usul it means obligation from zanni dalil, but context must always be checked.

Defending the Six-Fold Classification: Wajib Includes Farz, Mandub Includes Sunnah and Nafil
Defending the six-fold classification against objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Hanafi school defines 'wajib' and 'mandub' in a broad sense to include farz, sunnah, and nafil, and explain why makruh tahrimi is listed separately.

Core Idea
The six-fold classification stands because 'wajib' and 'mandub' are general terms that subsume farz, sunnah, and nafil.

The author of the matn classified the actions of the mukallaf into six categories. An objector argues that farz, sunnah, and nafil are separate, making nine categories. In this passage, the commentator Taftazani defends the original classification by showing that 'wajib' includes farz and 'mandub' includes sunnah and nafil. He also addresses why makruh tahrimi is not simply called haram. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and terminological reasoning behind this defense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims there are more than six categories because farz, sunnah, and nafil are separate from wajib and mandub.
2
Understand the commentator's response
Taftazani argues that 'wajib' in this context is used broadly to include farz, just as jurists commonly say 'Zakat is wajib' meaning it is farz.
3
Extend the logic to mandub
Similarly, 'mandub' is defined as 'that whose doing is preferable to its leaving', which includes both sunnah and nafil, because both are recommended.
4
Address the separate listing of makruh tahrimi
Although makruh tahrimi is a type of haram in one sense, the term 'haram' is not commonly used by Hanafi jurists for it, so it is listed separately.
5
Confirm the validity of the six-fold classification
With these clarifications, the original six categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram) are exhaustive and correct.

Source Text

مسک الملیح (۱۴۳) شرح التوضيح والتلويح  تحریمی اس سے محروم ہو جاتا ہے۔ جواب! (۵) مراد تفتازانی یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص مستحق حرمان شفاعت ہے اور استحقاق حرمان شفاعت وقوع شفاعت کے منافی نہیں ہے جس طرح استحقاق عذاب منافی عفو نہیں ہے ۔ ثم المراد بالواجب ما يشمل الفرض ايضا غرض شارح تفتازانی جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے مایاتی بہ المکلف (افعال و اعمال مکلف) کی چھ قسمیں بنائی ہیں حالانکہ چھ سے زیادہ ہیں کیونکہ فعل مکلف کی ایک قسم فرض ہے اسی طرح سنت نفل بھی فعل مکلف کے اقسام میں سے ہے یہ کل نو اقسام ہو گئیں تو وجہ حصر باطل ہوگئی ۔ جواب ! شارح جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ حصر درست ہے کیونکہ واجب فرض کو بھی شامل ہے کیونکہ فقہاء کی اصطلاح میں فرض کا استعمال بلفظ الواجب شائع ذائع ہے كـمـا يـقـال الزكوة واجبة الحج واجب بمعنی فرض یہاں بھی واجب کا یہی معنی عام مراد ہے اسی طرح مندوب سنت اور نفل دونوں کو شامل ہے کیونکہ مندوب کا معنی ہے ماکان فعلہ اولی من ترکہ یہ معنی عام ہے سنت اور نفل کو بھی شامل ہے۔ سوال ! پھر تو مکروہ تحریمی کو بھی جداز کر نہیں کرنا چاہئے کیونکہ وہ بھی حرام میں داخل ہے بالمعنی الائم تو اس کو کیوں علیحدہ و مستقلا ذکر کیا بخلاف الحرام سے شارح اسی اشکال کو دفع کر رہے ہیں کہ واجب کا اطلاق علی الفرض یہ تو شائع عند الفقہاء ہے لیکن اطلاق حرام مکروہ تحریمی پر یہ مشہور و معروف عند الفقہاء نہیں ہے اس لیے مکروہ تحریمی کو علیحدہ ومستقلا ذکر کیا اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ افعال مکلف منحصر ہیں في ستة اقسام فالحصر صحيح
Misk al-Malih (143) Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. The tahrimi is deprived of this. Answer (5): Taftazani means that this person is deserving of deprivation of intercession, and deserving deprivation of intercession does not contradict the occurrence of intercession, just as deserving punishment does not contradict pardon. Then the intended meaning of wajib includes farz as well. The aim of the commentator (Taftazani) is to answer an implied objection. Objection: The author made six categories of what comes from the mukallaf (actions of the mukallaf), yet there are more than six because farz is one category, similarly sunnah and nafil are also among the categories of the mukallaf's actions; thus there would be nine categories, so the justification for restriction is invalid. Answer: The commentator replies that the restriction is correct because wajib includes farz; in the terminology of jurists, the use of the term wajib for farz is widespread, e.g., 'Zakat is wajib', 'Hajj is wajib' meaning farz. Here also wajib is used in this general sense. Similarly, mandub includes both sunnah and nafil, because the meaning of mandub is 'that whose doing is preferable to its leaving'; this general meaning includes sunnah and nafil. Objection: Then makruh tahrimi should also not be singled out, because it is included in haram in one sense; why is it mentioned separately and independently? The commentator refutes this objection: That applying wajib to farz is widespread among jurists, but applying haram to makruh tahrimi is not well-known among jurists. Therefore makruh tahrimi is mentioned separately. Thus it is proven that the actions of the mukallaf are confined to six categories; so the restriction is correct.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the six-fold classification of a mukallaf's actions as presented in the matn. The commentator (Taftazani) first addresses an earlier point about deprivation of intercession, then moves to the main issue: an objector claims there are more than six categories (e.g., farz, sunnah, nafil), making the restriction invalid. The commentator's response is that the term 'wajib' here is used in a general sense that includes farz; similarly, 'mandub' is general and includes sunnah and nafil. A further objection about makruh tahrimi being separate from haram is answered by noting that while makruh tahrimi is haram in one sense, the common usage of 'haram' by jurists does not extend to it, so it is listed separately. The conclusion reaffirms the original sixfold restriction as correct.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): In this passage, wajib is used generically to include farz; it is a term for obligatory acts, commonly applied to farz by Hanafi jurists.
مندوب (mandub): Defined as 'that whose doing is preferable to its leaving'; it includes sunnah and nafil.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An act that is prohibited but not termed 'haram' in common juristic usage; it is included in the broader meaning of haram but listed separately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is not forbidden at all
B) Because jurists commonly call it haram
C) Because jurists do not commonly apply the term 'haram' to it
D) Because it is more severe than haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi six-fold classification of actions is defensible because 'wajib' and 'mandub' are broad terms that include subcategories like farz, sunnah, and nafil, and separate listing of makruh tahrimi is based on conventional usage.

The Six Meanings of Wujub in Hanafi Usul
Listing six meanings of wujub

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain each of the six meanings of wujub and apply the correct meaning in a given context.

Core Idea
Wujub has six distinct meanings: technical obligation, definitive duty, setting, confirmation, preference, and permanence.

In Hanafi legal theory, the term 'wajib' is used in multiple senses. This lesson unpacks the six meanings listed in the source, clarifying when each is intended. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly interpreting usul texts and avoiding confusion between technical obligation and everyday usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six meanings
List all six meanings from the source: (1) technical wujub (zanni obligation), (2) wujub as farz, (3) setting (as in sunset), (4) confirmation, (5) preference, (6) permanence.
Notice that meanings 3-6 are non-legal; only 1-2 are relevant to fiqh rulings.
2
Distinguish technical wujub from farz
The first meaning is the usuli definition: an obligation established by zanni (probabilistic) evidence. The second meaning equates wujub with farz (definitive obligation). In Hanafi usul, farz is from qati evidence, wujub from zanni. But in common usage, imams often say 'wajib' for farz.
This distinction is key to Hanafi epistemology: rulings differ in binding force based on evidence certainty.
3
Recognize lexical meanings
Meanings 3-6 are taken from Arabic language: setting (sunset), confirmation (establishment), preference (choosing), and permanence (necessary existence). These are not legal categories but contextual senses.
Wajib al-wujud (necessary existent) is a theological term for God's self-sufficiency.
4
Apply the correct meaning
When encountering 'wajib' in a text, determine which meaning is intended by context. For example, 'wajib al-adā' (required performance) uses meaning 1 or 2; 'wajab al-shams' uses meaning 3.
This skill prevents misinterpretation of classical texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائده! (۱) وجوب متعدد معانی میں مستعمل ہوتا ہے (۱) وجوب اصطلاحی ای ماثبت بدلیل ظنی (۲) وجوب بمعنی الفرض وهذا شائع عند الائمه كما يقال الزكوة واجبة والحج واجب وغيره (۳) وجوب بمعنی غروب كما يقال وجب الشمس اى غربت (۴) وجوب بمعنی ثبوت كما يقال وجب الشئى أى ثبت (۵) وجوب بمعنى اولى راح كما يقال هذا الوقت واجب ای راجح (۶) وجوب بمعنی دوام مقابلے میں امتناع اور امکان کے كما يقال واجب الوجود . قائده (۲) سنت مندوب ومستجب عند البعض مترادف ہیں ان میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے عند البعض ما الله ان میں فرق ہے سنت کی تعریف یہ ہے ما واظب عليه النبي ع وتر که احیانا بلا عذر اور مستحب کی تعریف مالم يواظب عليه النبي الله وفعله وتركه سواء - مندوب کی تعریف مالم يواظب عليه النبي وتركه اكثر واغلب من فعله
Benefit! (1) Wujub is used in multiple meanings: (1) Technical wujub: what is established by a probabilistic evidence. (2) Wujub in the sense of farz; this is common among the imams, as they say 'Zakat is wajib', 'Hajj is wajib'. (3) Wujub in the sense of setting, as in 'the sun set' (wajabat al-shams). (4) Wujub in the sense of confirmation, as in 'the thing is established' (wajaba al-shay'). (5) Wujub in the sense of preference, as in 'this time is preferred' (wajib). (6) Wujub in the sense of permanence, in contrast to contingency and possibility, as in 'necessary existent' (wajib al-wujud). Rule (2): Sunnah, mandub, and mustahab, according to some, are synonymous with no difference; according to others, there is a difference. The definition of sunnah is: what the Prophet continuously performed, sometimes without excuse. The definition of mustahab is: what the Prophet did not continuously perform, and he did it and left it equally. The definition of mandub is: what the Prophet did not continuously perform, and he left it more often or predominantly.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage begins with a fa'ida (benefit) listing six meanings of wujub. The first is the technical usuli meaning: an obligation established by a zanni (probabilistic) dalil. The second is a common usage where wujub means farz (definitive obligation). Other meanings include setting (for the sun), confirmation, preference, and permanence. Then a qa'ida (rule) discusses the terms sunnah, mandub, and mustahab. Some scholars treat them as synonyms; others distinguish them: sunnah is what the Prophet continuously did, mustahab is what he did and left equally, and mandub is what he left more often. The definitions are based on the Prophet's practice and the frequency of performance or omission.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): The term has six meanings: technical (zanni obligation), farz (definitive), setting, confirmation, preference, and permanence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Wujub in the sense of setting

Key Takeaway
The term wujub has six meanings; only the first (technical obligation) and second (farz) are directly relevant to fiqh rulings.

Distinguishing Sunnah, Mandub, and Mustahab
Defining sunnah, mandub, mustahab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definitions of sunnah, mandub, and mustahab and explain the scholarly disagreement over their synonymy.

Core Idea
Sunnah, mandub, and mustahab are distinguished by the frequency of the Prophet's performance and omission.

Beyond obligation, Hanafi usul classifies recommended acts into three terms: sunnah, mandub, and mustahab. While some scholars treat them as synonyms, others differentiate based on the Prophet's continuous practice and frequency of omission. This lesson examines those definitions and the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terms
The passage lists sunnah, mandub, and mustahab. Note that some scholars consider them synonymous, while others distinguish them.
This ikhtilaf affects how fiqh texts describe recommended acts.
2
Define sunnah
Sunnah: what the Prophet continuously performed, occasionally omitting without excuse. This indicates a stronger recommendation.
Example: the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah.
3
Define mustahab
Mustahab: what the Prophet did not continuously perform, and he did it and left it equally. This is a lesser recommendation.
Example: praying four rak'ahs before Asr.
4
Define mandub
Mandub: what the Prophet did not continuously perform, and he left it more often than doing. This is the weakest recommendation.
Example: praying two rak'ahs before Maghrib? (varies)
5
Apply the distinction
When a hadith shows the Prophet performed an act irregularly, classify it as mustahab or mandub based on frequency of omission.
If the Prophet did it and left it equally → mustahab; if he left it more often → mandub.

The definition of mandub is: what the Prophet did not continuously perform, and he left it more often or predominantly.

Taftazani's Objection on Mandub Including Sunnah
Objection and response about mandub including sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi tripartite classification of sunnah to resolve whether mandub includes sunnah and evaluate the objection.

Core Idea
Not all sunnah is equal: only sunan zawa'id are synonymous with mandub.

In this passage, we encounter a sharp objection by Taftazani against the claim that mandub includes sunnah. The objector argues that sunnah carries a prohibition on leaving, based on the Prophet's command to hold fast to his sunnah, whereas mandub by definition has no such prohibition. The Hanafi response offers a nuanced answer: it distinguishes between types of sunnah, showing that only the non-emphatic type (sunan zawa'id) is truly equivalent to mandub. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly classifying acts and their ruling in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the objection
Identify Taftazani's claim: mandub includes sunnah is problematic because mandub lacks a prohibition on leaving, but sunnah has such a prohibition based on a hadith.
The hadith cited: 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly guided caliphs.'
2
Analyze the first Hanafi response
The first answer redefines 'prohibition of leaving': it means a prohibition whose violation entails Hellfire. In this sense, neither mandub nor sunnah carries such a prohibition, so sunnah can be included in mandub.
3
Analyze the second Hanafi response: the tripartite division
The second answer distinguishes three types: sunnah huda (emphatic, blameworthy to leave), sunan zawa'id (synonymous with mandub, no blame), and nafl (purely voluntary). Only sunan zawa'id are included in mandub.
This classification resolves the apparent conflict.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is whether abandoning a sunnah act incurs blame. For sunnah huda it does; for sunan zawa'id it does not.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The passage prefers the Hanafi position by showing that Taftazani's objection does not apply to all sunnah, only to the emphatic type.

اعتراض تفتازانی کا یہ قول که مندوب سنت کو بھی شامل ہے قابل اشکال ہے کیونکہ شارح کے قول کے مطابق مندوب میں ترک فعل سے منع نہیں ہوتی اور اس کا تارک مستحق اسارت نہیں ہوتا جب کہ تارک سنت مستوجب سلامت و اسائت ہوتا ہے نیز اس میں منع عن الترک بھی ہے، قال النبی الله عليكم بسنتی وسنه الخلفاء الراشدين جواب ! (۱) منع عن الترک سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسی منع ہو کہ اس کا ارتکاب موجب عقاب النار ہو مندوب میں عدم منع سے بھی یہی مراد ہو گا اور بائیں معنی سنت مندوب میں داخل ہے کیونکہ اس سنت کا ترک بھی موجب عقاب نار نہیں ہے۔ جواب ! (۲) در اصل سنت تین قسم پر ہے (۱) سخت متوکده ويسمى سنة هدی اس کا تارک مستوجب ملامت و اسائت ہے (۲) سنن زوائد وهي التي ليس في فعلها تكميل الدين لكن فعلها افضل من تركھا یہ سنت مترادف ہے مندوب اور مستحب کے اس کا تارک لا يستحق لوما ولا كراهة ولا اسائة ولا عقابا كسنة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في قعوده وقيامه ومشيه واكله وشربه وغيره (۳) نقل . وهو ما يشاب المرء على فعله ولا يعاقب على تركه فالنفل ما لم يفعله عليه السلام ولم يرغب فيه بخصوصه فهو عبادة مشروعة لم يرغب فيها الشارع عليه السلام
Objection: Taftazani's statement that mandub includes sunnah is objectionable because according to the commentator's statement, mandub does not prohibit leaving and its abandoner is not deserving of punishment, while the abandoner of sunnah deserves reproach and blame; also there is a prohibition of leaving in it, as the Prophet said, 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly guided caliphs.' Answer (1): The prohibition of leaving means a prohibition whose commission entails punishment of Hellfire. In mandub, the absence of prohibition means this, and in this sense sunnah is included in mandub because leaving sunnah also does not entail punishment of Hellfire. Answer (2): In reality, sunnah is of three types: (1) Emphatic sunnah, called sunnah hudā; its abandoner deserves blame and reproach. (2) Additional sunan (sunna zawa'id), which are not for completing religion, but doing them is better than leaving; this sunnah is synonymous with mandub and mustahab; its abandoner does not deserve blame, dislike, reproach, or punishment, like the Prophet's sunnah in sitting, standing, walking, eating, drinking, etc. (3) Nafil (supererogatory); it is what one is rewarded for doing and not punished for leaving; so nafil is what the Prophet did not do and did not specifically encourage; it is an act of worship that the Lawgiver did not encourage.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents an objection by Taftazani against the claim that mandub includes sunnah. The objector argues that mandub lacks a prohibition on leaving, but sunnah has such a prohibition based on the hadith 'Hold fast to my sunnah...' and abandoning it incurs blame. Two responses are given: First, the prohibition on leaving in sunnah is not the type that carries hellfire; thus it is consistent with mandub. Second, sunnah is divided into three types: sunnah huda (emphatic, blameworthy to leave), sunnah zawa'id (synonymous with mandub, no blame), and nafil (purely voluntary). Only the second type is included in mandub. This clarifies the terminology and resolves the objection.

Key Terms
سنة هدى (sunnah huda): Emphatic sunnah; its abandoner deserves blame and reproach.
سنن زوائد (sunan zawa'id): Additional sunan; not required for completion of religion; doing is better than leaving; synonymous with mandub.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory; not done or encouraged by the Prophet; rewarded for doing, not punished for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for abandoning sunnah zawa'id?
A) Deserving of Hellfire
B) Deserving of blame and reproach
C) No blame, no punishment
D) The act becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi resolution shows that only emphatic sunnah (sunnah huda) carries blame; non-emphatic sunan (zawa'id) are equivalent to mandub.

Resolving the Act-Omission Division: Masdari vs. Hasil bil-Masdar
Explaining the two sides (act and omission) and the masdari vs hasil bil-masdar distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the masdari and hasil bil-masdar meanings of an action and apply this distinction to resolve logical objections in the classification of actions in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The same word 'fi'l' can mean abstract act or concrete state; distinguishing them prevents logical fallacies in classification.

In Hanafi usul, actions are classified into categories, each with an act side and an omission side. But this raises a logical issue: if 'fi'l' is both the whole category and a part, we seem to be dividing a thing into itself. This lesson unpacks the commentator's resolution: the term 'fi'l' has two distinct meanings – the masdari (verbal noun, abstract act) and the hasil bil-masdar (resulting state). The division uses the masdari sense, making it logically sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dilemma
Recognize that the category 'what comes from the mukallaf' is divided into six types, each with two sides: act (fi'l) and omission (tark). The objection is that 'fi'l' appears both as the whole and as a part, implying self-division.
This is a common logical puzzle in usul that requires careful terminological analysis.
2
Discover the Two Senses of 'Fi'l'
Understand that 'fi'l' has two meanings: the masdari (the abstract act, e.g., 'praying') and the hasil bil-masdar (the concrete state resulting, e.g., 'prayer' as a state). The commentator clarifies that the division uses the masdari meaning.
In Arabic, both are expressed by the same word, but conceptually they differ.
3
Apply the Distinction to the Division
When dividing 'what comes from the mukallaf' into act and omission, 'act' is taken in its masdari sense (the concept of doing), and 'omission' is also taken as a concept (non-doing). These are two conceptual sides, not two concrete states. Thus the category 'action' (as masdari) is not being divided into itself; rather, it is being divided into two sub-concepts.
This resolves the objection: the whole (masdari) is not identical to the part (also masdari but specifying the doing side); they are at the same conceptual level.
4
Solidify with the Example
Consider 'praying' (masdar) vs. 'prayer' (hasil). The division into act/omission uses the masdari meaning of the act (like 'praying') and the concept of not praying (omission). The concrete state of prayer is not part of the division.
In Persian, the words differ, making the distinction clearer, but in Arabic one must rely on context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكل منها طرفان فعل اى ايفاع على ما هو المعنى المصدری و ترک ای عدم فعل الخ غرض شارح توضیح متن ہے ! حاصل یہ کہ فعل مکلف کی چھ قسمیں ہیں پھر ہر قسم کی دو طرفیں ہیں (۱) طرف فعل (۲) طرف ترک پھر شارح نے یہ بھی وضاحت کر دی کہ فعل سے مصدری معنی مراد ہے یعنی الا بفاع کسی چیز کو واقع کرنا اور ترک بھعنی عدم فعل ہے اس سے بھی مصدری معنی عدم الايقاع مراد ہے حاصل بالمصدر مراد نہیں ہے وجہ ابھی آرہی ہے ) اب کل بارہ قسمیں بن جائیں گی۔والمراد بما يأتى المكلف غرض شارح جواب سوال مقدر۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ آپ نے یہ کہا ہے کہ مایاتی بہ المکلف کی چھ قسمیں ہیں پھر ہر ایک کی دو طرفیں ہیں ایک فعل دوسری ترک تو اشکال یہ پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ مایاتی بہ المکلف سے بھی فعل مکلف مراد ہے پھر اس کی دوطرفیں ہیں۔ ایک طرف فعل دوسری طرف ترک گویا مقسم بھی فعل مکلف اور اس کی قسم بھی فعل مکلف ہے پھر فعل کا معنی آپ نے مصدری کیا ہے یعنی الا بقاع تو لازم متقسم ( فعل ) کا بھی یہی معنی ہوگا تو حاصل یہ نکلے گا کہ ایقاع کی دو قسمیں (طرفیں ) ہیں ایک ایقاع دوسری عدم ایقاع یہ تو بالکل غلط ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں تقسيم الشئى إلى نفسه والی غیرہ لازم آتی ہے۔ جواب ! جواب سے قبل یہ بات ذہن نشیں فرمالیں کہ جب فاعل سے فعل کا صدور ہوتا ہے تو وہاں دو معنی حاصل ہوتے ہیں ایک معنی مصدری وحدتی اور دوسرا حاصل بالمصدر معنی مصدری تو واضح اور مشہور ہے حاصل با المصدر کی تعریف یہ ہے وہ بیت و حالت جو فائل کو بوقت صدور فعل عن الفاعل حاصل ہوتی ہے اسی ہیئت کا نام حاصل بالمصدر ہے یہ معنی مصدری پر مترتب اور اس کا نتیجہ ہوتا ہے مثلا ایک ہے نماز پڑھنا یہ مصدری معنی ہے جو ایک انتزاعی ہے موجود فی الخارج نہیں ہے ایک ہے نماز یعنی وہ ہیئت جو مصلی کو حاصل ہوتی ہے بوقت فعل صلوۃ اس کو حاصل بالمصدر کہا جاتا ہے عربی میں مصدر حاصل بالمصدر میں کوئی لفظی فرق نہیں ہے ایک ہی صیغہ مصدر اور حاصل بالمصدر دونوں کیلئے مستعمل ہوتا ہے البتہ فارسی میں دونوں میں لفظی فرق ہے مصدر کے آخر میں دن یا تن ہوتا ہے۔ حاصل بالمصدر کے آخر میں شین یا راہ ہوتی ہے مثلا کردن ، گفتن مصدر اور کردار و گفتار، حاصل بالمصدر ہیں اسی طرح کوشیدن ستودن مصادر اور کوشش بخشش ستائش حاصل با المصدر ہیں اس تمہید کے بعد اب جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب ثابت ہو گیا کہ فعل کے دو معنی ہیں (۱)
And each of them has two sides: act, i.e., occurrence, according to the masdari meaning, and omission, i.e., not acting, etc. The aim of the commentator is to explain the matn. The summary is that the actions of the mukallaf are six categories, then each category has two sides: (1) the act side (2) the omission side. Then the commentator also clarified that by 'fi'l' the masdari meaning is intended, i.e., bringing something into existence, and by 'tark' the meaning is non-existence of the act, also in the masdari sense of non-occurrence. The hasil bil-masdar is not intended; the reason will come later. Now there will be twelve categories in total. And the meaning of 'what comes from the mukallaf' is the aim of the commentator in answering an implied objection. Objection: You said that 'what comes from the mukallaf' has six categories, then each has two sides: act and omission. The problem arises that 'what comes from the mukallaf' also means the action of the mukallaf, yet its division includes act and omission, so the divided (the action) and the division (act/omission) would both be the action. Then you take 'fi'l' in the masdari sense, i.e., occurrence, then the divided (action) would also have that meaning, resulting in two types of occurrence: occurrence and non-occurrence, which is wrong because it would require dividing a thing into itself and another. Answer: Before answering, bear in mind that when an action issues from the agent, two meanings arise: one is the masdari (verbal noun) and the other is hasil bil-masdar (the resulting state). The masdari is clear and well-known. The definition of hasil bil-masdar is the state that the agent experiences at the time of the action; this is called hasil bil-masdar. It is dependent on the masdari meaning and is its result. For example, 'praying' is the masdari meaning, which is abstract and not externally existent; another is 'prayer' i.e., the state that the one praying experiences at the time of the act of prayer; this is called hasil bil-masdar. In Arabic, there is no lexical difference between masdar and hasil bil-masdar; the same form is used for both. However, in Persian there is a lexical difference: the masdar ends with 'dan' or 'tan', and the hasil bil-masdar ends with 'shin' or 'rah', e.g., kardan, guftan are masdars, and kardar, guftar are hasil bil-masdar; similarly, koshidan, situdan are masdars, and koshish, bakhshish, sita'ish are hasil bil-masdar. After this preamble, the sum of the answer is that since it is established that 'fi'l' has two meanings... (the text ends incompletely).
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage explains a key structural point: each of the six categories of actions has two sides – performing the act and omitting it, yielding twelve total. The commentator clarifies that when we say 'fi'l' (act) in the division, we mean the masdari (verbal noun) meaning – the act of doing – not the hasil bil-masdar (the resulting state). This distinction resolves an objection: if 'fi'l' (action) is the thing being divided and also one of the divisions, that would be self-division. The response is that the 'fi'l' being divided refers to the masdari meaning (the act in the abstract), while the division into 'act' and 'omission' uses the same term but in a different sense: 'act' as one side is also masdari, but it is not the same as the total category; rather, the category is the broader 'what the mukallaf does' which includes both performing and omitting. The example of praying: the masdar 'praying' is the abstract action, while the hasil bil-masdar 'prayer' is the concrete state. In Arabic, both use the same word, but in Persian they differ. The commentator thus shows that the division is logically sound.

Key Terms
مصدر (masdar): The verbal noun, the abstract act itself, e.g., 'praying'.
حاصل بالمصدر (hasil bil-masdar): The state resulting from the act, e.g., 'prayer' as the state of the worshipper.
ترک (tark): Omission of an act; also considered a 'fi'l' in the sense of not doing, but it is the absence of the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The difference between Arabic and Persian
B) The difference between masdari and hasil bil-masdar
C) The difference between fard and wajib
D) The difference between action and intention

Key Takeaway
The masdari/hasil bil-masdar distinction is a fundamental tool in Hanafi usul for avoiding equivocation in classifying actions.

Definition of Tark as 'Adam al-Fi'l in Hanafi Usul
Explaining why tark is defined as absence of action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul defines 'tark' as pure absence of action and apply this definition to maintain the twelve-fold classification of actions.

Core Idea
Tark is 'adam al-fi'l – pure absence – not refraining; refraining is itself an action.

In Hanafi usul, the term 'tark' (omission) is a technical term with a precise meaning. This passage, from Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, clarifies why the author defines tark as 'adam al-fi'l (absence of action) rather than its common linguistic meaning of refraining. Understanding this definition is essential to grasp the Hanafi classification of legal rulings (ahkam) into twelve categories: each of the six basic rulings (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh, haram) applies to both the action and its omission. If tark were taken as refraining, the classification would collapse, as refraining from haram is itself a wajib action.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish two meanings of tark
Recognize that 'tark' can mean either pure absence ('adam basit) or refraining (kaff al-nafs). The latter is a psychological act and counts as an action.
2
Understand the twelve-fold classification
The six primary categories (wajib, mandub, mubah, makruh tanzihi, makruh tahrimi, haram) each have two aspects: doing the act and omitting the act, yielding twelve divisions.
3
Identify the problem with the refraining meaning
If tark means refraining, then tark al-haram (refraining from prohibited) is itself an obligatory action, and tark al-wajib (refraining from obligatory) is a prohibited action, reducing the twelve to six.
4
Apply the definition of tark as 'adam al-fi'l
By defining tark as pure absence, tark al-haram is not an action at all; it is a distinct division that does not attract reward or punishment directly (except as part of the obligation to avoid haram). Thus the twelve-fold classification stands.

والامور المذكورة من الواجب والحرام وغيرهما الخ غرض شارح تفتازانی جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ وجوب حرمت ندب وغیرہ اقسام ستہ کی دو طرفیں بنائی گئی ہیں ایک فعل اور ایک ترک حالانکہ یہ تو صرف مکلف کے فعل کی صفات بنتی ہیں ترک یعنی عدم فعل کی نہیں بنتی یعنی جب فعل کا صدور مکلف سے ہوتا ہے اس وقت اسکو واجب یا مندوب کہا جاتا ہے اگر ترک اور عدم فعل ہے تو اسکو واجب اور مندوب وغیرہ نہیں کہا جائے گا لہذا جانب ترک کو وجوب ندب حرمت وغیرہ کی صفت قرار دیکر بارہ قسمیں بنانا کیسے صحیح ہے۔ جواب: خلاصہ جواب یہ ہے کہ تسلیم ہے کہ امور مذکورہ ( وجوب ندب وغیرہ ) فی الحقیقت تو فعل مکلف کی صفات ہیں نہ کہ ترک کی لیکن کبھی کبھی ان کو ترک کی صفات بھی قرار دیا جاتا ہے مثلا یوں کہا جاتا ہے عدم مباشرة الواجب حرام یہاں عدم مباشرۃ کا معنی ترک الواجب ہے تو ترک واجب کو حرام کہا گیا ہے دیکھئے حرام ترک (عدم نعل ) کی صفت واقع ہو رہا ہے اسی طرح یوں کہا جاتا ہے ، عدم مبــا شـــره الـحـرام واجب ای ترک الحرام واجب، تو یہاں بھی وجوب ترک کی صفت بن رہا ہے اسی معنی کی وجہ سے ان کو فعل اور ترک دونوں کی صفات قرار دے کر بارہ قسمیں بنائی گئیں۔
وانما فسر الترك بعدم الفعل ليصير قسما آخر غرض شارح جواب سوال مقدر ۔ سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے ترک کی تغییر عدم النفعل کے ساتھ کیوں کی ہے حیث قال وطرف الترک ای عدم الفعل ، حالانکہ لفظ ترک واضح ہے محتاج الی التفسیر نہیں ہے۔ جواب ! حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے ترک کی تفسیر عدم فعل کیسا تھ اس لیے کی ہے کیونکہ ترک دو معنوں میں استعمال ہوتا ہے ترک معنی عدم فعل جسے سلب بسیط اور نفی محض کہنا چاہئے یعنی فعل بالکل معدوم ہوتا ہے (۲) دوسرا معنی ترک ہمعنی کف النفس عن الفعل یعنی جب کسی کام کیلئے اسباب مہیا ہوں اور نفس اس کی طرف میلان کرے اس وقت نفس کو اس سے روک لینا ترک بایں معنی (کف النفس ) طرف فعل میں داخل ہے یعنی یہ بھی ایک قسم کا فعل ہے تو مصنف نے ترک کی تغییر عدم النفعل کے ساتھ کر کے بتلا دیا کہ یہاں ترک کا معنی اول ( عدم الفعل ) مراد ہے معنی ثانی کف

النفس مراد نہیں ہے کیونکہ اگر ترک یعنی کف النفس مراد ہوتا تو پھر فعل مکلف کی بارہ قسمیں نہیں بن سکتی تھیں کیونکہ ترک besturdubooks
الحرام بمعنی کف النفس عن الحرام بعینہ فعل واجب ہے تو یہ فعل واجب میں داخل ہو جاتا ہے اس طرح ترک الواجب بمعنی کف النفس بعینہ حرام ہے تو یہ حرام میں داخل ہو جاتا تو فعل مکلف کی بارہ قسمیں ختم ہو جاتیں۔ اس لیے ترک کی تفسیر عدم فعل کے ساتھ کی تاکہ بارہ قسمیں بن جائیں اگر ترک بمعنی عدم فعل ہو تو پھر ترک الحرام واجب میں داخل نہیں ہوگا ۔ بلکہ مستقل قسم ہوگی کیونکہ ترک حرام بمعنی عدم الفعل واجب میں داخل ہو تو اس پر ثواب ملنا چاہئے حالانکہ ثواب نہیں ملتا تو معلوم ہوا یہ بعینہ واجب انه نہیں ہے۔
Misk al-Malih, Sharh al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. besturdubooks.wordpress.com. [The meaning] derived from the source (2): In the source that comes from the obligated person, in the level of the divided term, the intended meaning of 'action' is not the masdari meaning but rather the product of the source (hasil bi al-masdar), i.e., the attribute that the doer obtains at the time of performing the action and that inheres in the doer, like the acquired attribute called 'prayer' and the acquired attribute called 'fasting', which inhere in the one praying and fasting, and which are an effect emanating from the obligated person. Then, in its two sides – action and omission – here 'action' means the masdari meaning, i.e., occurrence, and 'omission' means non-occurrence. Hence here there is no division of a thing into itself and its other, nor a division of occurrence into occurrence; rather there is a difference between the divided term and the divisions. Thus the objection is repelled. And the mentioned matters of obligatory, prohibited, etc. The commentator Taftazani intends to answer a presupposed question: How can the six categories (obligation, prohibition, recommendation, etc.) be predicated on both action and omission, making twelve divisions, when these are attributes of the action, not of omission? Answer: It is conceded that these are essentially attributes of the action, but sometimes they are also attributed to omission metaphorically. For example, it is said: 'Non-performance of the obligatory is prohibited', where non-performance means omission of the obligatory, so prohibition is an attribute of omission. Similarly, 'Non-performance of the prohibited is obligatory', so obligation is an attribute of omission. For this reason, they made twelve divisions by considering them attributes of both action and omission. And (the author) defined omission as absence of action to make it another division. The commentator answers another presupposed question: Why did the author define omission as absence of action, when the word 'omission' is clear and does not need explanation? Answer: Because 'omission' is used in two senses: (1) absence of action, which is pure negation and simple negation, i.e., the action is completely nonexistent; (2) omission meaning refraining from action, i.e., when means for an action are prepared and the soul inclines towards it, then restraining the soul from it – this meaning (reining) is included in action, i.e., it is a kind of action. So the author defined omission as absence of action to indicate that here the first meaning (absence of action) is intended, not the second meaning (reining). Because if omission meant reining, then the twelve divisions of the obligated person's actions could not be maintained. Since omission of the prohibited in the sense of reining from the prohibited is itself an obligatory action, it would enter into obligatory actions. Similarly, omission of the obligatory in the sense of reining is prohibited, so it would enter into prohibited. Then the twelve divisions would reduce. Therefore, he defined omission as absence of action so that twelve divisions arise. If omission is in the sense of absence of action, then omission of the prohibited will not enter into obligatory, but will be an independent division. [The argument continues: because if omission of the prohibited in the sense of absence of action entered into obligatory, then there would be reward for it, but there is no reward, so it is clear that it is not exactly obligatory.]
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) by Taftazani on Al-Tawdih, addressing definitions and classifications in usul al-fiqh. The author first clarifies the meaning of 'fi'l' in the context of dividing actions (af'al) into categories. He distinguishes between the masdari (verbal noun) meaning of 'action' as mere occurrence (iqa') and the 'hasil bi al-masdar' meaning – the attribute that results from the action and inheres in the doer, like the specific qualities of prayer and fasting. In the division of actions into action and omission, the intended meaning of 'fi'l' is the masdari sense (occurrence), and 'tark' means non-occurrence ('adam al-iqa'), thus avoiding the fallacy of dividing a thing into itself. Next, Taftazani explains why the six primary categories (wajib, haram, etc.) are applied to both action and omission, yielding twelve total. The objection is that these categories are attributes of actions, not omissions. The answer is that although inherently they describe actions, they are sometimes predicated on omissions by extension, as when we say 'leaving the obligatory is haram' – here 'haram' qualifies the omission. Thus, to cover both, the scholars considered each category in two aspects: its action and its omission. Finally, Taftazani justifies why the author defined 'tark' specifically as 'adam al-fi'l' (absence of action) rather than using the common word 'tark'. The reason is that 'tark' can mean either pure absence (salb basit) or the psychological act of refraining (kaff al-nafs). The latter is itself an action (a type of fi'l). If 'tark' were taken in the sense of refraining, then 'tark al-haram' would be wājib (since refraining from haram is an obligatory action), and 'tark al-wajib' would be haram, collapsing the twelve divisions back into six. Therefore, to preserve the twelve-fold division, the intended meaning of 'tark' here is pure absence, not the act of refraining. This is a crucial definitional clarification in Hanafi usul, as it affects how obligations and prohibitions are understood in relation to omission.

Key Terms
الترك (al-tark): In this passage, tark is defined as 'adam al-fi'l, i.e., the pure absence of an action, not the psychological act of refraining.
الفعل (al-fi'l): In the division of actions, fi'l means the masdari sense (occurrence/īqā') as opposed to the resulting attribute (hasil bi al-masdar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author of Al-Tawdih define 'tark' as 'adam al-fi'l rather than using its common meaning?
A) Because the word 'tark' is ambiguous and needs clarification.
B) To prevent the twelve categories from collapsing into six.
C) Because 'tark' in Arabic always means absence.
D) To align with the Mu'tazili definition.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'tark' is defined as pure absence of action ('adam al-fi'l) to maintain a distinct category for omission and the twelve-fold classification of legal rulings.

Necessity of the Twelve-Fold Division: Why Omission Categories Are Distinct
Defense of twelve-fold division against reductionist proposal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi usul scholars maintain a separate twelve-fold division for actions and omissions, and evaluate the proposal to reduce it to six.

Core Idea
An omission of haram is not rewarded, so it cannot be part of wajib—hence the twelve-fold division is necessary.

In this passage, the commentator Taftazani defends the classical twelve-fold division of the hukm shar'i (obligatory, recommended, etc.) against an objection that it is unnecessarily complex. The objector proposes that since omissions (e.g., tark al-haram) are themselves wajib, the six categories could be generalized to cover both action and omission. Taftazani refutes this by appealing to the author's definition of wajib as 'that for which reward is given' (ma yuthab 'alayh): omitting a haram act does not yield reward, so it cannot be included under wajib. This forces the six categories to remain distinct, producing the full twelve.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objector's proposal
Read the objector's argument: they claim the twelve-fold division is unnecessary because omissions (like tark al-haram) can be incorporated into the action categories by generalization. For example, define wajib as 'its action is wajib, and its omission is...' so that tark al-haram becomes a part of wajib.
Notice the objector assumes that 'tark al-haram' is wajib, which is true in Hanafi fiqh, but the question is whether it fits the definition.
2
Analyze the commentator's refutation
Taftazani argues that this generalization is impossible because the author (Sadr al-Shariah) has defined wajib as 'ma yuthab 'alayh' (that for which there is reward). If tark al-haram were included under wajib, then it would have to be rewarded, but there is no reward for simply omitting a prohibited act.
The key is the definitional constraint: the hukm categories are defined by their reward/punishment properties, not just by logical subsumption.
3
Understand the consequence for classification
Because tark al-haram does not yield reward, it cannot be part of wajib (which is defined by reward). Therefore, the six categories for actions must be matched by six corresponding categories for omissions, giving twelve total. The omission of haram is a distinct category (wajib al-tark) that cannot be collapsed into the action category.
This demonstrates that the twelve-fold division is not arbitrary but logically necessary given the definitions.
4
Relate to the broader usul principle
This passage illustrates how precision in definitions (hudud) is crucial in usul al-fiqh. The definition of 'wajib' as ma yuthab 'alayh is a Hanafi technical term that carries specific consequences for classification.
Other schools may define wajib differently, leading to alternative classifications.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage continues Taftazani's commentary, addressing two further objections. The first objection challenges the entire twelve-fold division as unnecessary. The objector proposes that since omissions can be subsumed under the six primary categories (e.g., 'tark al-haram is wajib'), we could simply generalize each category to cover both its action and its omission. For example, define wajib as 'its action is wajib and its omission is...' and then tark al-haram would be considered wajib. The commentator (Taftazani) refutes this by pointing out that the author (Sadr al-Shariah) has defined wajib as 'that for which there is reward' (ma yuthab 'alayh). If tark al-haram (in the sense of absence of the haram act) were included under wajib, then it would be rewarded, but there is no reward for omitting a haram act. Therefore, the categories must remain separate; omission of haram has no reward, so it cannot be wajib. This confirms the need for the twelve-fold division: six categories for actions and six corresponding categories for omissions. The second objection, which is incomplete in this window, concerns the author's statement that 'action of haram and makruh tahrimi and leaving wajib are punished'. The objector claims this contradicts the Ahl al-Sunnah position that punishment is not necessarily entailed for sins (as opposed to the Mu'tazila). Taftazani begins to respond, but the text breaks off. The implication is that the author's wording must be interpreted in line with Sunni creed.

Key Terms
ما يثاب عليه (ma yuthab 'alayh): That for which there is reward; the author's definition of wajib.
الواجب (al-wajib): In this context, wajib is defined by the author as 'ma yuthab 'alayh' (that which is rewarded), and its omission is punishable.
ترك الحرام (tark al-haram): Omission of a prohibited act; considered wajib in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Takeaway
The twelve-fold division is not redundant but logically necessary because omissions like tark al-haram do not fit the definition of their corresponding action categories.
