شارح تفتازانی احکم کے معانی بیان کرنا چنانچہ فرمایا کہ حکم متین معانی میں مستعمل ہوتا ہے گو یا ضمنا مصنف پر اعتراض کر دیا کہ حکم دو معنوں میں نہیں بلکہ تین معانی کیلئے آتا ہے (۱) حکم کا عرفی ( عند الناس) معنی پھر اس عرضی معنی کو مختلف الفاظ سے تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے (۱) مصنف نے تعبیر کیا ہے اسناد امرالی اخرایجا با او سلبا یعنی ایک شئی کی نسبت کرنا دوسری شئی کی طرف خواہ ایجابا ہو خواہ سلبا ہو (۲) شارح تفتازانی تعبیر کر رہا ہے النسبة التامة بین الامرین (ای الموضوع والمحمول) (۳) نسبته نامه خبریه (۴) نسبت امرالی امراخر ایجابا اوسلب (۵) النسبة من حیث الوقوع ولا وقوع (۲) حکم کا دوسرا معنی اصطلاحی ہے (ای فی اصطلاح اہل الاصول والفقہ ) وہ ہے خطاب اللہ تعالی المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء اوا تحیر یعنی حکم نام ہے خطاب اللہ کا مثلاً صلوا، صوموا، جو اوغیرہ پھر یہ خطاب متعلق ہو افعال و اعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ بالاقتضاء واجب سنت مندوب کو شامل ہے کیونکہ ان میں اقتضاء فعل ہے اور حرام مکروہ تحریمی و تنزیہی کو بھی شامل ہے کیونکہ ان میں اقتضاء ترک ہے او اتخییر مباح کو شامل ہے (۳) وفی اصطلاح المنطق سے تیسرا معنی حکم بیان کیا یہ معنی حکم کا منطقی ہے (ای عند اہل المناطقہ ) حکم منطقی کی تعریف یہ کی ادراک ان النسبہ واقعہ ام لیست بواقعہ یعنی اس بات کا اور اک و علم کہ نسبت تامہ واقع ہے یا نہ اور اسی کو بعینہ تصدیق کہا جاتا ہے تو عند المناطقہ حکم اور تصدیق مترادف ہیں۔ وهو ليس بمراد ههنا الخ شارح تفتازانی ! یہاں سے بتلانا چاہتے ہیں کہ فقہ کی تعریف میں حکم کے معانی ثلاثہ میں سے کون سامعنی مراد ہے تو فرمایا یہ تیسرا معنی ( معنی منطقی ) مراد نہیں ہو سکتا وجہ یہ بیان کی کہ حکم منطقی خود علم اور ادراک کا نام ہے کیونکہ ابھی گذرا ہے کہ اس کو تصدیق کہا جاتا ہے اور تصدیق علم ہی ہے لہذا اگر فقہ کی تعریف میں یہی مراد لیا جائے تو تعریف اس طرح ہو جائے گی الفقہ ھو علم بالعلوم الشرعیة (الاحکام) کی جگہ علوم کا لفظ آ جائے گا اسطرح تعریف صحیح نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ فقہ علوم شرعیہ کے علم کا نام نہیں ہے بلکہ معلومات شرعیہ ومسائل شرعیہ کے علم کا نام فقہ ہے۔ والمحققون على ان الثاني ايضا ليس بمراد الخ شارح تفتازانی ! فرماتے ہیں کہ مصنف نے اگر چہ یہ فرمایا ہے کہ یہاں حکم کا اصطلاحی معنی ممکن ہے لیکن محققین نے تصریح کی ہے کہ یہاں معنی اصطلاحی ( معنی ثانی ) عند الاصولیین بھی مراد نہیں ہو سکتا اس کی وجہ یہ بیان کی کہ اگر یہاں حکم کا معنی اصطلاحی خطاب اللہ مراد لیا جائے تو فقہ کی تعریف میں الشرعیہ اور اعملیہ کی قید کا تکرار اور لغو ہونا لازم آئے گا کیونکہ حکم خطاب اللہ کا نام ہے تو شرعی ہونا یہیں سے معلوم ہو گیا کیونکہ شریعت تو نام ہی خطاب اللہ کا ہے اس کے بعد دوبارہ الشرعیہ کا ذکر تکرار بن جائے گا اسی طرح المتعلق با فعال المکلفین سے حکم کا عملی ہونا ثابت ہوگیا پھر دوبارہ عملیہ کے قید کا ذکر کرنا تکرار محض ہوگا لہذا حکم کا یہ معنی بھی یہاں مراد نہیں ہو سکتا۔ بل المراد النسبة التامة جب آخری دو معنی مراد نہیں ہو سکتے تو شارح تفتازانی فرماتے ہیں کہ اب صرف ایک معنی اول باقی رہ گیا ہے وہ معنی عرفی ہے تو یہاں حکم سے یہی معنی مراد ہے یعنی نسبت تامہ خبر یہ جسے اسناد امرالی آخر بھی کہا جاتا ہے اور اس نسبت تامہ کے ساتھ جو علم متعلق ہو گیا اس کو تصدیق کہا جائے گا اور غیر نسبت نامہ کے ساتھ جو علم متعلق ہو گیا اس کو تصور کہا جائے گا اور مصنف نے يخرج التصورات و يبقي التصديقات سے اسی معنی (اسناد امرالی اخر ) کے مراد ہونے کی طرف اشارہ فرمايا - فيكون الفقه عبارة عن التصديق بالقضايا الشرعية سے شارح نے اس معنی عرفی کے مراد لینے کے بعد فقہ کی تعریف کا حاصل بیان کیا ہے کہ فقہ اب عبارت ہوگی قضایا شرعیہ عملیہ ( جو کیفیت عمل سے متعلق ہوں) کی تصدیق سے ایسی تصدیق جوادلہ تفصیلیہ سے حاصل ہو وہ ادلہ تفصیلیہ جن کو شریعت مطہرہ نے ان ( قضایا) پر نصب و مقرر کیا ہیوال ! فقہ کی تعریف میں لفظ ھوا اعلم تھا شارح تفتازانی نے اس کی جگہ لفظ تصدیق کیوں ذکر کیا۔ جواب! اشارہ کیا کہ یہاں العلم تصدیق کے معنی میں ہے۔ سوال افقہ کی تعریف میں بالا حکام کا لفظ تھا شارح تفتازانی نے اس کو تبدیل کر کے القضایا کا لفظ کیوں استعمال کیا۔ جواب ! جب یہاں حکم بمعنی نسبت تامہ و اسناد امر آخر مراد لیا گیا ہے اور نسبت نامہ خبریہ قضیہ ہی میں ہوتی ہے اور قضیہ کا جزء صوری بنتی ہے اس لیے شارح نے حکم کی جگہ القضایا کا لفظ ذکر کر دیا فوائد قیود
Commentator Taftazani explains the meanings of 'hukm': he said that 'hukm' is used in three meanings. First: the customary meaning (among people), which is expressed in various phrases: (1) the author expressed it as asnad amr ila akhar ijaban aw salban, i.e., attributing something to another, whether affirmatively or negatively; (2) commentator Taftazani expresses it as al-nisba al-tamma bayn al-amrayn (subject and predicate); (3) nisba tamam khabariyya; (4) nisbat amr ila amr akhar ijaban aw salb; (5) al-nisba min hayth al-wuqu' aw la wuqu'. Second: the terminological meaning (in the terminology of usuliyyun and fuqaha), which is khitab Allah ta'ala al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin bi'l-iqtida' aw al-takhyir, i.e., 'hukm' is the name of the address of Allah, e.g., 'pray', 'fast', etc. Then this address is related to the actions of the legally responsible persons by way of requirement: it includes wajib, sunnah, mandub because they require action; and haram, makruh tahrimi and tanzihi because they require abandonment; and mubah by way of choice. Third: in the terminology of logic, the logical meaning is defined as idrak an al-nisba waqi'a am laysat bi-waqi'a, i.e., cognition that the complete relation exists or does not exist; and this is precisely called tasdiq. So according to logicians, hukm and tasdiq are synonyms. He says: 'And it is not intended here.' Commentator Taftazani wants to show which of the three meanings of hukm is intended in the definition of fiqh. He says that the third meaning (logical) cannot be intended because logical hukm itself is knowledge and cognition, as it was mentioned that it is called tasdiq, and tasdiq is knowledge. Therefore if this meaning is taken in the definition of fiqh, the definition would become: al-fiqh huwa 'ilm bi'l-'ulum al-shar'iyya — instead of 'al-ahkam' the word 'ulum' would come, and the definition would not be correct, because fiqh is not the name of knowledge of the religious sciences, but rather the name of knowledge of religious matters and issues. And the investigators are of the opinion that the second meaning is also not intended. Commentator Taftazani says that although the author said that the terminological meaning is possible here, the investigators have specified that the terminological meaning (second meaning) according to usuliyyun cannot be intended either. The reason is that if the terminological meaning of hukm, i.e., khitab Allah, is taken, then the restriction 'al-shar'iyya' and 'al-'amaliyya' in the definition of fiqh would become redundant and useless, because hukm being the address of Allah, its being shar'i is already known (since shari'a is the name of the address of Allah), so mentioning 'al-shar'iyya' again would be repetition. Similarly, from 'al-muta'alliq bi-af'al al-mukallafin' the practical nature of hukm is established, so mentioning 'al-'amaliyya' again would be pure repetition. Therefore this meaning also cannot be intended here. Rather, the intended meaning is al-nisba al-tamma. Since the last two meanings cannot be intended, commentator Taftazani says that now only the first meaning (customary) remains, and that is intended here, i.e., the complete relational predicate (nisba tamam khabariyya) which is also called asnad amr ila akhar. And knowledge that relates to this complete relation is called tasdiq, and knowledge that relates to a non-complete relation is called tasawwur. The author indicated this meaning by his statement 'he excludes conceptions and retains assertions'. So from 'facon al-fiqh ibarat an al-tasdiq bi'l-qadaya al-shar'iyya' the commentator has expressed the result of the definition after taking the customary meaning: fiqh now would be the assertion of religious practical propositions (which relate to the quality of actions), an assertion that is obtained from detailed proofs that the pure shari'a has established for those propositions.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the term 'hukm' as it appears in the definition of fiqh. The commentator Taftazani clarifies that 'hukm' is used in three distinct senses: customary (urfi), terminological (istilahi) in usul, and logical (mantiqi). The goal is to determine which meaning is intended in the definition 'fiqh is knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings derived from detailed proofs'. The logical meaning is rejected because it would make the definition tautological (knowledge of knowledge). The terminological meaning is rejected because it would make the qualifiers 'shar'i' and 'practical' redundant, as the term 'hukm' already implies them. Therefore, the intended meaning is the customary one: a complete relational predication (nisba tamam khabariyya), i.e., a proposition. Hence, fiqh is defined as the assent (tasdiq) to religious practical propositions, which are derived from detailed proofs. This analysis ensures precision in the definition and guards against misinterpretation.

Key Terms
الحكم (al-hukm): In this passage, hukm is analyzed in three meanings: customary (complete relational predication), terminological (divine address), and logical (cognition of relation). The intended meaning is the customary one.
التصديق (al-tasdiq): Assent or affirmation of a proposition; knowledge of a complete relation.
النسبة التامة (al-nisba al-tamma): Complete relation or predication that constitutes a proposition (qadiyya).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the terminological meaning of 'hukm' rejected in the definition of fiqh?
A) It is not a valid meaning in Arabic.
B) It would cause redundancy with the words 'shar'i' and 'amali'.
C) The author of the text did not like it.
D) It is only used in logic.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh must be understood as a complete proposition (nisba tamma), not a divine command or a logical judgment.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
15 min
Critique of Defining Hukm as Khitab Allah in Fiqh Definition
Taftazani critiques Sadr al-Shariah's definition of fiqh when hukm means khitab Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of hukm in the definition of fiqh and critique the consequences of taking it as khitab Allah.

Core Idea
Taking hukm as khitab Allah makes qualifiers redundant, forcing forced interpretations.

In the classical definition of fiqh, the term 'hukm' is ambiguous. Most scholars, including Taftazani, prefer the customary meaning (isnad amr ila akhar). However, Sadr al-Shariah allowed the technical usul meaning (khitab Allah). This lesson unpacks Taftazani's critique of that choice, showing how it leads to logical complications and redundant qualifiers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the standard definition and the two interpretations of hukm
The definition of fiqh is 'knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings from their detailed evidences.' The term hukm can be taken in its 'urfi sense (attribution of a command to another) or in its technical usul sense (khitab Allah).
The customary meaning is preferred by the majority (jumhur) and investigators (muhaqqiqun).
2
Analyze the consequences of taking hukm as khitab Allah
If hukm = khitab Allah, then the qualifiers 'shar'iyyah' (since khitab Allah is inherently shar'i) and 'amaliyyah' (since it concerns actions of mukallaf) become redundant. The definition would reduce to 'knowledge of rulings from evidences.'
This redundancy forces the author to adopt forced interpretations (takallufat) to justify the qualifiers.
3
Examine the forced interpretations by Sadr al-Shariah
To justify the qualifiers, he divided hukm into shar'i and ghayr shar'i, redefined shar'iyyah narrowly as 'ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar', and generalized 'fi'l' to include heart actions. These lead to circular dependency (dawr) and inconsistency with Ash'ari principles.
Taftazani lists multiple takallufat, each creating new problems.
4
Understand Taftazani's preferred resolution
Taftazani prefers the customary meaning, which makes the qualifiers functional and avoids takallufat. This is the position of the jumhur and muhaqqiqun.
The choice of interpretation affects the clarity and logical coherence of the definition.

غلام زید میں اضافت تب درست ہوگی جب وجود زید کی معرفت ہو نیز یہ بھی معلوم ہو کہ زید ذواختیار، ذو علم ، وملک ، ذو قدرت ، ذوحیات چیز ہے اگر نہ وجود زید کی معرفت ہو نہ صفات کی تو اضافت غلام زید صحیح نہیں الشرع جب ثابت ہوا کہ وجوب الایمان موقوف علی الشرع ہے اور خود شریعت موقوف علی وجوب الایمان ہے تو دور لازم آئے گا۔ وانما قال الخطاب بما يتوقف الخ غرض جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مصنف نے خطاب اور حکم شرعی کی تعریف کی ھو خطاب بما توقف علی الشرع یعنی خطاب اس چیز کے ساتھ کہ وہ چیز موقوف ہو شریعت پر یوں تعریف کیوں نہیں کی هو الخطاب الذى يتوقف على الشرع كه وه خود خطاب شریعت پر موقوف ہو اسی طرح غیر شرعی کی تعریف یوں کی جاتی الخطاب الذى لا يتوقف على الشرع خلاصہ اشکال یہ ہے شرعی اور غیر شرعی کی تعریف میں لفظ ما کا ذکر نہیں ہونا چاہئے ۔ جواب ! شارح تفتازانی جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ شرعی اور غیر شرعی کی تعریف میں لفظ ما کا ذکر کرنا بہت ضروری ہے ورنہ خرابی لازم آئے گی کیونکہ اگر لفظ ما نہ ہو تو تعریف حکم شرعی اس طرح ہوگی الخطاب الذى يتوقف على الشرع یعنی خود خطاب موقوف ہو شریعت پر حالانکہ خطاب اللہ قدیم ہے اور قدیم چیز کسی پر موقوف نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ موقوف دلیل حدوث ہوتی ہے اسی لیے ما کا لفظ بڑھا دیا گیا ہے اب حکم شرعی کی تعریف یہ ہوگی ھو الخطاب بما يتوقف على الشرع يعنی اس چیز کے ساتھ خطاب اللہ جو چیز موقف على الشرعیہ ہو اس صورت میں خود نفس خطاب شریعت پر موقوف نہیں ہوگا بلکہ متعلق خطاب ( وہ چیز جس کے ساتھ خطاب کا تعلق ہے مثلا صلوۃ صوم ) وہ شریعت پر موقوف ہو گا فلا بر دالاشكال - ولقائل ان يمنع توقف الشرع على وجوب الايمان ونحوه الخ غرض سوال علی المصنف ! مصنف نے حکم کی دو قسمیں بنائی شرعی غیر شرعی پھر غیر شرعی (بمعنی مالا توقف علی الشرع ) کی مثال بیان کی وجوب الایمان وجوب تصدیق النبی اور کہا کہ یہ شریعت پر موقوف نہیں اور دلیل یہ بیان کی اگر یہ شریعت پر موقوف ہوں تو لزم
It is apparent on this estimation that the intention of the commentator's phrase is that on the estimation that when the meaning of hukm is 'isnad amr ila akhar' (attribution of a command to another), then in the definition of fiqh the benefits of the restrictions are completely clear, without any dust, pure and transparent, free from defect and difficulty, just as by reflecting on the definition, the benefits of the restrictions will become perfectly clear. And the author permitted that by hukm here the terminology of the people of usul (i.e., khitab Allah) could be intended. The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to present an objection to the author. The report of the objection is that the majority and the investigators took in the definition of fiqh the meaning of hukm as 'urfi (isnad amr ila akhar), and according to that meaning the benefits of the restrictions in the definition were perfectly clear. But the author said that here the meaning of hukm could also be khitab Allah. Now an objection occurs to the author: if the meaning of hukm is taken as khitab Allah, then in the definition of fiqh the restriction 'shar'iyyah' and ''amaliyyah' become useless, because from khitab Allah its being shar'i is understood, and from 'with the actions of the mukallaf' its being 'amali is proven. Then the definition of fiqh should have been just 'knowledge of the rulings from their detailed evidences.' So the author, to save these restrictions (shar'iyyah and 'amaliyyah) from being redundant and repetitive and to make them proper, committed many forced interpretations and arbitrary acts in explaining the intended meaning of the people. It would have been better if the author had not taken this meaning so that he would not have to commit these forced interpretations. So he went to what Taftazani intended, that he is explaining the forced interpretations the author committed. (1) The first forced interpretation is that he made two divisions of hukm: shar'i and ghayr shar'i, whereas hukm in the meaning of khitab Allah is only shar'i, not non-shar'i. (2) The second forced interpretation is that he defined shar'iyyah as 'ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'' (that which depends on the sharia), in the sense that if the address of the Lawgiver had not come, then knowledge of this ruling would not be possible, whereas the definition of shar'iyyah is 'ma warada bihi khitab al-shar'iyyah' (that which the sharia address came with), which is more general than 'ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'. When he made two divisions of hukm in the meaning of khitab Allah: shar'i and ghayr shar'i, he defined shar'i hukm as 'huwa al-khitab bima yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'' (i.e., the address of Allah about something that depends on the sharia), e.g., the obligation of prayer and fasting. And he defined ghayr shar'i as 'huwa al-khitab bima la yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'' (i.e., the address about something that does not depend on the sharia), and he gave as an example the obligation of faith in Allah and the obligation of affirming the Prophet's prophethood. These are rulings that do not depend on the sharia because the sharia depends on five matters: (1) existence of Allah, (2) knowledge of Allah, (3) power of Allah, (4) speech of Allah, (5) affirmation of the prophethood of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The sharia of Allah depends on these five matters because the sharia is attributed to Allah, and for the validity of attribution, knowledge of the existence of the thing attributed to is necessary, and knowledge of its attributes. For example, the attribution 'slave of Zayd' is correct only when one knows the existence of Zayd and also that Zayd is a being with authority, knowledge, possession, power, life. If there is no knowledge of Zayd's existence or attributes, then the attribution is not correct. Similarly, the attribution of sharia to Allah is correct only when the existence of Allah and His being All-Knowing, All-Powerful, All-Wise is proven, and faith in that is obtained. Also, for the establishment of sharia, affirmation of the intermediary (the Prophet) is necessary. If the intermediary is not affirmed, how can the sharia be established? In any case, from this explanation it is proven that the sharia depends on the obligation of faith in Allah and the obligation of affirming the Prophet (which is obtained by the evidence of miracles). Now if the obligation of faith and the obligation of affirming the Prophet themselves depend on the sharia, then a circle will occur: the sharia depends on them, and they again depend on the sharia. That is called a cycle (dawr). Therefore, it is proven that the obligation of faith and the obligation of affirming the Prophet do not depend on the sharia, which is what was claimed. And this is called a non-shar'i ruling. So by adding the restriction 'shar'iyyah', this non-shar'i ruling (obligation of faith and obligation of affirming the Prophet) is excluded. So the author adopted this whole forced interpretation to make the restriction 'shar'iyyah' beneficial and effective. Also, to make the restriction ''amaliyyah' beneficial, he generalized 'af'āl' (actions) in 'af'āl al-mukallafīn' and intended by it both actions of the heart and actions of the limbs, whereas 'fi'l' is used only for actions of the limbs. Also, he committed arbitrariness in saying that the obligation of faith does not depend on the sharia, whereas according to the Ash'aris, the obligation of faith depends on the sharia, because the Ash'aris say 'la wujub illa bi al-sam'' (no obligation except by the revelation). When it is established that the obligation of faith depends on the sharia, and the sharia depends on the obligation of faith, then a cycle would occur. And he said: 'al-khitab bima yatawaqqaf' etc. The purpose is to answer a presupposed question. The question is: the author defined the address and shar'i hukm as 'huwa al-khitab bima tatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'' (i.e., address concerning something that depends on the sharia). Why did he not define it as 'al-khitab alladhi yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'' (the address itself that depends on the sharia)? Similarly, the definition of non-shar'i would be 'al-khitab alladhi la yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'. The summary of the objection is that the word 'ma' should not be mentioned in the definition of shar'i and non-shar'i. The answer: The commentator Taftazani is answering that it is very necessary to mention the word 'ma' in the definition of shar'i and non-shar'i, otherwise corruption would be necessary. Because if the word 'ma' is not there, the definition of shar'i hukm would be 'al-khitab alladhi yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar' (the address itself that depends on the sharia), whereas the address of Allah is eternal, and an eternal thing does not depend on anything, because dependence is a sign of temporality. Therefore, the word 'ma' was added. Now the definition of shar'i hukm will be 'huwa al-khitab bima yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar' (the address concerning something that depends on the sharia). In this case, the address itself does not depend on the sharia, but the object of the address (the thing with which the address is connected, e.g., prayer, fasting) will depend on the sharia. So there is no objection. And one could say: one may deny the dependence of the sharia on the obligation of faith and similar matters. The purpose is an objection against the author. The author made two divisions: shar'i and non-shar'i, then gave as an example of non-shar'i (in the meaning of 'ma la yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar') the obligation of faith and the obligation of affirming the Prophet, and said they do not depend on the sharia, and gave as proof: if they depended on the sharia, then a cycle would occur.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by Taftazani (the super-commentator) on Sadr al-Shariah's formulation in Al-Tawdih. The issue is the proper definition of fiqh. The common definition is 'knowledge of the practical shar'i rulings derived from their detailed evidences.' The key term is 'hukm' (ruling). Most scholars interpret 'hukm' in this context in its 'urfi (customary) sense: the attribution of a command to another (isnad amr ila akhar). On this interpretation, the qualifiers 'shar'iyyah' (shar'i) and ''amaliyyah' (practical) are useful and clear. However, Sadr al-Shariah allowed that 'hukm' could also mean the terminology of the usul scholars: the address of Allah (khitab Allah) pertaining to the actions of the mukallaf. Taftazani points out that if we take 'hukm' as khitab Allah, the qualifiers become redundant: khitab Allah is intrinsically shar'i, and pertaining to actions of the mukallaf implies 'amali. So the definition would reduce to just 'knowledge of rulings from their evidences,' making the qualifiers superfluous. To justify them, Sadr al-Shariah engaged in several forced interpretations (takallufat). First, he divided hukm into shar'i and ghayr shar'i, even though hukm as khitab Allah is always shar'i. Second, he defined shar'i hukm as the address concerning something that depends on the sharia (ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'), and gave examples like the obligation of prayer and fasting, which depend on revelation. Non-shar'i hukm he defined as the address concerning something that does not depend on the sharia, like the obligation of faith in Allah and affirming the Prophet. This is problematic because from an Ash'ari perspective (which the author follows), there is no obligation except through revelation (la wujub illa bi al-sam'), so even the obligation of faith depends on the sharia, leading to a circular dependency. Taftazani also criticizes the generalizing of 'af'al' to include actions of the heart, when 'fi'l' normally means limb actions. Finally, Taftazani defends the inclusion of the word 'ma' in the definition to avoid implying that the eternal address itself depends on the sharia. This passage exemplifies the precise logical analysis characteristic of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The authority weight is from the later period (mutakkhirin), as Taftazani is a later Hanafi scholar writing a super-commentary on a matn.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): In the definition of fiqh, it can mean either the customary attribution of a command to another (isnad amr ila akhar) or the address of Allah (khitab Allah) as per usul terminology.
شرعي (shar'i): In this context, it qualifies hukm: a shar'i ruling is one that depends on the sharia (ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar') meaning it cannot be known without divine address.
ما يتوقف على الشرع (ma yatawaqqaf 'ala al-shar'): That which depends on the sharia; i.e., its knowledge requires revelation; without sharia it would not be known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Taftazani, what is one problem with interpreting 'hukm' in the definition of fiqh as 'khitab Allah'?
A) It makes the qualifiers 'shar'iyyah' and ''amaliyyah' redundant.
B) It makes the definition too long.
C) It contradicts the Quran.
D) It is not a valid meaning of hukm.

Key Takeaway
Taftazani shows that defining fiqh with hukm as khitab Allah forces unnecessary logical contortions; the customary meaning is clearer.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
The Definition of Hukm Shar'i and the Refutation of Circularity (Dawr)
Usul dispute: definition of hukm shar'i and refutation of dawr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i includes the word 'ma' and distinguish between the essence of faith (nafs al-iman) and its obligation (wujub al-iman) to resolve the problem of circularity.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition uses 'ma' to avoid implying the eternal divine address is dependent; essence vs obligation breaks the circle.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih tackles a critical usul problem: how to define hukm shar'i without falling into circular reasoning (dawr). The author explains the subtle but crucial inclusion of the word 'ma' in the definition, and then defends the classification of wujub al-iman as a Shar'i ruling against an objection that would otherwise imply infinite regress. By the end of this lesson, you will see how Hanafi usul masters used precise wording and logical distinctions to safeguard the foundations of the discipline.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the definition of hukm shar'i
Identify the exact Arabic definition and note the inclusion of 'ma'. Understand why without 'ma' the definition would imply the divine address itself depends on Shari'ah, which is impossible for the eternal speech of Allah.
The definition is: 'huwa al-khitabu bima yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar''.
2
Understand the initial classification of wujub al-iman
The author initially places wujub al-iman and wujub al-tasdiq as non-Shar'i (ma la yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar') to avoid dawr. The reasoning: if they were Shar'i, they would depend on Shari'ah, but Shari'ah also depends on them (since Shari'ah requires faith in Allah and the Prophet).
This is the objector's reading of the author's intent.
3
Examine the objector's argument against dawr
The objector denies dawr by distinguishing between nafs (essence) and wujub (obligation). The Shari'ah depends on nafs al-iman (the essence of faith), not on wujub al-iman. Thus the direction of dependence differs: Shari'ah depends on essence, obligation depends on Shari'ah. No circle occurs.
The objector argues that the author's proof 'lazima al-dawr' is invalid.
4
Trace the Hanafi response and resolution
The commentator clarifies that Taftazani misunderstood: the original text's example (wujub al-iman) was actually meant as an example of rulings dependent on Shari'ah (ma yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar'). The pronoun references show that Shari'ah depends on the essence (nafs), not the obligation. Therefore, wujub al-iman is indeed Shar'i, and no circularity exists.
The response hinges on careful pronoun resolution: 'tawaqqufi al-shar'i 'alayhi' refers to nafs al-iman.
5
Appreciate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: correctly defining hukm shar'i and understanding the foundation of obligation (whether reason or revelation) affects the entire usul system. This dispute clarifies that wujub al-iman is a Shar'i ruling established by revelation (sam'), while the essence of faith is a precondition for the Shari'ah itself.
This distinction preserves the integrity of the definition and avoids theological pitfalls.

علیہ شرع ہے لہذا دور لازم نہیں آتا دور تب لازم آتا کہ شرع کا موقوف علیہ وجوب ایمان ہوتا اور وجوب ایمان کا موقوف علیہ شرع بنتی حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے تو مصنف کی دلیل لزم الدور باطل ہے۔ جواب ! اس اشکال کا یہ جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ در اصل تفتازانی کو غلط فہمی ہو گئی وہ سمجھ بیٹھا ہے کہ وجوب ایمان وجوب تصدیق ، مالا توقف علی الشرع کی مثال ہیں حالانکہ یہ ما توقف على الشرع کی مثال ہیں البتہ آگے ونحوهما کی هما ضمیر نفس ایمان نفس تصدیق کی طرف راجع ہے اور لــمـا لايتوقف على الشرع نحوهما کا بیان ہے اور لتوقف الشرع علیہ کی ضمیر بھی نفس ایمان کی طرف راجع ہے تو وجوب ایمان وجوب تصدیق شریعت پر موقوف ہیں یہ توقف کی مثال ہیں البتہ نفس ایمان نفس تصدیق شرع پر موقوف نہیں ہے توقف الشرع علیہ ای علی نفس الایمان ( ہذا الجواب لائج ید و ظاہر عبارۃ المصنف ) فيلزم الدور فاندفع اشكال الشارح قوله ثم الشرعى اما نظرى
It becomes established and faith is acquired upon it. In this way, for the establishment of the Shari'ah, the verification of the intermediary is also necessary; that intermediary is the Noble Prophet. If the intermediary is not verified, how will the Shari'ah be established? In any case, from this discussion it will be established that the Shari'ah is dependent on the obligation of faith in Allah and the obligation of verifying the Prophet (which verification is obtained by the evidence of miracles). Now, if the obligation of faith and the obligation of verifying the Prophet then themselves become dependent on the Shari'ah, then circularity (dawr) would be necessary: that the Shari'ah is dependent on them, and they again are dependent on the Shari'ah. This is called dawr. Hence it is established that the obligation of faith and the obligation of verifying the Prophet are not dependent on the Shari'ah, and that is the claim. And this is called a non-Shar'i ruling. So by adding the qualification 'al-Shar'iyyah', this non-Shar'i ruling (obligation of faith and obligation of verifying the Prophet) is excluded. So the author adopted all this effort to make the qualification 'al-Shar'iyyah' beneficial and effective. Also, to make the expression 'al-'amaliyyah' beneficial, he generalized 'af'al' in 'af'al al-mukallafin' and intended both actions of the heart and actions of the limbs, although the term 'fi'l' is used only for actions of the limbs. Also, he committed arbitrariness in this way by saying: 'The obligation of faith is not dependent on the Shari'ah', although according to the Ash'aris, the obligation of faith is dependent on the Shari'ah, because the Ash'aris say: 'No obligation except by revelation (al-sam') i.e., the Shari'ah.' When it is established that the obligation of faith is dependent on the Shari'ah, and the Shari'ah itself is dependent on the obligation of faith, then circularity (dawr) would be necessary. And his statement: 'al-khitab bima yatawaqqaf...' is for the purpose of answering an implied objection. The objection is: The author defined khitab and hukm shar'i as 'huwa khitabun bima tawaqqafa 'ala al-shar'', i.e., khitab with a thing that is dependent on the Shari'ah. Why did he not define it as 'huwa al-khitabu alladhi yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar'' i.e., the khitab itself is dependent on the Shari'ah? Similarly, the definition of non-Shar'i would be 'al-khitabu alladhi la yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar''. The summary of the objection is that in the definition of Shar'i and non-Shar'i, the word 'ma' should not be mentioned. Answer: The commentator Taftazani answers that mentioning the word 'ma' in the definition of Shar'i and non-Shar'i is very necessary, otherwise corruption would arise. Because if the word 'ma' is not present, then the definition of hukm shar'i would be 'al-khitabu alladhi yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar'' i.e., the khitab itself is dependent on the Shari'ah, whereas the khitab of Allah is eternal, and an eternal thing is not dependent on anything, because dependence is an indication of temporality. Hence the word 'ma' was added. Now the definition of hukm shar'i becomes: 'huwa al-khitabu bima yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar'' meaning: the khitab of Allah is with a thing that is dependent on the Shari'ah. In this case, the khitab itself is not dependent on the Shari'ah, but the object of the khitab (the thing with which the khitab is concerned, e.g., prayer, fasting) is dependent on the Shari'ah. So the objection is removed. And there is one who may deny the dependence of the Shari'ah on the obligation of faith and similar things. This is for an objection against the author. The author made two divisions of hukm: Shar'i and non-Shar'i. Then he gave an example of non-Shar'i (in the sense of that which is not dependent on the Shari'ah): the obligation of faith and the obligation of verifying the Prophet, and said that these are not dependent on the Shari'ah. And he gave the proof: if these are dependent on the Shari'ah, then circularity would be necessary because the Shari'ah is dependent on them. The objector says: We do not acknowledge circularity; there is no circularity here. Because here on one side are faith in Allah and verification of the Prophet, and on the other side is the Shari'ah. Then in the side of faith and verification, there are three possibilities: (1) The essence of faith in Allah and the essence of verification of the Prophet, (2) The obligation of faith and the obligation of verification of the Prophet, (3) Knowledge of the obligation of faith and knowledge of the obligation of verification of the Prophet. Now the author said that the obligation of faith and the obligation of verification of the Prophet are not dependent on the Shari'ah, because the Shari'ah itself is dependent on the obligation of faith and the obligation of verification of the Prophet. If the obligation of faith becomes dependent on the Shari'ah, then circularity would be necessary. We say: Your statement that the Shari'ah is dependent on the obligation of faith and the obligation of verification of the Prophet is wrong. Rather, the establishment of the Shari'ah—whether by Shari'ah is meant the speech of Allah or the Shari'ah of the Prophet—is dependent on the essence of faith in Allah and His attributes and on the essence of verifying the prophethood of the Prophet (peace be upon him) through miraculous evidence. And the essence of faith is something else, and the obligation of faith and the obligation of verifying the Prophet is something else. From the Shari'ah being dependent on the essence of faith and the essence of verifying the Prophet, it does not necessarily follow that the Shari'ah is also dependent on the obligation of faith and the obligation of verifying the Prophet or knowledge of the obligation of faith and knowledge of the obligation of verifying the Prophet, because we have explained that these are separate. In summary, the Shari'ah is dependent on the essence of faith in Allah. So the object of dependence of the Shari'ah is the essence of faith and the essence of verification. Then we say that the essence of faith and the essence of verifying the Prophet are not dependent on the Shari'ah, such that circularity would become necessary. Rather, the obligation of faith and the obligation of verifying the Prophet are dependent on the Shari'ah, as is the doctrine of the scholars, that the obligation of faith is not established without a textual (sam'i) and Shar'i proof. Therefore, when the essence of faith and the essence of verification are not dependent on the Shari'ah, circularity will not be necessary, because in circularity, the direction of dependence must be the same. For example, if A is dependent on B, and then B is dependent on A, then circularity would be necessary. If the direction of dependence is different, then circularity is not necessary. (1) If A is dependent on B, and then B is dependent on C, then it is not called circularity. Here also the direction of dependence is different, because the object of dependence of the Shari'ah is the essence of faith, not the obligation of faith, and the object of dependence of the obligation of faith is the Shari'ah. Hence circularity does not arise. Circularity would arise only if the object of dependence of the Shari'ah were the obligation of faith, and the object of dependence of the obligation of faith were the Shari'ah, but this is not the case. So the author's proof 'lazima al-dawr' is invalid. Answer: To this objection, it is answered that actually Taftazani misunderstood; he thought that the obligation of faith and the obligation of verification are examples of that which is not dependent on the Shari'ah, whereas these are examples of that which is dependent on the Shari'ah. However, the pronoun 'huma' in 'wa nahwihima' refers back to the essence of faith and the essence of verification, and the statement 'lima la yatawaqqafu 'ala al-shar'' is an explanation of 'nahwihima', and the pronoun in 'li tawaqqufi al-shar'' 'alayhi' also refers back to the essence of faith. So the obligation of faith and the obligation of verification are dependent on the Shari'ah; these are examples of dependence. However, the essence of faith and the essence of verification are not dependent on the Shari'ah; the dependence of the Shari'ah is upon them, i.e., upon the essence of faith. (This answer is not apparent from the author's words.) So circularity becomes necessary, and the objection of the commentator is repelled. Then his statement: 'thumma al-shar'i imma nazari...'
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute regarding the definition of hukm shar'i (legal ruling) and the problem of dawr (circular reasoning). The author (the commentator of Miskulmaleeh) explains why the definition of hukm shar'i must include the word 'ma' (that which) to avoid implying that the divine address itself is dependent on the Shari'ah, which would be improper since the address of Allah is eternal. The passage then moves to an objection concerning the classification of wujub al-iman (obligation of faith) and wujub al-tasdiq al-nabi (obligation of verifying the Prophet). The author initially presented these as examples of non-Shar'i rulings (that which is not dependent on the Shari'ah) to avoid circularity: if they were dependent on the Shari'ah, then since the Shari'ah is itself dependent on them, an infinite regress or circularity would occur. An objector (possibly a critic within the Hanafi or Ash'ari tradition) denies the circularity by distinguishing between the essence (nafs) of iman and tasdiq and their obligation. The objector argues that the Shari'ah is dependent on the essence of iman and tasdiq, not on their obligation; thus the direction of dependence is different, and no circularity arises. The commentator then responds that Taftazani (the author of al-Talwih) misunderstood: the examples given by the original author (presumably Sadr al-Shari'ah) were actually meant to illustrate rulings that are dependent on the Shari'ah, not independent. The pronoun references clarify that the essence of iman and tasdiq are what the Shari'ah depends on, while the obligation of these is what depends on the Shari'ah. Therefore, the apparent circularity is resolved. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi usul method of precise definition and logical analysis, showing how a small change in wording (adding 'ma') can prevent a major theological and legal problem. It also shows the interplay between different Hanafi scholars (the original matn author, the commentator, and the supercommentator) in refining definitions.

Key Terms
الحكم الشرعي (al-hukm al-shar'i): The divine address (khitab) concerning something that is dependent on the Shari'ah.
دور (dawr): Circular reasoning: A depends on B and B depends on A in the same respect.
موقوف (mawquf): Dependent (upon something else); a state of contingency.
وجوب الإيمان (wujub al-iman): The obligation of faith; a ruling that is established by the Shari'ah.
نفس الإيمان (nafs al-iman): The essence or reality of faith; the inner conviction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi resolution in this passage, why does the definition of hukm shar'i require the word 'ma' (بما)?
A) Without it, the definition would imply that the divine address itself is dependent on the Shari'ah, which is impossible.
B) Without it, the definition would be grammatically incomplete.
C) Without it, the definition would contradict the Ash'ari school.
D) Without it, the definition would be too vague.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of hukm shar'i uses 'ma' to preserve the eternality of divine speech and, through the distinction between essence and obligation, avoids circularity in foundational usul concepts.

The Redundancy Fallacy in Defining Fiqh
Critique of a definitional restriction as redundant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical fallacy of ikhrāj al-mukhrāj in a definition and explain why Taftazani objects to the restriction 'amaliyya' in the definition of fiqh.

Core Idea
A restriction is redundant if it excludes what is already outside the definition.

In this passage, the commentator Taftazani challenges a common division of shar'i rulings. The author had split shar'i into theoretical (nazari) and practical (amali), and then in defining fiqh restricted it to practical rulings. Taftazani points out a subtle but serious logical flaw: if the technical term 'hukm' already excludes theoretical rulings, then adding 'amaliyya' is unnecessary. This lesson walks through the objection and its implications for the precision of usul definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divided term and its divisions
The term 'shar'i' is defined as 'that which depends on sharia'. It is divided into nazari (theoretical) and amali (practical). The commentator clarifies this before raising his objection.
2
Understand the purpose of the restriction 'amaliyya'
In the definition of fiqh, the author used 'amaliyya' to exclude nazari rulings. But this only makes sense if nazari rulings are a subset of the term being defined.
3
Recall the definition of 'hukm istilahi'
Hukm istilahi is defined as 'khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin' (the address of Allah related to the actions of the mukallafin). This definition by its terms excludes anything not related to actions.
Af'al means actions; nazari rulings like 'ijma is a proof' are not actions.
4
Analyze the objection: ikhrāj al-mukhrāj
Since nazari rulings are already excluded by the very definition of hukm (they are not about actions), adding 'amaliyya' to exclude them is redundant—it excludes what is already out of scope. This is the fallacy of ikhrāj al-mukhrāj.
The objection targets the author's definition of fiqh, not the division itself.
5
Conclude the force of the critique
The restriction is invalid because it serves no purpose; a sound definition should not contain redundant conditions. This shows the importance of precise terminology in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text

That is, that which depends on the sharia. The purpose of the commentator Taftazani is to explain the text. The author (matn) had mentioned two divisions of shar'i. While explaining them, the commentator says: Here the divided term 'shar'i' means 'dependent on sharia'. It has two divisions: one is (1) nazari (theoretical), i.e., that which is not related to the quality of action, and the second is (2) amali (practical) shar'i ruling, which is related to the quality of action. So by the restriction 'al-amaliyya', it is intended to exclude shar'i nazari. An example of a nazari ruling is 'ijma is a proof'. And this is only correct... The commentator Taftazani's purpose is to object to the author. The objection is: The exclusion of nazari rulings by the restriction 'al-amaliyya' can be valid only if they (nazari rulings) are included in the technical term 'hukm' (meaning the address of Allah). However, there is a problem regarding the inclusion of nazari rulings in the technical hukm, which will soon appear. That problem is: Hukm in the sense of khitab Allah does not include nazari rulings because the phrase 'al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin' is a restriction. By 'af'al', actions are meant. So the technical hukm only includes practical rulings. Nazari rulings are excluded from the actions of the mukallaf. Therefore, the exclusion of nazari rulings by the restriction 'al-amaliyya' would be of the type 'ikhrāj al-mukhrāj' (excluding what is already excluded), which is invalid. Then his statement: 'min adillatiha'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is about the definition and division of shar'i rulings. The matn (original text) divided shar'i into nazari (theoretical) and amali (practical). The commentator (Taftazani) explains that 'shar'i' here means something that depends on sharia. He gives an example of a nazari ruling: 'ijma is a proof'. Then he raises an objection: the restriction 'amali' in the definition of fiqh (which says 'ahkam shar'iyya amaliyya') is used to exclude nazari rulings, but if nazari rulings are not even included in the term 'hukm' (which is defined as khitab Allah al-muta'alliq bi af'al al-mukallafin), then excluding them is redundant (ikhrāj al-mukhrāj). This is a critique of the author's definition. The passage demonstrates the precision required in Hanafi usul definitions.

Key Terms
شرعي نظري (shar'i nazari): A ruling that is derived from sharia but not directly related to the quality of an action, e.g., 'ijma is a proof'
حكم اصطلاحي (hukm istilahi): The technical term for hukm: the address of Allah related to the actions of the mukallafin
إخراج المخرج (ikhrāj al-mukhrāj): A logical fallacy of excluding what is already excluded, i.e., a redundant restriction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Taftazani consider the restriction 'amaliyya' problematic in the definition of fiqh?
A) Because nazari rulings are not derived from sharia
B) Because nazari rulings are already excluded by the definition of hukm as related to actions
C) Because nazari rulings are more important than amali
D) Because the author did not mention nazari rulings

Key Takeaway
A definition that adds a restriction to exclude what is already outside its scope commits the fallacy of ikhrāj al-mukhrāj and must be refined.

Dividing Hukm Shar'i: Nazari vs Amali and the Critical Refinement
Refinement of the definition of hukm sharʿi by Taftazani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define hukm sharʿi according to the Hanafi usul, distinguish between nazari and amali rulings, and identify the logical flaw in excluding nazari rulings by the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya'.

Core Idea
Theoretical rulings are not part of hukm sharʿi terminologically; excluding them is redundant.

In this passage, the commentator al-Taftazani refines the author’s division of hukm sharʿi. He explains that the term 'sharʿi' here means 'that which depends on revelation,' and it divides into theoretical (nazari) and practical (amali). However, he points out that the author’s use of the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' to exclude theoretical rulings is logically flawed because theoretical rulings are already not included in the terminological definition of hukm (as khitab Allah). Understanding this critical nuance sharpens your grasp of foundational usul concepts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two divisions
Hukm sharʿi (in the broader sense) is divided into nazari (theoretical) and amali (practical). A theoretical ruling is not related to action, e.g., the authority of ijmaʿ. A practical ruling relates to action.
The broader definition is 'that which depends on revelation.'
2
Understand the commentator’s objection
Taftazani objects that the author’s restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' is meant to exclude nazari rulings, but this is only valid if nazari rulings were included in the terminological definition of hukm (khitab Allah). They are not, because khitab Allah is restricted to speech related to actions of the mukallaf.
Khitab Allah: the address of Allah.
3
Trace the reasoning
The author’s definition of hukm sharʿi as 'that which depends on revelation' includes nazari rulings. But the terminological definition (hukm as khitab Allah) does not. So when the author says 'al-hukm al-sharʿi al-ʿamali' to define fiqh, the exclusion of nazari is redundant because they were never in that category.
Redundancy is called 'ikhraj al-kharij' in Arabic.
4
Apply the insight
In Hanafi usul, theoretical rulings like 'ijmaʿ is a proof' are not considered hukm in the strict sense but are foundational principles. Practical rulings are the direct subject of fiqh.
This distinction prevents confusion in later derivations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih: i.e., that which depends on revelation. The commentator Taftazani explains the text: The author had mentioned two divisions of shar'i, and now the commentator explains that here 'shar'i' is meant as 'that which depends on revelation.' It has two divisions: (1) theoretical, which is not related to the quality of action, and (2) practical shar'i ruling, which is related to the quality of action. So by the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya,' it is intended to exclude the theoretical shar'i. An example of a theoretical ruling is 'ijmaʿ is a proof.' And this is only valid— the commentator Taftazani's purpose is to object to the author, saying that the exclusion of theoretical rulings by the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' is only correct if those rulings are included in the terminological ruling (meaning the speech of Allah). However, the inclusion of theoretical rulings in the terminological ruling is problematic, which will come soon. The problem is that the ruling meaning the speech of Allah does not include theoretical rulings because of the restriction 'al-mutaʿalliq bi afʿal al-mukallafin'—actions mean deeds. So the terminological ruling only includes practical rulings; theoretical rulings are excluded from the actions of the mukallaf. Therefore, excluding theoretical rulings by the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' would be like removing something that is already out, which is invalid.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a definition and analysis of the types of hukm sharʿi. The commentator explains that the term 'sharʿi' here means that which depends on revelation (al-sharʿ). It is divided into two: theoretical (nazari) and practical (ʿamali). Theoretical rulings are those that are not related to the quality of action, e.g., the ruling that ijmaʿ is a proof. Practical rulings are those related to action. The author's definition uses the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' (practical) to exclude theoretical rulings from the definition of fiqh. However, the commentator points out an objection: this exclusion is only valid if theoretical rulings are actually included in the terminological definition of 'hukm' (as khitab Allah). But the standard definition of hukm as khitab Allah requires it to be related to the actions of the mukallaf. Theoretical rulings are not related to actions, so they are not included in the term 'hukm' to begin with. Therefore, excluding them by the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' is redundant—it is like excluding something that was never there. This is a critical refinement of the matn, highlighting a logical flaw in the author's formulation.

Key Terms
الحکم الشرعی (al-hukm al-sharʿi): That which depends on the revelation (al-sharʿ).
نظری (nazari): A ruling not related to the quality of action, e.g., the authority of ijmaʿ.
عملی (ʿamali): A ruling related to the quality of action of the mukallaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say that excluding nazari rulings by the restriction 'al-ʿamaliyya' is like excluding something already out?
A) Because nazari rulings are not derived from revelation.
B) Because nazari rulings are not included in the terminological definition of hukm (khitab Allah) which is restricted to actions of the mukallaf.
C) Because nazari rulings are not needed in fiqh.
D) Because the author mistakenly thought nazari rulings are practical.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between theoretical and practical rulings is crucial; the term 'hukm sharʿi' terminologically only covers practical rulings, and excluding theoretical ones is redundant.

Redundancy of 'bil-istidlal' in the Definition of Fiqh
Debate on whether the qualifier 'by inference' is redundant after 'knowledge from detailed proofs'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether the qualifier 'bil-istidlal' is necessary in the Hanafi definition of fiqh and explain the Hanafi position on its redundancy.

Core Idea
The Hanafi definition of fiqh already implies inference; 'bil-istidlal' is redundant.

This lesson examines a key debate in usul al-fiqh: whether the qualifier 'by inference' (bil-istidlal) is required in the definition of fiqh. The Hanafi position, championed by Sadr al-Shariah, holds that it is redundant because the phrase 'knowledge of the rulings from their detailed proofs' inherently entails inferential reasoning. We will walk through the arguments of Taftazani and see why the Hanafis consider his responses weak. Understanding this controversy sharpens your grasp of fiqh terminology and the boundaries between acquired and intuitive knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge from proofs
Differentiate between knowledge obtained intuitively (badahah) and knowledge obtained through inference (istidlal). Only the latter is called fiqh.
Intuitive knowledge includes that of prophets and angels; it is not derived through contemplation.
2
State the purpose of 'bil-istidlal' according to Ibn al-Hajib
Ibn al-Hajib added the qualifier to exclude the intuitive knowledge of prophets and angels from the definition of fiqh.
The author initially thought it was to exclude the muqallid's knowledge, but the text clarifies it was for prophetic knowledge.
3
Analyze the Hanafi claim of redundancy
The phrase 'from detailed proofs' already implies that the knowledge is acquired through inference, because 'from proofs' means deriving the ruling by looking into the proof, as Taftazani himself admitted.
Therefore, 'bil-istidlal' is repetitive and adds no new exclusion.
4
Evaluate Taftazani's four responses
Taftazani gives four justifications for the qualifier, but the Hanafis reject them as weak and contradictory to his own admission that 'the meaning of acquiring knowledge from the proof is that he looks into the proof'.
The correct position is that the qualifier is redundant, as stated by Sadr al-Shariah.

و علم رسول کو خارج کرنا چاہتے ہیں کیونکہ علم جبرائیل و علم رسول کو فقہ نہیں کہا جاتا وجہ یہ ہے احکام کا علم دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا ادلہ سے ہوگا یا نہ اگر نہیں ہے تو وہ علم علم اللہ ہے لہذا من ادلتها التفصیلیہ سے علم واجب تعالی خارج ہو گیا اگر احکام کا علم من الادلہ ہو تو پھر وہ دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا وہ حصول علم من الدليل بالضرورة والبداہتہ ہوگا یعنی دلیل میں غور و فکر سوچ و بچار کی ضرورت نہیں ہوگی بلکہ دلیل کو دیکھتے ہی بلا تد بر حکم معلوم ہوگا یا وہ علم بالاستدلال و بالاستنباط والاجتهاد تدبر و فکر سوچ و بچار فی الدلیل اور مقدمات کو ترتیب دینے سے حاصل ہو گا اگر احکام کا علم دلیل سے تو حاصل ہو لیکن بالبداہۃ والضرورۃ ہو تو اصطلاح میں اس کو بھی فقہ نہیں کہا جاتا جیسے علم جبرائیل علم الرسول اور اگر حصول علم من الدلیل بطریق لاستدلال والاستنباط ہو تو اس کو اصطلاح میں فقہ کہا جاتا ہے جیسے مجتہد کا علم تو علامہ ابن الحاجب نے فقہ کی تعریف میں بالاستدلال کی قید لگا کر علم جبرائیل و علم رسول کو خارج کیا ہے کیونکہ اس کو فقہ نہیں کہا جا ۔ لیکن مصنف کو وہم ہوا کہ بالاستدلال کی قید سے علم مقلد کو خارج کرنا مقصود ہے اس لیے انہوں نے اشکال کر دیا کہ یہ تکرار ہے۔ جواب ! حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے بالکل درست فرمایا ہے قید بالاستدلال ہر صورت میں مکر رہتی ہے مصنف کو کوئی غلط نہیں اور تو ہم نہیں ہوا بلکہ آپ ہی مبتلائے تو ہم ہوئے ہیں آپ کا قول والمصنف تو ھم اند احتراز عن علم المقلد خود مینی علی التوہم ہے کیونکہ مصنف نے تو صرف اتنا کہا ہے کہ قید بالاستدلال مکر رہے وجہ تکرار انہوں نے بیان نہیں کی یہ تو آپ نے بیان کی جو کہ مبنی بر تو ہم ہے مصنف کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ قید بالاستدلال ہر حال میں مکرر ہے خواہ یہ علم مقلد سے احتراز ہو یا علم جبرائیل وعلم الرسول سے کیونکہ جب من اول تھا کا تعلق علم سے ہے تو اسی سے ثابت ہو رہا ہے کہ فقہ ایسے علم کا نام ہے جو ادلہ سے حاصل ہو اور حصول علم من ادلہ کا معنی خود شارح تفتازانی نے ہی بیان کیا ہے انہ نظر فی الدلیل فیعلم منہ الحکم اس سے صاف واضح ہو رہا ہے کہ فقہ علم استدلالی کا نام ہے اور علم حاصل من الدلیل وہی ہوتا ہے جو دلیل میں نظر وفکر غور و فکر کرنے کے بعد حاصل ہو لہذا علم مقلہ علم جبرائیل علم رسول سب من اولتها التفصیلیہ سے خارج ہو رہے ہیں لہذا اس کے بعد با الاستدلال کی قید ہر حال میں تکرار محض ہے ( بعض حضرات نے یہ جواب دیا ہے کہ مقصود مصنف ولا شک انہ مکرر سے یہ ہے کہ یہ قید کوئی ضروری نہیں کیونکہ مقصد اس کے بغیر بھی حاصل ہو جاتا ہے)۔ فان قیل سے شارح اشکال و جواب ذکر کر رہے ہیں اشکال یہ ہے کہ بالاستدلال کی قید ہر حال میں مکرر ہے کیونکہ حصول علم من الادلہ ( وہ علم جو ادلہ سے حاصل ہو ) خود استدلال کی طرف مشعر ہے یعنی علم کے ادلہ سے حاصل ہونے کا مقصد ہی یہی ہے کہ وہ استدلال سے حاصل ہو لہذا بالاستدلال کی قید مکرر ہوئی کیونکہ علم جبرائیل علم رسول من الادلہ سے ہی خارج ہو گئے اور یہی بات تو مصنف نے متن کے اندر فرمائی تھی تو قول مصنف حق و صحیح ثابت ہوا۔ قلنا لو سلم شارح تفتازانی اس اشکال کے چار جواب دے رہے ہیں (۱) ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے حصول علم من الادلہ مشعر الی الاستدلال ہے کیونکہ حصول علم من ادلہ بھی بطریق الاستدلال ہوتا ہے اور کبھی بطريق البداہۃ والحدس ہوتا ہے اب جو علم بداہت وحدس سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اسے یوں تو کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ علم حاصل من الدلیل ہے یوں نہیں کہا جاتا کہ یہ حاصل من الاستدلال ہے لیکن شارح کا یہ عدم تسلیم منی علی العلم والعصف ہے کیونکہ چند سطور قبل شارح خود اعتراف کر چکے ہیں کہ حصول علم من ادلہ کا مقصد صرف اور صرف یہی ہے کہ دلیل میں نظر و فکر کر کے اس سے حکم کو اخذ کیا جائے عبارت ملاحظہ فرمائیے و معنى حصول العلم من الدليل انه ينظر في الدليل فيعلم منه الحكم ۔ سا کے بعد شارح کے عدم تسلیم کو ہٹ دھرمی اور تنگ نظری کے علاوہ اور کیا کہا جا سکتا ہے (۲) جواب دوم فذكر الاستدلال لتصريح بما علم ضمنا والتزاما سے دیا ہے اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو بھی بالاستدلال کی قید تکرار نہیں بلکہ تصريح بما علم ضمنا والتزاما ہے (۳) اولدفع الوہم ہے تیسر ا جواب ہے کہ یہ قید دفع وہم کیلئے ہے کوئی شخص کہہ سکتا تھا کہ علم جبرائیل علم رسول فقہ میں داخل ہیں اس وہم کو دفع کرنے کیلئے بالاستدلال کی قید لگادی (۴) اوللبیان جواب رابع یہ ہے کہ یہ قید ترازی نہیں بلکہ قید واقعی ہے تعریف کی وضاحت و بیان کیلئے ہے اور ایسا شائع ذائع فی التعریفات ہے کہ بعض قیودات صرف : مساحت و تاکید کیلئے آتی ہیں وہ قیودات مخرجہ احتراز یہ نہیں ہوتیں۔ ناظرین کرام غور فرمائیے شارح کے یہ تمام جوابات ضعیفہ اور تاویلات رکیکہ اور اعذار باردہ ساقطہ ہیں حق بات وہی ہے جو علامہ صدر نے کی ہے ( ولا شک انہ مکرر ) والحق احق ان يتبع
Misk al-Malih: Commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. They intend to exclude the knowledge of the Messenger because the knowledge of Gabriel and the Messenger is not called fiqh. The reason is that knowledge of rulings is not free from two states: either from the proofs or not. If not, then that knowledge is the knowledge of Allah. So by 'from its detailed proofs', the knowledge of Allah is excluded. If knowledge of rulings is from the proofs, then it is not free from two states: either acquiring knowledge from the proof by necessity and intuition—meaning no need for contemplation in the proof, rather upon seeing the proof the ruling is known without deliberation—or that knowledge is through inference, deduction, and ijtihad, by pondering and arranging premises. If knowledge of rulings is acquired from a proof but by way of intuition and necessity, then in terminology it is also not called fiqh, like the knowledge of Gabriel and the knowledge of the Messenger. And if the acquisition of knowledge from the proof is through inference and deduction, then in terminology it is called fiqh, like the knowledge of a mujtahid. So Ibn al-Hajib, in his definition of fiqh, placed the qualifier 'by inference' to exclude the knowledge of Gabriel and the Messenger because it is not called fiqh. But the author mistakenly thought that the qualifier 'by inference' was intended to exclude the knowledge of the muqallid, so he objected that it is redundant. Answer: The summary answer is that the author is absolutely correct; the qualifier 'by inference' is in every case redundant. The author is not mistaken; rather you are the one afflicted with misunderstanding. Your statement 'and the author is confused about whether it excludes the knowledge of the muqallid' is itself based on misunderstanding because the author only said that the qualifier 'by inference' is redundant, and he did not state the reason for redundancy. It is you who stated that, which is based on misunderstanding. The author's intent is that the qualifier 'by inference' is redundant in any case, whether it excludes the knowledge of the muqallid or the knowledge of Gabriel and the Messenger, because when 'from its' is related to knowledge, it proves that fiqh is the name of knowledge acquired from proofs, and the meaning of acquisition of knowledge from proofs is itself expressed by Sharh al-Taftazani: 'he looks into the proof and from it knows the ruling.' From this it is clear that fiqh is the name of inferential knowledge, and knowledge acquired from a proof is only that which is obtained after looking and pondering in the proof. Therefore, the knowledge of the muqallid, Gabriel, and the Messenger are all excluded by 'from its detailed proofs'. Hence, after that, the qualifier 'by inference' is pure redundancy. (Some people have responded that the author's purpose with 'and there is no doubt that it is redundant' is that this qualifier is not necessary because the purpose is achieved without it.) 'If it is said' — from here the commentator (sharh) mentions objection and answer. The objection is: the qualifier 'by inference' is in every case redundant because the acquisition of knowledge from the proofs (knowledge acquired from proofs) itself indicates inference, meaning the purpose of knowledge being from proofs is that it is acquired by inference. Therefore, the qualifier 'by inference' is redundant because the knowledge of Gabriel and the Messenger are already excluded by 'from the proofs', and this is exactly what the author said in the matn. So the author's statement is proven true. We say: even if that is granted, Sharh al-Taftazani gives four responses to this objection: (1) We do not accept that the acquisition of knowledge from proofs indicates inference, because knowledge from proofs sometimes occurs through inference and sometimes through intuition and guessing. Knowledge that comes through intuition and guessing is called 'knowledge acquired from the proof' but not 'knowledge acquired from inference'. But this denial by the commentator is based on ignorance and obstinacy because a few lines earlier the commentator himself admitted that the meaning of acquiring knowledge from proofs is only that one looks into the proof and derives the ruling from it. Consider the phrase: 'the meaning of acquiring knowledge from the proof is that he looks into the proof and from it knows the ruling.' After that, what else can be said about the commentator's denial except that it is stubbornness and narrow-mindedness? (2) The second response: 'mentioning inference is to clarify what was known implicitly and concomitantly.' If we accept that, the qualifier 'by inference' is not redundant but rather clarification of what was known implicitly. (3) The third response: it is to repel a misunderstanding. Someone might have thought that the knowledge of Gabriel and the Messenger are included in fiqh, so the qualifier 'by inference' is added to repel this misunderstanding. (4) The fourth response: it is for clarification. The qualifier is not only for excluding but is a real qualifier for explaining the definition. And it is widespread in definitions that some qualifiers come only for clarification and emphasis, not for exclusion. Respected readers, consider carefully that all these responses of the commentator are weak, odious interpretations, and cold, falling excuses. The correct statement is what 'Allāmah Ṣadr has said: 'and there is no doubt that it is redundant.' And the truth is more deserving to be followed.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiyah) addressing the definition of fiqh and the necessity of the qualifier 'bil-istidlal' (by inference). The author (Misk al-Malih) supports Sadr al-Shariah's view that this qualifier is redundant because the phrase 'knowledge from detailed proofs' already implies inference. He refutes the objections of Sharh al-Taftazani, who gives four responses arguing that the qualifier is needed. The author systematically dismantles each response, accusing Taftazani of inconsistency. The correct Hanafi position is that fiqh is defined as knowledge of legal rulings derived from detailed proofs through inference, and specifying 'inference' is unnecessary because derivation inherently involves it. This passage highlights the precision of Hanafi usul terminology.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of legal rulings derived from detailed proofs through inference (ijtihad).
استدلال (istidlal): Inferential reasoning from evidence to a ruling; the process of deriving a ruling through intellectual effort.
بداہت (badahah): Intuitive, immediate knowledge obtained without deliberate inference, such as prophetic knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the qualifier 'bil-istidlal' redundant in the definition of fiqh?
A) Because it excludes the muqallid's knowledge.
B) Because the phrase 'knowledge from detailed proofs' already implies inference.
C) Because Ibn al-Hajib made a mistake.
D) Because Taftazani admitted it is redundant.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position establishes that fiqh by definition is inferential; no additional qualifier is needed.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
Defining Hukm: The Divine Speech as Source of Rulings
Beginning the definition of hukm with genus and differentia

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hukm as given in this passage, identify its genus and differentia, and apply the qualifiers to distinguish included vs excluded divine speech.

Core Idea
Hukm is Allah's speech that addresses the responsible person's actions with a requirement or option.

This passage inaugurates the definition of hukm in the commentary on al-Tawdih. After defining fiqh as knowledge of legal rulings, the commentator explains that hukm must be defined. He presents a definition attributed to Imam Abul Hasan al-Ash'ari: 'the speech of Allah related to the actions of the responsible (mukallafin) with requirement or option.' By analyzing the qualifiers, we will understand exactly what constitutes a legal ruling in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition stated in the text
Locate the exact Arabic phrase defining hukm and its English equivalent.
The definition is given after the matn: 'خطاب اللہ تعالی المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخيير'.
2
Separate genus (jins) and differentia (fasl)
Distinguish the broader category (genus) from the specific qualifier (differentia).
Genus: 'the speech of Allah'. Differentia: 'related to actions of the responsible with requirement or option'.
3
Apply the differentia to exclude irrelevant divine speech
Use the differentia to identify which divine addresses are not considered hukm.
Excluded: stories, parables, verses about divine attributes. Included: commands, prohibitions, permissions regarding actions.
4
Note the source of the definition
Observe that the commentator attributes this definition to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
This shows the Hanafi school's engagement with Ash'ari usul.
5
Connect to the Hanafi position
Understand that Hanafis accept this definition but emphasize that hukm is the address itself, not an attribute.
The madhhab note in key terms elaborates this nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن توضیح
ولما عرف الفقه بالعلم بالاحكام الشرعية وجب تعريف الحكم وتعريف الشرعية فقال والحكم قيل خطاب اللہ تعالی مصنف اپنی عبارت تنقیح کو ماقبل سے ربط دے رہے ہیں کہ جب ہم نے متن تنقیح میں فقہ کی تعریف ھوا العلم بالاحکام الشرعیہ سے کی تو ہمارے اوپر واجب ہے کہ حکم کی تعریف کریں اور الشرعیہ کی بھی تعریف بیان کریں اس لیے ہم حکم کی تعریف کرتے ہیں بعض حضرات نے حکم کی تعریف کی ہے خطاب الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التخيير مصنف نے وضاحت فرمائی کہ یہ تعریف امام ابوالحسن اشعری سے منقول ہے فقولہ خطاب اللہ سے فوائد قیود بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ تعریف حکم میں خطاب اللہ درجہ جنس ہے جمیع خطابات اللہ کو بلا تقیید تخصیص شامل ہے اور المتعلق با فعال المکلفین فصل اول ہے اس سے وہ خطابات اللہ خارج ہو گئے جو افعال واعمال مکلفین کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں جیسے قص و امثال وہ آیات جو صفات اللہ کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں جیسے لا اله الا اللہ وغیرہ البتہ والله خلقكم وما تعملون جیسا خطاب افعال المتکلفین میں داخل ہو کر حکم کی تعریف میں باقی ہے آیت کا معنی یہ ہے کہ
Text of al-Tawdih: 'And when fiqh was defined as knowledge of legal rulings, it became necessary to define hukm and to define shar'iyyah. So he said: hukm, it is said, is the speech of Allah Almighty.' The author (of the commentary) connects his expression of al-Tanqih to what preceded: when we defined fiqh in the text of al-Tanqih as 'knowledge of legal rulings', it became incumbent upon us to define hukm and also to define shar'iyyah. Therefore, we define hukm. Some people have defined hukm as the speech of Allah Almighty related to the actions of the responsible (mukallafin), with requirement (iqtida') or option (takhyir). The author explained that this definition is transmitted from Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. His saying 'the speech of Allah' — he is explaining the benefits of the qualifiers: in the definition of hukm, 'the speech of Allah' is a genus, including all divine speech without restriction. And 'related to the actions of the responsible' is the first differentia; by it, those speeches of Allah that are not connected to the actions and deeds of the responsible are excluded, such as stories and parables, and verses related to divine attributes like 'La ilaha illa Allah', etc. However, a speech like 'And Allah created you and what you do' is included among the actions of the responsible and remains in the definition of hukm. The meaning of the verse is that...
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe (sharh) on the matn of al-Tawdih, beginning the definition of hukm (legal ruling). The author connects it to the previous definition of fiqh. The definition given is: 'the speech of Allah related to the actions of the responsible (mukallafin) with requirement or option.' This definition is attributed to Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. The commentator then dissects the qualifiers: 'the speech of Allah' is the genus, and 'related to the actions of the responsible' is the differentia, which excludes divine speech not concerning human actions (e.g., stories, attributes). An example of included speech is the verse 'Allah created you and what you do.' The passage is incomplete but sets up the standard Hanafi definition of hukm.

Key Terms
حكم (hukm): The speech of Allah related to the actions of the responsible, with requirement or option.
خطاب اللہ (khitab Allah): Divine speech (kalam) that is eternal and self-subsisting in God; the source of legal rulings.
شرعیہ (shar'iyyah): Pertaining to revealed law (Shari'ah), indicating the source of the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition given in this passage, what does 'hukm' (legal ruling) refer to?
A) The action of the mukallaf itself.
B) The speech of Allah related to the actions of the responsible, involving requirement or option.
C) A rational judgment independent of revelation.
D) The consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The definition of hukm as Allah's speech concerning actions with requirement or option is the foundation for identifying legal rulings in the Quran and Sunnah.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Critique of the Sharih: Is Istidlal Necessary for Fiqh?
Refuting the sharih's rejection that fiqh requires istidlal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school insists that fiqh requires istidlal and evaluate the sharih's flawed arguments against it.

Core Idea
Fiqh demands active reasoning (istidlal); intuitive knowledge (badahah) does not qualify.

In defining fiqh as 'knowledge of rulings from detailed evidences,' a sharih (commentator) argued that knowledge obtained through intuition (badahah) or conjecture (hads) comes from the dalil but not from istidlal, making the restriction 'bi al-istidlal' redundant and problematic. The author of Misk al-Malih refutes this by citing the sharih's own earlier statement that obtaining knowledge from the dalil requires looking into it and deducing the ruling—which is precisely istidlal. This lesson dissects the critique and clarifies the Hanafi stance on the essential role of istidlal in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested point
Read the passage and determine what exactly the sharih rejected and why. He claimed that knowledge from badahah/hads, though derived from a dalil, does not involve istidlal, so the definition including 'bi al-istidlal' would exclude such knowledge.
The sharih's refusal is about the definition being too narrow.
2
State the author's critique
The author points out that the sharih himself earlier said: 'The meaning of obtaining knowledge from the dalil is that one looks into the dalil and knows the ruling from it.' This looking into (nazar) is istidlal. So the sharih contradicts himself.
The author uses the sharih's own words against him.
3
Examine the sharih's four justifications
The author presents four answers the sharih might give to defend his position: (1) mentioning istidlal makes explicit what is implicit, (2) it repels the misconception that angelic/prophetic knowledge is fiqh, (3) it is a real explanatory restriction, (4) etc. The author dismisses all as weak.
These justifications are attempts to show the restriction is not repetitive.
4
Understand the author's conclusion
The author quotes 'Allamah Sadr al-Shari'ah who states: 'There is no doubt that it is repetitive.' The author agrees, indicating that the restriction is indeed repetitive but not harmful. The sharih's error was in thinking it excluded knowledge, when it merely reiterates what 'min al-dalil' already implies.
The truth is that the restriction is repetitive, so the sharih's complaint is baseless.
5
Apply the lesson to usul methodology
This dispute illustrates how definitions in usul must be precise and consistent. Recognizing when a restriction is repetitive (mukarrir) versus exclusive (mukhtass) is a key skill. The Hanafi position holds that istidlal is integral to fiqh; the definition should reflect that, even if it means repetition.
Repetition for emphasis or clarity is acceptable in technical definitions.
