بطريق البداہۃ والحدس ہوتا ہے اب جو علم بداہت وحدس سے حاصل ہوتا ہے اسے یوں تو کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ علم حاصل من الدلیل ہے یوں نہیں کہا جاتا کہ یہ حاصل من الاستدلال ہے لیکن شارح کا یہ عدم تسلیم منی علی العلم والعصف ہے کیونکہ چند سطور قبل شارح خود اعتراف کر چکے ہیں کہ حصول علم من ادلہ کا مقصد صرف اور صرف یہی ہے کہ دلیل میں نظر و فکر کر کے اس سے حکم کو اخذ کیا جائے عبارت ملاحظہ فرمائیے و معنى حصول العلم من الدليل انه ينظر في الدليل فيعلم منه الحكم ۔ سا کے بعد شارح کے عدم تسلیم کو ہٹ دھرمی اور تنگ نظری کے علاوہ اور کیا کہا جا سکتا ہے (۲) جواب دوم فذكر الاستدلال لتصريح بما علم ضمنا والتزاما سے دیا ہے اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو بھی بالاستدلال کی قید تکرار نہیں بلکہ تصريح بـمـا عـلـم ضمنا والتزاما ہے (۳) اولدفع الوہم ہے تیسر ا جواب ہے کہ یہ قید دفع وہم کیلئے ہے کوئی شخص کہہ سکتا تھا کہ علم جبرائیل علم رسول فقہ میں داخل ہیں اس وہم کو دفع کرنے کیلئے بالاستدلال کی قید لگادی (۴) اوللبیان جواب رابع یہ ہے کہ یہ قید ترازی نہیں بلکہ قید واقعی ہے تعریف کی وضاحت و بیان کیلئے ہے اور ایسا شائع ذائع فی التعریفات ہے کہ بعض قیودات صرف : مساحت و تاکید کیلئے آتی ہیں وہ قیودات مخرجہ احتراز یہ نہیں ہوتیں۔ ناظرین کرام غور فرمائیے شارح کے یہ تمام جوابات ضعیفہ اور تاویلات رکیکہ اور اعذار باردہ ساقطہ ہیں حق بات وہی ہے جو علامہ صدر نے کی ہے ( ولا شک انہ مکرر ) والحق احق ان يتبع
Misk al-Malih. ... Explanation of al-Tawdih. By way of badahah and hads, knowledge is obtained. Now, knowledge obtained from badahah and hads is said to be knowledge obtained from the dalil, but it is not said to be obtained from istidlal. However, the sharih's refusal to accept this is stubbornness and narrow-mindedness, because a few lines earlier, the sharih himself admitted that the purpose of obtaining knowledge from evidence is only to look into the evidence and deduce the ruling from it. Observe the expression: 'The meaning of obtaining knowledge from the dalil is that one looks into the dalil and knows the ruling from it.' After this, what else can be said except that the sharih's refusal is stubbornness and narrow-mindedness? (2) Second answer: He provided 'the mention of istidlal to make explicit what was known implicitly and by commitment.' Even if accepted, the restriction of istidlal is not repetition, but rather an explicit statement of what was known implicitly and by commitment. (3) First, to repel the misconception. The third answer is that this restriction is to repel the misconception that one might say that the knowledge of Jibril and the knowledge of the Messenger are included in fiqh. To repel this misconception, the restriction of istidlal was added. (4) First, for clarification. The fourth answer is that this restriction is not superfluous, but rather a real restriction for the clarification and explanation of the definition. And it is common in definitions that some restrictions come only for elaboration and emphasis; those restrictions are not exclusive (exclusionary). Dear readers, ponder: all these answers of the sharih are weak, his interpretations are flimsy, and his excuses are cold and invalid. The truth is what 'Allamah Sadr stated: 'There is no doubt that it is repetitive.' And the truth is more deserving to be followed.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a sharp critique of the sharih (commentator) by the author of Misk al-Malih regarding a point in the definition of fiqh. The issue is whether the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of the rulings from their detailed evidences' necessarily implies that the knowledge is obtained through istidlal (deductive inference) or can it be obtained through badahah (immediate intuition) or hads (conjecture). The sharih apparently claimed that knowledge obtained from badahah and hads is knowledge from the dalil but not from istidlal, making the condition of istidlal in the definition superfluous. The author counters that the sharih's own earlier statement—'the meaning of obtaining knowledge from the dalil is that one looks into the dalil and knows the ruling from it'—contradicts his later position. The author then examines four potential justifications the sharih might offer for why the restriction of istidlal is not repetitive: (1) to make explicit what is implicit, (2) to repel the misconception that angelic or prophetic knowledge would otherwise be included, (3) to serve as a real explanatory restriction rather than superfluous, and (4) other weak excuses. The author dismisses all these as weak and insists that the correct position is that of 'Allamah Sadr (Sadr al-Shari'ah) who held that the restriction is indeed repetitive. This dispute reflects the Hanafi usul principle that the definition must precisely delineate the subject matter.

Key Terms
بداہۃ (badahah): Immediate, intuitive knowledge without deliberation.
حدس (hads): Conjecture or estimation based on limited evidence.
استدلال (istidlal): Deductive reasoning from evidence to derive a ruling.
دلیل (dalil): Evidence or proof from which a ruling is derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the main reason the author considers the sharih's refusal to accept the definition with 'bi al-istidlal' to be stubborn?
A) Because the sharih denied that badahah exists.
B) Because the sharih's own earlier statement implies that istidlal is necessary.
C) Because the sharih is known to be ignorant of usul.
D) Because the author prefers Sadr al-Shari'ah's view.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh requires active reasoning (istidlal); mere intuitive knowledge from evidence does not qualify; the sharih's critique is based on a self-contradiction.
